201 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Casino Free Phila. v. Pa. Gaming Control Bd.


No. 153 EM 2006


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


594 Pa. 202; 934 A.2d 1249; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2429


June 26, 2007, Submitted 
November 21, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for Review in the Nature of a Complaint Seeking Declaratory Judgment and Injunctive Relief Pursuant to 4 Pa.C.S. § 1904.
Pa. Gaming Control Bd. v. City Council, 593 Pa. 241, 928 A.2d 1255, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1583 (Pa., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner civic organizations and others filed an application for leave to file a petition in the nature of a complaint seeking declaratory judgment and injunctive relief against respondent board, challenging 4 Pa.C.S. § 1102(10).


OVERVIEW: The civic organizations asserted that 4 Pa.C.S. § 1102(10) violated Pa. Const. art. II, § 1, the anti-delegation clause, because the legislature did not include any standards by which the board was to evaluate the social effects of gaming. The court found that the statute listed nearly a dozen different policies and objectives that the board was to consider, one of which was the social effect provision; this did not constitute legislation that conferred carte blanche legislative power on an administrative agency to declare basic policy questions. To the contrary, it showed a significant channeling of discretion. Furthermore, there was nothing in the anti-delegation clause that required an exhaustive definition of each of these eleven purposes and objectives. The legislature was not constitutionally required to micromanage the administrative agencies it created.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

202 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


D'Alessandro v. Pa. State Police


No. 131 MAP 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


594 Pa. 500; 937 A.2d 404; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2431


September 13, 2006, Argued 
November 21, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at D'Alessandro v. Pa. State Police, 2008 Pa. Commw. Unpub. LEXIS 312 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court dated June 24, 2005, at No. 2195 C.D. 2004, reversing the decision of the Administrative Law Judge of the Office of Attorney General dated September 16, 2004, at No. FAD00514. Intermediate Court Judges: Bernard L. McGinley, Bonnie B. Leadbetter, JJ., and Jim Flaherty, Senior Judge.878 A.2d 133 (Pa. Cmwlth. 2005).
D'Alessandro v. Pa. State Police, 878 A.2d 133, 2005 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 330 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Under 18 Pa.C.S. § 6109, appellee applicant sought a license to carry a firearm, which was denied by appellant Pennsylvania State Police (PSP) because he had committed an act of domestic violence and thus could not obtain a firearm under 18 U.S.C.S. § 922(g)(9), part of the Federal Gun Control Act. The Office of the Attorney General agreed with the PSP's determination. The Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania reversed the denial. The PSP appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Commonwealth Court held that evidence that the applicant, who had been convicted of simple assault, had committed an act of domestic violence was inadmissible and that the PSP had thus not proven ineligibility for a license. The court held that a statement in a police report describing the victim as the applicant's "live in girlfriend" was not untrustworthy under 42 Pa.C.S. § 6104. The police report contained no obvious errors, and there was no indication that the statement that the victim lived with the applicant came from an unreliable source. The applicant and the victim had no apparent contemporaneous reason to lie about whether they were living together as boyfriend and girlfriend, and it was not unreasonable to assume that the investigating officer would need to probe their relationship in order to make a charging decision. Thus, the disputed evidence was admissible. An administrative agency law judge, however, had applied Pennsylvania law, rather than federal law, in determining what was required to prove a domestic relationship. It was not clear whether this had been properly challenged or what the consequences of a challenge would be. Thus, the case was to be remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Commonwealth Court's decision. It remanded the case to the Commonwealth Court for proceedings consistent with its opinion.

 

203 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Lee


No. 38 EAP 2004, No. 15 EAP 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


594 Pa. 266; 935 A.2d 865; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2436


October 17, 2006, Argued 
November 21, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
38 EAP 2004

Appeal from the Order entered on May 21, 2004 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Philadelphia County concerning constitutionality of Megan's Law cases at Nos. 0308-1001, 0305-0162 and 0305-0198. Trial Court Judge: Carolyn Engel Temin, Senior Judge.

15 EAP 2005

Appeal from the Order entered on April 11, 2005 by the Philadelphia Court of Common Pleas Granting Defendant's Challenge to the Constitutionality of Megan's Law at No. 0302-0398 1/1. Trial Court Judge: Anthony J. DeFino, Senior Judge.
Commonwealth v. Drain, 935 A.2d 9, 2007 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3787 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated action, the state challenged orders of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which found unconstitutional the lifetime registration, notification, and counseling (RNC) provisions that applied to sexually violent predators pursuant to 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 9795.1-.3, 9796, 9797, 9798 of Pennsylvania's Registration of Sexual Offenders Act (Megan's Law II), 42 Pa.C.S. § 9791 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Defendants pled guilty or were convicted of, inter alia, rape. The trial court held that because Megan's Law II did not allow for reassessment of a defendant at any time after a sentence was imposed, the RNC sanctions were overbroad and violated due process rights and that the RNC provisions were excessive and punitive. On appeal, the court first found that the matter was ripe for review. However, the court held that the lifetime RNC provisions were not unconstitutional. Defendants failed to demonstrate that the remedial regime was so unreliable and deficient that the RNC provisions were constitutionally punitive and warranted the safeguards of Apprendi. Overinclusiveness was not dispositive where the danger posed to society was so great. The clearest proof required to demonstrate that the sanctions had a punitive character notwithstanding the legislature's contrary intent stated in 42 Pa.C.S. § 9791 could not be satisfied merely by providing evidence in favor of a more generous account of the likelihood of rehabilitation than that found by the Pennsylvania General Assembly in requiring registration of sex offenders.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower courts' orders and remanded the cases for further proceedings.

 

204 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Dobbins


No. 69 MAP 2006


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


594 Pa. 71; 934 A.2d 1170; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2449


December 5, 2006, Argued 
November 20, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered July 28, 2005 at No. 1749 MDA 2004 affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bradford County, Criminal Division, entered July 28, 2004 at No. 03-CR-618. Trial Court Judge: John C. Mott, J. Intermediate Court Judges: Joseph A. Del Sole, President Judge Emeritus, Michael T. Joyce and Richard B. Klein, JJ.
Commonwealth v. Dobbins, 2005 PA Super 274, 880 A.2d 690, 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2509 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of methamphetamine-related charges. The Superior Court (Pennsylvania) affirmed his conviction. Defendant appealed. He argued that the charges against him should have been dismissed because sheriff's deputies lacked the authority independently to investigate and prosecute offenses under the Controlled Substance, Drug, Device and Cosmetic Act, 35 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 780-101 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The court noted that it had previously held that sheriffs were not investigative or law enforcement officers for purposes of the Wiretapping and Electronic Surveillance Act, 18 Pa.C.S. § 5701 et seq., because they lacked authority to conduct investigations of or to make arrests for the predicate offenses of the act, including offenses under the Controlled Substance Act. This holding controlled the present case. Moreover, the previous holding underscored a court's duty to strictly construe any statute that granted the authority to invade Pennsylvania's constitutional right of privacy. Accordingly, absent specific statutory authorization, sheriffs lacked authority to conduct independent investigations under the Controlled Substances Act, including the seeking of search warrants where no breach of the peace or felony had occurred in their presence. Here, sheriff's deputies had conducted an unwarranted investigation of private property based on suspicion rather than the commission of any felony or breach of the peace in their presence; thus, the resulting search was illegal. Next, the proper remedy when evidence had been discovered by an illegal search was suppression, not dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the Superior Court's opinion. It remanded the case with direction to the Superior Court to remand the case to the trial court with direction to suppress all evidence discovered through the sheriff's deputies' illegal investigation, and to conduct further proceedings as necessary.

Phila. Entm't & Dev. Partners., L.P. v. City of Philadelphia


No. 88 EM 2007


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


594 Pa. 468; 937 A.2d 385; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2407


July 9, 2007, Submitted 
November 20, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument denied by, Request denied by Phila. Entm't & Dev. Partners., L.P. v. City of Philadelphia, 594 Pa. 468, 937 A.2d 385, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2701 (2007)
Related proceeding at Phila. Entm't & Dev. v. City of Philadelphia, 595 Pa. 538, 939 A.2d 290, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2867 (2007)
Related proceeding at Phila. Entm't & Dev. Partners L.P. v. City Council, 596 Pa. 422, 943 A.2d 955, 2008 Pa. LEXIS 342 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Phila. Entm't & Dev. Partners., L.P. v. City of Philadelphia, 594 Pa. 51, 934 A.2d 1158, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2225 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent City Council for the City of Philadelphia (city council) enacted an ordinance that encouraged the orderly development of major entertainment facilities in the city, including gaming facilities, through establishment of Commercial Entertainment Districts. Petitioner gaming company filed an emergency petition for review in the state supreme court to challenge the ordinance's constitutionality and sought issuance of a writ of mandamus.


OVERVIEW: The General Assembly enacted a law that provided for slot machine gaming at a set number of licensed facilities within the Commonwealth. Under the law, an entity was permitted to apply to the state gaming control board for a license. The gaming company applied for a slot machine license to be located at a licensed facility on property it owned. At that time, the property was zoned for commercial use. The city council then enacted an ordinance that required the submission of entertainment facility development plans. Upon approval of the plan, all underlying zoning classifications on property were superseded. After the gaming company petitioned for a slot machine license, the zoning for the gaming company's property was changed to a residential classification. The gaming company challenged the constitutionality of the ordinance and sought a petition for writ of mandamus, but the state supreme court found the constitutional challenge was not ripe because the ordinance had not yet been applied to the land at issue and that it could not consider the mandamus request since the relevant statute allowing for appeal, 4 Pa.C.S. § 1506, allowed for appellate, not original, jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court dismissed without prejudice the gaming company's request that the state supreme court review the constitutionality of the city council's ordinance that changed the zoning designation of property the gaming company owned and on which a licensed gaming facility had been located. Also, the state supreme court transferred the gaming company's petition for writ of mandamus to a specified trial court.

 

206 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Russo


No. 135 MAP 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


594 Pa. 119; 934 A.2d 1199; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2450


April 6, 2006, Submitted 
November 20, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered January 7, 2005, at No. 1050 C.D. 2004, affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Wyoming County, Criminal Division, entered April 23, 2004, at No. 2003-445. 864 A.2d 1279 (Pa. Cmwlth. 2005). Trial Court Judge: Brendan J. Vaston, J. Intermediate Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, President Judge, Dan Pellegrinin and Renee Cohn Jubelirer, JJ.
Commonwealth v. Russo, 864 A.2d 1279, 2005 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 11 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed an order of a trial court. The trial court denied defendant's suppression motion and convicted defendant of unlawful possession of game or wildlife, a violation of 34 Pa.C.S. § 2307, and unlawful devices and methods in violation of 34 Pa.C.S. § 2308. Defendant was ordered to pay fines, restitution, and the costs of prosecution.


OVERVIEW: After the game commission received a tip that defendant's hunting camp was baited in violation of § 2308(a)(8), a wildlife conservation officers visited the hunting camp that was clearly posted with "No Trespassing" signs. A forensic DNA analysis established that all the blood and tissue recovered by the officers came from the bear whose carcass was seized at defendant's residence. The trial court held that the bait piles were not within the curtilage of the camp, and the appellate court found that defendant had no reasonable expectation of privacy under Pa. Const. art. I, § 8. On appeal, the court performed an Edmund analysis that the appellate court did not make and found that nothing in the plain text of Pa. Const. art. I, § 8 suggested that open fields were entitled to the same degree of privacy as one's person or home. Pennsylvania history and jurisprudence from states with similar provisions weighed strongly against any notion that open fields were entitled to the same heightened privacy as one's person or home. The baseline protections of the U.S. Const. amend. IV were compatible with Pennsylvania policy considerations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's determination that the wildlife conservation officers did not violate defendant's right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures.

 

207 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Davidson


No. 34 MAP 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


595 Pa. 1; 938 A.2d 198; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2451


October 19, 2005, Argued 
November 20, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered October 14, 2004 at Docket Number 779 EDA 2003 which Affirmed the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, entered February 25, 2003, at Criminal No. 1109-02. 860 A.2d 575 (Pa. Super. 2004). Trial Court Judge: Joseph P. Cronin, Jr., J. Intermediate Court Judges: Maureen Lally-Green, Peter Paul Olszewski, and Phyillis W. Beck, JJ.
Commonwealth v. Davidson, 2004 PA Super 396, 860 A.2d 575, 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3835 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pennsylvania Superior Court entered a judgment that affirmed the trial court's judgments of conviction that found defendant guilty following a bench trial of 28 counts of Sexual Abuse of Children in violation of 18 Pa.C.S. § 6312(d) for images of child pornography that defendant had on his home computer. It then imposed sentence on defendant on each of the 28 offenses, to be served concurrently. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police learned that defendant had images on his home computer of children engaging in sex acts and investigated. They determined that there were more than 1,300 images of child pornography in both video format and still photographs there. He was arrested and charged with multiple counts of Sexual Abuse of Children in violation of 18 Pa.C.S. § 6312(d), which prohibited individuals from knowingly possessing specified material depicting children less than 18-years-old engaging in a prohibited sexual act or in the simulation of such an act. 18 Pa.C.S. § 6312(a) made depictions of such nudity illegal if it was for sexual stimulation or gratification. After defendant was convicted on 28 counts and given concurrent sentences on the convictions, the appellate court affirmed. On further review, the state supreme court found that 18 Pa.C.S. § 6312(d) was neither unconstitutionally vague, since it gave sufficiently clear notice of the prohibited conduct, nor overbroad, as the nudity depicted had to be for sexual stimulation or gratification. It further found that each item possessed was to be treated as a separate offense and, thus, separate punishments could be imposed for each conviction.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was affirmed.

Allfirst Bank v. Commonwealth


No. 82 MAP 2006, No. 83 MAP 2006


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


593 Pa. 631; 933 A.2d 75; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2173


March 7, 2007, Argued 
October 17, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court at No. 619 FR 2003 entered on May 12, 2006, overruling exceptions and entering as final the order entered on March 27, 2006 affirming the order of the Board of Finance & Revenue dated August 15, 2003 at No. 0310303. Intermediate Court Judges: Bonnie Brigance Leadbetter, President Judge. James Gardner Colins, Bernard L. McGinley, Dan Pellegrini, Rochelle S. Friedman, Renee Jebelirer Cohn, Robert E. Simpson, JJ.

Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court at No. 620 FR 2003 entered on May 12, 2006, overruling exceptions and entering as final the order entered on March 27, 2006 affirming the order of the Board of Finance & Revenue dated August 15, 2003 at No. 0310304. Intermediate Court Judges: Bonnie Brigance Leadbetter, President Judge. James Gardner Colins, Bernard L. McGinley, Dan Pellegrini, Rochelle S. Friedman, Renee Jebelirer Cohn, Robert E. Simpson, JJ.
Allfirst Bank v. Commonwealth, 895 A.2d 669, 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 139 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank sought judicial review in the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) of an order of the Board of Finance and Revenue resettling the bank's reports of its liability for bank shares taxes, under 72 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 7701 - 7706, and ordering the bank to pay additional taxes. The Commonwealth Court affirmed the order of the Board of Finance & Revenue, and the bank sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The bank said the bank shares tax should be levied on its sole shareholder, but its shareholder could not constitutionally be taxed because it was a foreign corporation. The supreme court found the bank, not its shareholder, paid the tax, the calculation of which was based on the book value of the bank's net assets. Under a three-part test to find the tax's true incidence, considering (1) whether the state could collect the tax from the bank's depositors should the bank fail to pay it, (2) whether the bank was relieved of liability as to interests of depositors who had an account on the tax's assessment date but withdrew their deposits before the tax collection date, and (3) whether the bank, should it pay the tax, had a legal right to indemnification from the depositors, the Commonwealth had no enforcement authority against shareholders, the second factor was not implicated, as shares of stock subsisted when sold, and, under the third factor, once the bank paid the tax, it had no statutory means to force shareholders to indemnify it. The tax's practical effect was to tax the bank's net assets rather than its shareholders, so it was, effectively, the taxpayer.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Commonwealth Court was affirmed.

 

210 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Rega


Nos. 506 & 507 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


593 Pa. 659; 933 A.2d 997; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2176


December 5, 2006, Argued 
October 17, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Rega v. Pennsylvania, 552 U.S. 1316, 128 S. Ct. 1879, 170 L. Ed. 2d 755, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 3180 (2008)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Stay granted by, Remanded by Commonwealth v. Rega, 598 Pa. 185, 955 A.2d 345, 2008 Pa. LEXIS 1269 (2008)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Rega v. Wetzel, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 114161 (W.D. Pa., Aug. 18, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered on June 21, 2002 in the Court of Common Pleas of Jefferson County at CP-33-CR-0000026-2001 and CP-33-CR-0000524-2001. Trial Court Judge: John H. Foradora.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court considered defendant's direct appeal from a sentence of death imposed by the Jefferson County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) following defendant's conviction for first-degree murder (18 Pa.C.S. § 2502) and the related crimes of robbery, burglary, theft by unlawful taking or disposition, aggravated assault, criminal mischief, unlawful restraint, theft by receiving stolen property, and criminal conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction for first-degree murder, as the Commonwealth presented expert testimony from a forensic pathologist concerning examination of the victim's body and the pathologist's opinion that the cause of death was homicide. Testimony from defendant's co-conspirators directly implicated defendant as the killer, and was corroborated by circumstantial evidence regarding defendant's financial position before and after the murder, the theft of the gun used in the murder, and defendant's role in opening a safe, distributing the money, and disposing of the evidence. Although the trial court arguably confused the jury by instructing them to consider a trooper's statement regarding a conversation with defendant's friend "for the truth of the statement," the trial court properly cleared up the confusion by clarifying that they should "consider it simply for the fact that (the friend) made the statement." Therefore, not only was the trooper's reference to the friend's statement not hearsay (Pa. R. Evid 801(c)), but to the extent the trial court confused the jury, it also cured any potential confusion.


OUTCOME: The verdict of first-degree murder and the sentence of death were affirmed.

 

211 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Kelley v. State Emples. Ret. Bd.


No. 124 MAP 2006, No. 125 MAP 2006


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


593 Pa. 487; 932 A.2d 61; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1988


May 16, 2007, Argued 
September 26, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Kelley v. Pa Emples. Ret. Bd., 170 L. Ed. 2d 69, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 1348 (U.S., Feb. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered January 24, 2006 at 850 C.D. 2005, which Reversed in Part; Affirmed in Part the decision of State Employees' Retirement System dated April 7, 2005, at No. 2002-02. Appeal allowed November 27, 2006 at 127 MAL 2006. Intermediate Court Judges: Bonnie Brigance Leadbetter, President Judge, James Gardner Colins, Bernard L. McGinley, Dan Pellegrini, Rochelle S. Friedman, JJ.
Kelley v. State Emples. Ret. Bd., 890 A.2d 1173, 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 22 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee state employees' retirement board (SERB) denied appellant retiree's request to convert his Class A service under the state employees' retirement system (SERS) to Class AA or Class D-4 service. The retiree appealed. The Pennsylvania Commonwealth Court reversed SERB's ruling regarding Class AA service but affirmed its ruling regarding Class D-4 service. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: While a senator, the retiree accrued Class A benefits; while a judge, he accrued Class E-1 rather than Class A benefits. SERB rejected his claim that 2001 Pa. Laws 26 (Act 9), which added Class AA and Class D-4 to SERS, denied him equal protection by granting unequal pension benefits to legislators. It ruled that under 71 Pa.C.S. § 5306(a.1), his senate service did not qualify him for Class AA membership, and that his request for Class D-4 membership was time barred. The lower court held (1) SERB violated the retiree's equal protection rights by denying conversion of his Class A service to Class AA, and (2) his application for Class D-4 membership was timely, but its denial did not violate his constitutional rights. The high court held that as there was a rational basis for precluding Class E-1 members, who received more benefits than Class A members, from obtaining enhanced benefits under Class AA, 71 Pa.C.S. § 5306(a.1) was constitutional. Under 71 Pa.C.S. § 5306.2(a), the retiree was ineligible for Class D-4 membership since he was not a senator when he applied. 71 Pa.C.S. § 5306(a.2)'s exclusion of former legislators from Class D-4 membership did not violate equal protection.


OUTCOME: The high court reversed the lower court's ruling regarding Class AA membership and affirmed its denial of Class D-4 membership.

Commonwealth v. Bennett


No. 6 EAP 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


593 Pa. 382; 930 A.2d 1264; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1739


January 19, 2006, Submitted  
August 23, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by, Decision reached on appeal by Commonwealth v. Bennett, 964 A.2d 428, 2008 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3531 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Judgment of Superior Court entered on February 4, 2004 at 3511 EDA 2001 quashing the appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, at 9007-00010 2/2 and 9007-0018-0025. Appeal Allowed February 1, 2005 at 100 EAL 2004. Trial Court Judge: Ricardo C. Jackson, Senior Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Kate Ford Elliott, President Judge, Joseph A. Del Sole, President Judge Emeritus, Joseph A. Hudock, Michael T. Joyce, Correale F. Stevens, John L. Musmanno, Debra Todd, Richard B. Klein, Justin M. Johnson. JJ. 2004 PA Super 25, 842 A.2d 953 (Pa. Super. Ct. 2004)(en banc).
Commonwealth v. Bennett, 2004 PA Super 25, 842 A.2d 953, 2004 Pa. Super. LEXIS 70 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted allowance to appellant to challenge the order of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which quashed the petition for relief filed by appellant, pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa.C.S. § 9541 et seq. Appellant was convicted of the robbery of a jewelry store.


OVERVIEW: Appellant had filed a second pro se PCRA petition, requesting reinstatement of his PCRA appeal rights nunc pro tunc and claiming that all prior counsel were ineffective, particularly for failing to file a direct appeal of his conviction or challenging such failure. The PCRA court granted that second PCRA petition and restored appellant's right to file an appeal nunc pro tunc. New counsel was appointed and appellant filed a PCRA appeal nunc pro tunc from the PCRA court's order that dismissed his first PCRA petition. The PCRA court quashed the appeal, concluding appellant's second PCRA petition, from which his appellate rights were reinstated nunc pro tunc, was untimely and that it, therefore, had no jurisdiction to grant relief. The court held that the PCRA court erred in quashing the appeal as appellant was entitled to an extension to file the appeal, pursuant to 42 Pa.C.S. § 9545(b)(1)(ii), since he established sufficient allegations to invoke § 9545(b)(1)(ii) by establishing that his counsel abandoned him by failing to file an appellate brief. The court held that appellant must be given the opportunity to seek the review to which he was entitled.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order and remanded the case to the PCRA court for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

Pa. Gaming Control Bd. v. City Council


No. 55 EM 2007, No. 56 EM 2007


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


593 Pa. 241; 928 A.2d 1255; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1583


April 27, 2007, Submitted 
August 3, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition dismissed by HSP Gaming, L.P. v. City Council, 593 A.2d 358, 930 A.2d 1251, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1589 (Pa., 2007)
Related proceeding at Phila. Entm't & Developement Ptnrs., L.P. v. City of Philadelphia, 934 A.2d 1158, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2225 (Pa., 2007)
Related proceeding at Casino Free Phila. v. Pa. Gaming Control Bd., 934 A.2d 1249, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2429 (Pa., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Emergency Petition for Review of the Pennsylvania Gaming Control Board Concerning the Ordinance Passed by City Council for the City of Philadelphia on March 29, 2007.

Emergency Petition of the Pennsylvania Gaming Control Board in the Nature of a Complaint for Declaratory Judgment.
Pa. Gaming Control Bd. v. City Council of Phila., 593 Pa. 508, 932 A.2d 869, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1724 (Pa., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Pennsylvania Gaming Control Board, filed petitions against respondents, a city council and others, seeking to permanently enjoin respondents from submitting a ballot question to the Philadelphia electorate concerning gambling within the city.


OVERVIEW: Under the Pennsylvania Race Horse Development and Gaming Act, 4 Pa.C.S. § 1101 et seq., the Board approved two slot machine licenses for locations inside the City of Philadelphia. Respondents enacted an ordinance that submitted a ballot question to Philadelphia's qualified electors, asking them whether the Philadelphia Home Rule Charter should be amended to prohibit the city council and the city's Department of Licenses and Inspections from taking certain actions that would permit the use of gaming within designated areas of the city. The appellate court held that under the Gaming Act, the General Assembly obligated the Board to locate licensed facilities in first class cities and intended for the Board to make that decision alone, 4 Pa.C.S. §§ 1304(b)(1), 1307. The General Assembly did not intend for the electorate of a first class city to be given the opportunity to consider, approve, disapprove, nullify, or otherwise affect the Board's decision once it was made or to prevent its implementation. Thus, the court held that the ordinance was an unlawful and unconstitutional exercise of power, and was invalid pursuant to Pa. Const. art. IX, § 2, 53 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 13133(b).


OUTCOME: Respondents were permanently enjoined from placing the question on the ballot. It was also ordered that the application for summary relief filed by respondents as to petition I was denied, petition II was dismissed as moot, and the application for summary relief filed by respondents as to petition II was dismissed as moot.


 

214 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Finchio


No. 48 WAP 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


592 Pa. 577; 926 A.2d 968; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1453


September 7, 2006, Submitted  
July 18, 2007, Decided  
July 18, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, entered November 9, 2005 at No. CP-25-CR-0000241-2005. Trial Court Judge: Ernest J. DiSantis, Jr.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County (Pennsylvania) which declared a portion of Pennsylvania's DUI statute, 75 Pa.C.S. § 3802, unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped defendant's vehicle and noticed signs of intoxication as well as the presence of illegal drugs and drug paraphernalia in the vehicle. Defendant was arrested and transported to a hospital, where chemical testing revealed a blood-alcohol content (BAC) of 0.19 percent. He was thereafter charged with DUI pursuant to 75 Pa.C.S. § 3802, as well as multiple drug offenses. Defendant filed an omnibus pretrial motion which included a motion to dismiss the DUI count based upon the asserted unconstitutionality of § 3802. The trial court declared § 3802 unconstitutional, and granted the motion to dismiss the DUI count. The trial court indicated that the DUI statute was overly broad and created an improper conclusive presumption that, if defendant's BAC was above the threshold at the time of testing, then it had to have been above the threshold at the time of driving. The appellate court held that those issues had already been decided and § 3802 was constitutional. Thus, the trial court erred in dismissing the DUI count.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

215 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Rainey


No. 468 & 469 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


593 Pa. 67; 928 A.2d 215; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1462


May 23, 2006, Submitted  
July 18, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Rainey v. Sec'y Pa. Dep't of Corr., 2016 U.S. App. LEXIS 17524 (3d Cir. Pa., Sept. 27, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Orders entered on July 26, 2004 and August 27, 2004 denying PCRA relief in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, Philadelphia County at Nos. 9004 1967-1972. Trial Court Judge: John J. Poserina, Jr., Senior Judge.
Commonwealth v. Rainey, 590 Pa. 256, 912 A.2d 755, 2006 Pa. LEXIS 1144 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his petition for post-conviction relief, pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 9541-9546. Appellant was convicted for first-degree murder and the death sentence was imposed. The court noted that appellant's petition was governed by the previous version of the PCRA, 42 Pa.C.S. § 9543.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's conviction stemmed from the murder of a 74-year-old man wherein appellant and his co-defendant, along with another youth, decided to rob the victim at his home. In preparation for the robbery, it was shown that appellant armed himself with a 20-gauge shotgun. In dismissing appellant's petition, the PCRA court explained why all of appellant's claims were either previously litigated, waived, or not cognizable under the PCRA. The court acknowledged that many of appellant's claims were waived as a result of previously litigating the same or failing to raise the issues. However, as to appellant's claim that he received ineffective assistance of counsel as a result of his appellate counsel failing to raise trial counsel's failure to investigate and present mitigating evidence during the penalty phase of appellant's trial, the court was unable to accept the PCRA court's reasoning in support of its rejection of that claim that trial counsel chose not to present mitigation evidence in an effort to keep the jury from viewing appellant as a continuing danger to others. The court was unable to ascertain the extent of trial counsel's awareness of any mitigation proof.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of the PCRA court and remanded the case for an evidentiary hearing on appellant's claim that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to investigate and present background and mental health mitigation evidence during the penalty phase of his capital case. In all other respects, the court affirmed the order.

Riverwalk Casino v. Pa. Gaming Control Bd.


No. 27 MM 2007


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


592 Pa. 505; 926 A.2d 926; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1430


May 15, 2007, Argued  
July 17, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at HSP Gaming, L.P. v. City Council, 595 Pa. 508, 939 A.2d 273, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2539 (2007)
Related proceeding at DePaul v. Commonwealth, 600 Pa. 573, 969 A.2d 536, 2009 Pa. LEXIS 670 (2009)
Related proceeding at Keystone Redevelopment Partners, LLC v. Decker, 674 F. Supp. 2d 629, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 117210 (M.D. Pa., 2009)
Related proceeding at Keystone Redevelopment Partners, LLC v. Pa. Gaming Control Bd., 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 515 (Pa. Commw. Ct., Sept. 16, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for Review from an Order of the Pennsylvania Gaming Board Dated February 1, 2007, Granting the Applications of HSP Gaming LP and Philadelphia Entertainment & Development Partners, LP and Denying the Application of Riverwalk Casino, LP for a Category 2 Slot Machine License in Philadelphia, Pennsylvania.
Soc'y Hill Civic Ass'n v. Pa. Gaming Control Bd., 593 Pa. 1, 928 A.2d 175, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1228 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant filed a petition for review challenging an order of respondent, the Pennsylvania Gaming Control Board, which denied the applicant's request for a licence to operate a Category 2 slot machine facility in the City of Philadelphia. In denying the application, the Board denied two other applications and granted two from other applying entities.


OVERVIEW: In total, five applications were submitted, with the Board reviewing, investigating, and conducting public input hearings on each. The Board, in approving the licenses of two of the applying entities, concluded that those entities represented the best fit. The Board found that the successful applicant had the best location and design plans and that one of the entities had the least community opposition voiced to the Board. On appeal, the applicant asserted that the Board conducted private deliberations to discuss the merits of the applications, in violation of the open meeting provisions of the Sunshine Act, 65 Pa.C.S. § 704. The court disagreed, finding that the Board's deliberations fell within the recognized exception to the Sunshine Act for quasi-judicial deliberations since, in its functioning, the Board had to consider detailed confidential information regarding the applicants and their proposals, which were properly deliberated in executive sessions prior to the vote before the public. The court rejected the applicant's argument that two recusing Board members possessed the potential to exert undue influence on other Board members as mere speculation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Board's adjudication and order approving the applications for the Category 2 Slot Machine licenses to the two successful applicants and denying the application submitted by the applicant.

Pocono Manor Investors, LP v. Pa. Gaming Control Bd.


No. 30 MM 2007


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


592 Pa. 625; 927 A.2d 209; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1418


May 15, 2007, Argued 
July 12, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Companion case at Station Square Gaming, LP v. Pa. Gaming Control Bd., 592 Pa. 664, 927 A.2d 232, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1445 (Pa., 2007)
Related proceeding at In re Dauphin County Fourth Investigating Grand Jury, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2591 (Pa., Dec. 10, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for Review of the Adjudication and Order of the Pennsylvania Gaming Control Board in the Matters of the Applications for Category 2 Slot Machine Licenses in a Revenue or Tourism Enhanced Location dated February 1, 2007.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant challenged the order of respondent, the Pennsylvania Gaming Control Board, which approved a Category 2 slot machine license in a revenue- or tourism-enhanced location, pursuant to the Pennsylvania Race Horse Development Act, 4 Pa.C.S. § 1304(a), to intervenor, another applicant. Both petitioner and intervenor had filed applications for the Category 2 licenses.


OVERVIEW: Originally five applicants were involved in seeking the licenses. The Board found that all five applicants were suitable and, therefore, considered which proposals best served the Commonwealth's and public's interests in making its decision. Further, because 4 Pa.C.S. § 1304(b) placed a mileage limitation on the location of the gaming facilities, the Board could only award a license to petitioner or intervenor. The Board based its decision approving the application of intervenor upon finding that intervenor's proposal best served the objectives of the Act, with the location of intervenor's facility providing a location conducive to economic development and gaming without overburdening local services. On appeal, petitioner asserted various procedural irregularities and other claims of error. However, the court was unwilling and unable to surmount the broad discretion granted to the Board in approving an application. The court noted that it was within the Board's discretion to ignore any deadlines or procedures nor made a capricious decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Board's decision approving the license of intervenor.

219 of 2746 DOCUMENTS



Schmehl v. Wegelin


No. 87 MAP 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


592 Pa. 581; 927 A.2d 183; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1278


November 29, 2005, Submitted 
June 12, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Wegelin v. Schmehl, 128 S. Ct. 619, 169 L. Ed. 2d 394, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 12176 (U.S., Nov. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Civil Division, entered on July 14, 2005 at Dkt. No. 05-5526. Trial Court Judge, Scott D. Keller.
Schmehl v. Wegelin, 2005 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 486, 76 Pa. D. & C.4th 569 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant paternal grandparents sued appellees, the divorced mother and father of their grandchildren, seeking partial custody under § 5312 (23 Pa.C.S. § 5312) of the Pennsylvania Domestic Relations Code. The Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Pennsylvania, held that 23 Pa.C.S. § 5312 violated the Equal Protection Clause and dismissed the grandparents' suit. They appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father did not oppose the grandparents' suit, but was joined as a necessary party. Section 5312 provided for grandparent visitation of a child only when the child's parents were divorced, divorcing, or separated for six months or more; standing to obtain partial custody or visitation was not afforded to grandparents of children whose parents were married and living together. The trial court held that § 5312's disparate treatment of intact families and divorced or separated parents violated equal protection principles. The high court disagreed. As the mother's interest in the care, direction, and control of her children was a fundamental right under the Due Process Clause, infringement of such right required strict scrutiny review to determine whether the infringement was supported by a compelling state interest and was narrowly tailored to effectuate that interest. Section 5312 did not violate the Equal Protection Clause because the State had compelling interest in the children's wellbeing, there was a heightened risk of harm arising from the breakdown of a marriage, and the classification under § 5312 was directly and narrowly tailored to such breakdowns.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Soc'y Hill Civic Ass'n v. Pa. Gaming Control Bd.


No. 40 EM 2007


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


593 Pa. 1; 928 A.2d 175; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1228


May 7, 2007, Submitted  
June 4, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Application granted by, Petition dismissed by, Application denied by, Sub nomine at Neighbors Allied for the Best Riverfront v. Pa. Gaming Control Bd., 592 Pa. 609, 927 A.2d 199, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1314 (2007)
Application granted by, Petition dismissed by, Request denied by, Motion dismissed by, Sub nomine at City Council v. Pa. Gaming Control Bd., 592 Pa. 608, 927 A.2d 199, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1313 (2007)
Application granted by, Petition dismissed by, Sub nomine at Heiko v. Pa. Gaming Control Bd., 592 Pa. 610, 927 A.2d 200, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1315 (2007)
Related proceeding at Riverwalk Casino v. Pa. Gaming Control Bd., 592 Pa. 505, 926 A.2d 926, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1430 (2007)
Petition dismissed by Soc'y Hill Civic Ass'n v. Pa. Gaming Control Bd., 593 Pa. 323, 929 A.2d 635, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1476 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Pa. Gaming Control Bd. v. City Council of Phila., 593 Pa. 508, 932 A.2d 869, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1724 (2007)



DISPOSITION:  The petition for review was dismissed and the application for summary relief was granted.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Pennsylvania Gaming Control Board entered a decision that granted conditional licenses to intervenors, an entertainment company and a gaming company, for specified slot machine licenses for a particular city and denied the applications for those licenses that had been filed by three other applicants. Petitioner concerned parties filed a petition for review while the entertainment company and gaming company applied for summary relief.


OVERVIEW: The state gaming control board entered a decision that granted conditional slot machine licenses to the entertainment company and gaming company pursuant to 4 Pa.C.S. § 1204; it also denied the applications of other applicants for such licenses. The concerned parties, who had not appeared before the state gaming control board, petitioned for review of the state gaming control board's decision. The entertainment company and gaming company, joined by the state gaming control board, applied for summary relief that alleged that the concerned parties lacked standing to appeal. The state supreme court found that they lacked standing to appeal and to assert a constitutional challenge to 4 Pa.C.S. § 1204. The state supreme court first noted that 4 Pa.C.S. § 1204 expressly gave it exclusive appellate jurisdiction in the matter. It then found that the concerned parties lacked standing to appeal because they were not a party to the proceedings before the state gaming control board and did not intervene in those proceedings. It also found that they did not have standing to lodge a constitutional challenge because they did not have a direct, substantial, and immediate interest in the matter.


OUTCOME: The petition for review was dismissed and the application for summary relief was granted.


 

221 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Long


Nos. 39 and 40 WAP 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


592 Pa. 42; 922 A.2d 892; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1151; 35 Media L. Rep. 1850


May 9, 2006, Argued  
May 31, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Superior Court entered March 31, 2005 at Nos. 123 WDA 2004 and 166 WDA 2004 affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County entered December 31, 2003 at No. 4201 of 1999. Trial Court Judges: William J. Ober, J. Intermediate Court Judges: John L. Musmanno, Debra Todd, and Patrick R. Tamilia, JJ.
Commonwealth v. Long, 2005 PA Super 119, 871 A.2d 1262, 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 496 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a TV station and a newspaper, sought to secure the names and addresses of the impaneled jurors in a criminal trial. They were denied access by the trial court, and appealed, arguing that the trial court's order violated the common law right of access and the constitutional right of access to criminal trials guaranteed by the First Amendment and Pa. Const. art. I, § 11. The Superior Court, Pennsylvania, affirmed. This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: In Pennsylvania, impaneled jurors' names and addresses in criminal cases were not subject to a common law right of access. However, an "experience and logic" analysis demonstrated that the First Amendment and Pa. Const. art. I, § 11, which provided a coextensive right of access, provided a qualified right of access to jurors' names. This qualified right of access provided the public with enough information to confirm the identity of jurors when necessary, furthered the objective of a fair trial to the defendant, and gave assurances of fairness to society as a whole. There was no First Amendment right of access to jurors' addresses, however, in light of a legitimate need to protect the privacy interests of average citizens were called to serve on juries. In the instant court, the trial court refused appellants' request for access to the impaneled jurors' names because the case was widely publicized and sensationalized. But the trial court did not offer record findings demonstrating that closure was essential to preserve higher values and was narrowly tailored to serve that interest. In the absence of particularized findings, the refusal to disclose the jurors' names was unwarranted.


OUTCOME: The order of the superior court was reversed.

 

222 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Yuhasz


No. 67 MAP 2006


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


592 Pa. 120; 923 A.2d 1111; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1157


December 4, 2006, Argued  
May 31, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered November 17, 2005 at No. 3044 EDA 2004 which Affirmed the Northampton County Court of Common Pleas Criminal Division entered on October 1, 2004 at No. 2003-3797. Trial Court Judge: William F. Moran, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Michael T. Joyce, Maureen Lally-Green, and Justin M. Johnson, JJ.
Commonwealth v. Yuhasz, 890 A.2d 1109, 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 5374 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant pled guilty to statutory sexual assault, the trial court sentenced him to 24 to 60 months in prison, which was within the statutory limit of 10 years, but outside the range recommended by Pennsylvania's Sentencing Guidelines, 204 Pa. Code § 303.1 et seq. Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence; the Pennsylvanian Superior Court affirmed. He sought further review.


OVERVIEW: As defendant had no criminal record, the Sentencing Guidelines' standard range was a minimum sentence of six to 14 months. The trial court justified the longer sentence it imposed on the following grounds: the victim was only 14, while defendant was in his mid-30s; defendant was a confidant of the victim and her family; the victim described the sexual acts as "coarse"; and she suffered adverse psychological effects. Defendant argued that the sentence violated the Sixth Amendment as interpreted by Blakely because the reasons for the enhancement were not established by a jury beyond a reasonable doubt. The intermediate appellate court held that Blakely did not apply to Pennsylvania's indeterminate Sentencing Guidelines. The high court noted that as the Guidelines were purely advisory, trial courts could sentence defendants outside the Guidelines. As defendant was sentenced within the statutory maximum sentence provided by 18 Pa.C.S. § 106(b)(3), the fact that the trial court considered material not admitted in his guilty plea in departing from the sentencing guidelines was constitutionally irrelevant.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was affirmed.

 

223 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Duda


No. 24 WAP 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


592 Pa. 164; 923 A.2d 1138; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1169


September 11, 2006, Argued  
May 31, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County entered July 5, 2005 at No. CP-2-CR-0013158-2004. Trial Court Judge: David R. Cashman, J.
Commonwealth v. Duda, 2005 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 505 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee was charged with misdemeanor driving under the influence (DUI) under 75 Pa.C.S. 3802(a)(1), (2). In a pretrial motion, appellee challenged the constitutionality of § 3802(a)(2) under the U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV, and Pa. Const. art. I, § 9. The Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Pennsylvania, found 75 Pa.C.S. 3802(a)(2) unconstitutional and dismissed the related count. The Commonwealth appealed.


OVERVIEW: 75 Pa.C.S. § 3802(a)(2) was not invalid based upon reasoning applicable to the invalidation of 75 Pa.C.S. § 3731 (repealed) because, unlike § 3731, 75 Pa.C.S. § 3802(a) was not simply an amendment to an existing DUI law intended to provide an alternate means of conviction for the offense, but instead represented a wholesale redrafting of the DUI law reflecting a redefinition of the offense. While the offense was defined by reference to a blood alcohol content (BAC) measurement taken some time after driving, the prohibited conduct was drinking excessively and then driving, a conclusion buttressed by the title of 75 Pa.C.S. § 3802, and statutes that prohibited driving after drinking by reference to a threshold BAC level were not unconstitutionally vague. Furthermore, the statute was not constitutionally overbroad because its two-hour rule, which applied to drivers who drank a sufficient amount of alcohol and then drove such that their blood alcohol content was in the prohibited range within two hours after driving, versus all other drivers, was rationally related to the Commonwealth's valid interest in curbing alcohol-related roadway accidents.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was reversed insofar as it invalidated § 3802(a)(2). The matter was remanded for further proceedings consistent with the appellate court's opinion.

 

224 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Burger v. Sch. Bd. of the McGuffey Sch. Dist.


No. 6 WAP 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


592 Pa. 194; 923 A.2d 1155; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 1170


March 2, 2006, Argued; April 13, 2007, Resubmitted  
May 31, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Washington County entered December 17, 2004 at No. 2001-562. Trial Court Judge: Paul M. Pozonsky, J. Intermediate Court Judges: Keith B. Quigley, Senior Judge.
Burger v. Bd. of Sch. Dirs., 576 Pa. 574, 839 A.2d 1055, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 2586 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Washington County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) ruled that 24 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 10-1080 unconstitutionally conflicted with Pa. Const. art. VI, § 7 and that it therefore lacked subject matter jurisdiction over appellant former employee's challenge, based on 24 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 10-1080, to appellee school board's termination of him as school district superintendent. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was accused of sexual harassment and sexual discrimination. He appeared at a hearing represented by counsel and, the trial court determined, had sufficient opportunity to respond to the charges. The board held a public meeting at which it unanimously voted to discharge him. The trial court held that because appellant was a "civil officer" within the meaning of Pa. Const. art. VI, § 7, who was appointed by the board, the board had the absolute power to remove him under Pa. Const. art. VI, § 7. The trial court thus held that 24 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 10-1080 was unconstitutional because it placed limitations on the authority of the Board to remove a superintendent from office. The high court disagreed. Section 10-1080 did not conflict with Pa. Const. art. VI, § 7 because the limitations it imposed on the board's authority to remove superintendents concerned matters bearing on the superintendents' "behaving themselves well while in office" within the meaning of Pa. Const. art. VI, § 7. The trial court plainly had jurisdiction to entertain such a challenge. As appellant failed to develop reasons why the high court should address his second, ancillary issue, it declined to do so.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

226 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Sims


No. 51 EAP 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


591 Pa. 506; 919 A.2d 931; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 861


April 3, 2006, Argued  
April 18, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered August 10, 2005 at No. 1035 EDA 2004 vacating the Judgement of Sentence entered on March 8, 2004 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division at 0309-0558. Trial Court Judge: Glynnis D. Hill, Judge Intermediate Court Judges: Joseph A. Del Sole, President Judge Emeritus, and Susan Peikes Gantman and Peter Paul Olsezewski, JJ.
Commonwealth v. Sims, 2005 PA Super 288, 883 A.2d 593, 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2886 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, charged with escape (18 Pa.C.S. § 5121), was convicted of attempted escape after a bench trial. He appealed, challenging the sufficiency of the evidence and arguing that he could not be convicted of attempted escape because that crime had not been charged. The Pennsylvania Superior Court, agreeing with the second contention, reversed his conviction and vacated his judgment of sentence. The Commonwealth appealed.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that defendant tried to duck under a correctional officer's arm in an apparent, but unsuccessful, attempt to escape from a prisoner transportation van. The intermediate appellate court held that as the escape statute did not proscribe an attempt to escape, defendant's conviction for the crime of attempted escape could not stand because he had not been separately charged with attempt to escape; it did not address defendant's sufficiency-of-the-evidence claim. The high court held that a defendant could be convicted of an offense included in an offense charged in the indictment or the information, even if the lesser-included offense had not been charged. An offense was a lesser-included offense for purposes of this rule when, inter alia, it consisted of an attempt to commit the offense charged, in violation of 18 Pa.C.S. § 901(a). This rule comported with due process, as the evidence the prosecution had to present to show that a defendant committed the crime of escape, if sufficient, was necessarily sufficient to show that he took a substantial step toward committing that crime; thus, there was no unfair surprise.


OUTCOME: The high court reversed the order of the intermediate appellate court and remanded the matter to that court for consideration of defendant's claim that the evidence had been insufficient to convict.

 

227 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Rios


No. 335 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


591 Pa. 583; 920 A.2d 790; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 864


April 11, 2003, Submitted  
April 18, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Order entered on March 21, 2001 in the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, at 3174-3185 October Term 1992. Trial Court Judge: James A. Lineberger, Senior Judge.
Commonwealth v. Rios, 546 Pa. 271, 684 A.2d 1025, 1996 Pa. LEXIS 2115 (1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which denied and dismissed appellant's petition under the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 9541-46. Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder, robbery, unlawful restraint, aggravated assault, burglary, criminal conspiracy, and possession of an instrument of a crime.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from the robbery of a residence. Two women in the home were able to identify appellant, with one being in the same room watching appellant and his accomplice beat the victim then shooting him in the head. Appellant had a significant history of violent crime felony convictions and received the death sentence. Appellant was appointed new counsel for purposes of direct appeal. On appeal from the denial of his PCRA petition, appellant asserted numerous claims of ineffective assistance of counsel. The court only addressed the ineffective assistance claims related to trial counsel's ineffectiveness as it was a necessary element of appellate counsel's ineffectiveness. The court found no ineffectiveness with regard to defense counsel not calling any alleged alibi witnesses since the trial court conducted a colloquy with appellant and discerned that appellant knowingly assented to the decision not to present alibi witnesses. Further, the jury was given a curative instruction with regard to seeing appellant briefly in a hallway with shackles. The endangered bystander aggravator was properly proven since the bystander did not have to be in the direct line of fire.


OUTCOME: For the reasons explained at length herein, we hold that the PCRA court properly denied Appellant collateral relief, and therefore affirm.

 

228 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Pa. State Troopers Ass'n v. Gaming Control Bd.


No. 171 MM 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


591 Pa. 561; 920 A.2d 173; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 842


November 15, 2006, Submitted  
April 17, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Leave to File Original Process and Petition for Review in the Nature of a Complaint for Declaratory Judgment and in Mandamus Seeking Injunctive and Other Equitable Relief.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a state troopers association and its president, filed an application for leave to file original process and requested that the court invoke its original jurisdiction pursuant to § 1904 of the Pennsylvania Race Horse Development and Gaming Act, 4 Pa.C.S. §§ 1101-1904, regarding a petition for declaratory judgment and in mandamus against respondent state gaming control board.


OVERVIEW: The petition was based on the board's actions in outsourcing background investigations to three private firms rather having the state police conduct such investigations. The association claimed that the board's actions violated separation of powers principles as set forth in Pa. Const. art. II, § 1 and art. IV, § 2. Upon consideration, the court denied the association's application, finding that it did not have original jurisdiction under 4 Pa.C.S. § 1904 as the association's application did not seek a finding that the Act was unconstitutional. While the association argued that its challenge was constitutional based on the separation of powers argument, the court held that the association's actual complaint was not that the Act itself was unconstitutional, but that the board's conduct misconstrued the Act and applied it improperly. The association actually sought enforcement of the Act, albeit pursuant to its interpretation of the Act's terms. The court therefore transferred the action to the commonwealth court pursuant to Pa.R.A.P. 751 because that court had original jurisdiction over all civil actions or proceedings against a commonwealth party under 42 Pa.C.S. § 761.


OUTCOME: The court denied the association's application and transferred the petition for review to the commonwealth court pursuant to Pa.R.A.P. 751.

Harkness v. Unemployment Comp. Bd. of Review


No. 112 MAP 2005, No. 113 MAP 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


591 Pa. 543; 920 A.2d 162; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 840; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P12,509


December 7, 2005, Argued  
April 17, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered February 3, 2005 at No. 150 C.D. 2004 vacating and remanding the Order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review, at No. B-420451 dated January 7, 2004. Appeal allowed September 28, 2005 at 193 MAL 2005. Intermediate Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, President Judge, Bernard L. McGinley, Doris A. Smith-Ribner, Bonnie B. Leadbetter, Renee Cohn Jubelirer, Robert E. Simpson, and M. Hannah Leavitt, JJ.
Harkness v. Unemployment Comp. Bd. of Review, 867 A.2d 728, 2005 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 48 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An employer and the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review sought review of an order from the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which vacated the Board's order that found claimant former employee ineligible for unemployment compensation benefits (UCBs). The trial court held that it was error for the employer to have been represented at a hearing before a referee by a non-attorney "tax consultant."


OVERVIEW: The employee worked as a beauty advisor and after a rude customer confronted her, she used an obscenity when telling the customer to leave. Although the employee was not immediately terminated, as she could have been pursuant to the employee handbook, she was terminated upon her return from a one-week vacation. The employee's application for UCBs was denied upon a determination that she was ineligible for benefits, and she appealed. At a hearing before a referee, wherein the employer was represented by a non-employee, non-lawyer, the employee was deemed to have engaged in willful misconduct which made her ineligible for UCBs under 43 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 802(e). The Board affirmed the referee's determination. However, the trial court reversed that decision upon finding that the referee erred in allowing the employer to have been represented by the non-attorney. On further review, the court initially determined that such representation by the non-lawyer did not constitute the practice of law. Further, the Unemployment Compensation Law permitted such representation of an employer in UCB proceedings, based on § 502 of the Law, 43 Pa Stat. Ann. § 822.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Alliance Home of Carlisle v. Bd. of Assessment Appeals


No. 208 MAP 2004


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


591 Pa. 436; 919 A.2d 206; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 844


May 17, 2005, Argued  
April 17, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered June 15, 2004, at No. 595 C.D. 2002, affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County, Civil Division, entered on January 31, 2002, at No. 01-5659. Appeal allowed November 30, 2004 at 609 MAL 2004. Trial Court Judge: Edgar B. Bayley, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, President Judge, Bernard L. McGinley, Doris A. Smith-Ribner, Dan Pellegrini, Renee Cohn Jubelirer, Robert E. Simpson, Hannah M. Leavitt, JJ.
Alliance Home v. Bd. of Assessment Appeals, 852 A.2d 428, 2004 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 473 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the owner and operator of a licensed continuing care retirement community (the facility), challenged the order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a trial court order that denied exemption from real estate tax purposes to appellant, pursuant to Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 2(a)(v). Appellees, a county, a school district, a borough, and a board of assessment were also parties.


OVERVIEW: The board of assessment had originally determined that appellant no longer qualified for the charitable tax exemption based on its independent living apartments not being used for charitable purposes. On appeal, appellant argued that the trial court had erred in denying it a tax exemption by looking separately at the parcel of land on which the independent living apartments was located, rather than treating appellant as a single institution in evaluating its claim of entitlement to tax exemption for the entire parcel. The court agreed with appellant, concluding that it was undisputed that it qualified as an institution of purely public charity under the case law standards. In applying the rebuttable presumption set forth in 10 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 376(a)(1) and (b), the court held that there was no dispute as to appellant's institutional status and that in evaluating the real property of an institution, the basic unit of the corporation was not subject to division. Rather, the court's evaluation had to focus on the corporation overall. As such, the court found that appellant's express corporate and charitable purpose was to provide a home and care for the aged and infirm.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and held that the facility qualified for real estate tax exemption.

Commonwealth v. Estman


No. 49 WAP 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


591 Pa. 116; 915 A.2d 1191; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 382


March 2, 2006, Submitted  
February 21, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered February 9, 2005 at No. 749 WDA 2004, affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Mercer County entered April 13, 2004 at No. 124CRIMINAL2003. Appeal Allowed November 28, 2005 at 95 WAL 2005. Trial Court Judge: Thomas R. Dobson. Intermediate Court Judges: Joseph A. Hudock, John L. Musmanno and Patrick R. Tamilia, JJ.
Commonwealth v. Estman, 2005 PA Super 52, 868 A.2d 1210, 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 114 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2005)



DISPOSITION: The court affirmed the superior court's decision.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth of Pennsylvania refiled charges against defendant, arising from misconduct that she allegedly committed while acting as a public tax collector. She successfully moved to dismiss two of the charges, for alleged violations of 18 Pa.C.S. §§ 3927(a), 3922(a). The Commonwealth appealed after the Superior Court of Pennsylvania affirmed a common pleas court's order dismissing those charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in January 2003 with violating 18 Pa.C.S. §§ 3927(a), 3922(a), and several specific misdemeanor tax collection law crimes. A district court dismissed the 18 Pa.C.S. §§ 3927(a), 3922(a), charges, which were general felony theft charges, pursuant to precedent that held that state law did not allow prosecutions under general penal code provisions when special penal provisions were available. The Commonwealth refiled the 18 Pa.C.S. §§ 3927(a), 3922(a), charges after 42 Pa.C.S. § 9303 took effect on February 7, 2003. Section 9303 provided that defendants could be prosecuted under all available criminal statutes, regardless of the generality or specificity of the statutes. Defendant successfully argued that § 9303 could not be applied retroactively to her case and that, therefore, she could not be prosecuted under 18 Pa.C.S. §§ 3927(a), 3922(a). The court agreed with the Superior Court's finding that while 42 Pa.C.S. § 9303 arguably was a procedural statute, it had a substantive effect on defendants facing criminal charges. Because § 9303 was substantive, it could not be applied retroactively. The 18 Pa.C.S. §§ 3927(a), 3922(a), charges were properly dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's decision.

McGrory v. DOT, Bureau of Driver Licensing


No. 48 MAP 2005


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


591 Pa. 56; 915 A.2d 1155; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 358


April 4, 2006, Argued  
February 20, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered July 16, 2003, at 2949 C.D. 2002, which Affirmed the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County, Civil Division, entered November 26, 2002, at No. 02-5511-17-6. Appeal allowed May 9, 2005 at 588 MAL 2003. Trial Court Judge: Ward F. Clark, Senior Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Doris A. Smith-Ribner, Hannah M. Leavitt, JJ. Charles P. Mirarchi, Jr., Senior Judge. 828 A.2d 506 (Pa. Cmwlth. 2003).
McGrory v. DOT, Bureau of Driver Licensing, 828 A.2d 506, 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 515 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2003).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the intermediate appellate court was reversed.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Pennsylvania Department of Transportation (PennDOT) suspended appellee driver's license and required him to install ignition interlock devices before restoration of his driving privileges. The trial court reversed; PennDOT appealed. The Pennsylvania Commonwealth Court held that under 42 Pa.C.S. § 7003 of the former Pennsylvania Ignition Interlock Law, PennDOT could not order such devices installed. PennDOT sought further review.


OVERVIEW: After the driver was convicted of his ninth driving under the influence (DUI) offense, the criminal trial court sentenced him to time served, but for some unknown reason, did not order him to install ignition interlock devices on his vehicles, as was required by the former Ignition Interlock Law due to his multiple convictions. The intermediate appellate court held that PennDOT had no independent authority under former 42 Pa.C.S. § 7003 to enforce the ignition interlock requirement if the trial court failed to do so. The high court disagreed. The plain language of § 7003(2) clearly dictated that a person subject to the Interlock Law had to apply to PennDOT for an interlock-restricted license as a condition of the restoration of his driving privileges, or suffer a further term of license suspension. Though the high court had struck and severed certain provisions in the prior Interlock Law requiring the trial courts to order installation of ignition interlock devices when sentencing DUI offenders, the Interlock Law could be fairly and reasonably read to effectuate the legislative intention without the provisions that were severed.


OUTCOME: The decision of the intermediate appellate court was reversed.

Kendrick v. DA of Phila. County


No. 15 EAP 2004


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


591 Pa. 157; 916 A.2d 529; 2007 Pa. LEXIS 361


April 11, 2005, Argued  
February 20, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by Kendrick v. DA, 488 F.3d 217, 2007 U.S. App. LEXIS 13249 (3d Cir. Pa., June 7, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Certification of Question of Law from the United States Court of Appeals for the Third Circuit. Appeal allowed March 19, 2004 at 27 EM 2004.
Commonwealth v. Kendrick, 560 Pa. 682, 742 A.2d 672, 1999 Pa. LEXIS 2459 (1999)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state supreme court granted the petition for certification of question of law from the federal appellate court, which raised a single question of Pennsylvania law: whether the state supreme court's Besch decision established a new rule of law that could not be applied to cases on collateral review. The state supreme court then considered its response.


OVERVIEW: When police arrived at defendant's residence in response to a complaint, they discovered plastic bags containing several hundred grams of cocaine. More than four months earlier, they had executed a search warrant at defendant's residence and discovered defendant had 34 grams of cocaine. Eventually, defendant entered a negotiated guilty plea to, inter alia, one count of violating the Pennsylvania Corrupt Organizations Act, 18 Pa.C.S. § 911 et seq. He did not file a direct appeal. However, he later filed an amended post-conviction petition in which he claimed that the evidence did not establish that crime. While his petition was pending, the state supreme court decided Besch, which held that the statute was not intended to criminalize wholly illegitimate enterprises, such as his drug dealing. The trial court then denied the petition and did not address defendant's amended petition, which cited Besch. When defendant's case moved to the federal court's, the federal appellate court certified the question of whether Besch was a new rule of law that could not be applied retroactively. The state supreme court found Besch was not a new rule, but the interpretation of an existing statute.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court responded to the certified question by holding that Besch did not establish a new rule of law.

Commonwealth v. Jones


No. 409 CAP, No. 425 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


590 Pa. 202; 912 A.2d 268; 2006 Pa. LEXIS 2565


November 18, 2004, Submitted  
December 29, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: 409 CAP

 [***1] Appeal from the Order entered on March 13, 2003 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division denying PCRA relief for a new trial at Nos. 8209-714, 716, 718, 721, 723, 725, 727 & 739. Court of Common Pleas Granted a new penalty phase hearing but not a new trial. Cross appeal from the Order entered on March 13, 2003 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division denying PCRA relief for a new trial at Nos. 8209-0412. Trial Court Judge: Carylon Engel Temin, Senior Judge.

425 CAP

Appeal from the Order entered on March 13, 2003 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County granting new penalty proceeding on PCRA at Nos. 8209-0412 1/1. Trial Court Judge: Carylon Engel Temin, Senior Judge.
Commonwealth v. Jones, 569 Pa. 229, 802 A.2d 1232, 2002 Pa. LEXIS 1302 (2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found appellant guilty of, inter alia, two counts of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death pursuant to 42 Pa.C.S. § 9711(c)(1)(iv). He appealed an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division denying a new trial pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA). The Commonwealth cross-appealed an order granting relief in the form of a new penalty hearing.


OVERVIEW: The court held that because the prosecution's theory was that appellant intended to kill a targeted victim, but instead killed two bystanders, the trial court properly instructed the jury on the principle of transferred intent. Although appellant argued that the instruction given violated his due process right as there was no rational connection between the proven facts and the ultimate fact presumed by the jury, the court held that the facts established that appellant intended to kill the targeted victim and that he possessed both the malice and the specific intent to do so. Transferring that intent to an unintended victim was permitted by 18 Pa.C.S. § 303 and provided the rational connection. The trial court did not err in admitting a shooting victim's statement as excited utterances under Pa. R. Evid. 803(2) where less than 10 minutes after being shot, the victim identified appellant as one of the shooters while the victim was bleeding from his gunshot wound and awaiting transport to the hospital. Approximately 30 minutes later, the victim confirmed this fact when responding to questions posed by the police officers by stating that appellant was one of the shooters.


OUTCOME: The order of the PCRA court was vacated to the extent that it granted appellant relief in the form of a new penalty hearing and affirmed in all other respects. The case was remanded to the PCRA court to allow appellant to plead and argue his claim of layered ineffectiveness properly.
