Commonwealth v. Robinson


No. 377 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


583 Pa. 358; 877 A.2d 433; 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1328


March 12, 2003, Submitted  
June 22, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability granted, in part Robinson v. Beard, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 112326 (M.D. Pa., Sept. 30, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered on 4/22/2002 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Cumberland County denying PCRA petition at No. 96-1183. Trial Court Judge: Edgar B. Bayley, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Robinson, 1999 Pa. LEXIS 162 (Pa., Jan. 26, 1999)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner challenged a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, Cumberland County (Pennsylvania), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief under the Pennsylvania Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9541-9546.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted and sentenced to death for shooting and killing the new boyfriend of his former girlfriend. He filed a petition for post-conviction relief, which the lower court denied. On appeal, the court affirmed the denial of the petition. The court found that trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to develop and introduce evidence warranting a voluntary manslaughter charge and verdict and for failing to argue on direct appeal that the prisoner was entitled to an instruction on voluntary manslaughter. The prisoner's death sentence was not based upon an improper application of the perpetration of a felony aggravating circumstance, and counsel was not ineffective in failing to litigate claims about that aggravator. Trial counsel's failure to investigate and present at sentencing the evidence of the prisoner's increasingly paranoid behavior, paranoid schizophrenia, family dysfunction and abuse, diminished capacity, and emotional trauma at the time of the offenses did not deprive him of his constitutional right to the effective assistance of counsel. The proportionality review performed by the court was not constitutionally defective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

270 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Pennsylvanians Against Gambling Expansion Fund, Inc. v. Commonwealth


229 MM 2004


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


583 Pa. 275; 877 A.2d 383; 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1318


March 9, 2005, Argued  
June 22, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] In the original jurisdiction of the Supreme Court of Pennsylvania pursuant to 4 Pa.C.S. § 1904.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action in which petitioners, members of the General Assembly, a county commissioner, organizations, and named individuals, raised constitutional challenges to the regularity of the procedures employed in enacting the Pennsylvania Race Horse Development and Gaming Act, respondents, the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, officials, and the Pennsylvania Gaming Control Board, filed preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer to the complaint.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners filed an action seeking declaratory judgment and injunctive relief, claiming that the procedures employed in enacting the Gaming Act, 4 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1101 et seq., violated Pa. Const. art. III, §§ 1, 3, 4, 6, 10. Respondents filed preliminary objections in the nature of the demurrer, and the parties agreed to proceed to final merits resolution. The court determined that it had original and exclusive jurisdiction to resolve the constitutional challenges raised pursuant to 4 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1904. Because the legislative petitioners had standing and because all petitioners collectively asserted the various challenges, the court did not need to determine whether the non-legislative petitioners had standing. The court found that there was a single unifying subject, which was the regulation of gaming; however, certain provisions of the Gaming Act violated Pa. Const. art. III, § 3 by providing for outright distributions, while other provisions permissibly provided for subsequent appropriation through a subsequently enacted budget. Those provisions that were held unconstitutional were severed from the rest of the Gaming Act, which was sustained by the court.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioners' request for relief by striking certain provisions of the Gaming Act pursuant to the Gaming Act's severability provision but found that the remainder of the Gaming Act withstood petitioners' constitutional challenge.

 

271 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Taylor


No. 367 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


583 Pa. 170; 876 A.2d 916; 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1321


March 1, 2004, Argued  
June 21, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered on January 11, 2002 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Allegheny County at numbers 200012463 and 200013804. Trial Court Judge: Lawrence J. O'Toole, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Pennsylvania, of three counts of first-degree murder, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2502(a), and other crimes. The jury returned three sentences of death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was black, argued with a white worker, retrieved a gun from his apartment, and went looking for the worker. He did not find him, but fatally shot the worker's white coworker; he then shot four other white men whom he selected at random, killing two and maiming two. The supreme court found that the evidence supported the murder convictions. As defendant's own expert testified that defendant had the capacity to form a specific intent to kill, an instruction on third-degree murder or diminished capacity was not required. Defendant refused to cooperate with the State's expert; defendant argued, and the trial court agreed, that the expert had sufficient access to defendant to render an opinion. Therefore, defendant's challenge to the admissibility of the expert's opinion based on the insufficiency of his examination failed. The victim impact evidence was not excessive as the number of victims necessitated the large number of witnesses. Defendant's Atkins claim had to be raised in a postconviction motion as the record was not sufficiently developed. The sentence of death was not the product of any arbitrary factor, and the evidence supported the finding of one aggravator.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences of death and dismissed his claim of death penalty ineligibility based upon mental retardation without prejudice to his right to raise that claim on collateral review.

Appeal from the Order Commonwealth Court, dated June 25, 2003, at No. 642 FR 2001, granting Appellant's application for determination of finality.

Appeal from the Order Commonwealth Court, dated June 25, 2003, at No. 666 FR 2001, granting Appellant's application for determination of finality.
Safe Harbor Water Power Corp. v. Williams, 825 A.2d 733, 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 368 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court for determination were the collective appeals of appellants, 22 utility companies, from the decision of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) wherein that court held that appellants were not entitled to settlement of their respective tax liabilities before appellee, the Pennsylvania Department of Revenue, initiated its collection proceedings with regard to a statutory realty tax.


OVERVIEW: The case involved appellants' 1997 alleged liability for taxes imposed pursuant to the Public Utility Realty Tax Act (PURTA), Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, §§ 8101-A through 8108-A (1997). There was a $ 71 million shortfall in revenue in 1997 and how the Department reconciled that shortfall formed the basis of the dispute. The Department sent notices to appellants indicating their individual supplementary tax (suptax) liability, an assessment to make up for the shortfall, was due to the Department within 45 days or else the utility was subject to interest and penalty. Appellants filed suit seeking declaratory and injunctive relief and asserted that the notices were invoices that started the collection process for the suptax, and that the Department was to issue individual settlements of the 1997 suptax before sending the notices and requiring payment. The court disagreed and held that PURTA did not require the Department to issue settlement as a precursor to delivering the notices prescribed by Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 8104-A (1997). The court noted that had the Pennsylvania legislature intended to provide for a pre-deprivation process, it would have done so within PURTA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and remanded the case to the trial court for adjudication of unresolved matters.

Commonwealth v. Ludwig


No. 7 WAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


583 Pa. 6; 874 A.2d 623; 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1033


September 27, 2004, ReSubmitted  
May 19, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, entered March 12, 2002 at No. CC 200114991. Trial Court Judge: Jeffrey A. Manning, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Ludwig, 55 Pa. D. & C.4th 449, 2002 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 152 (2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Commonwealth appealed the order from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which granted defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus on grounds that statute under which he was charged, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2506, drug delivery resulting in death, was unconstitutionally vague and that the Commonwealth failed to present sufficient evidence to establish a prima facie case of the elements.


OVERVIEW: Three girls, an 18-year-old, 17-year-old, and a 15-year-old, decided to consume the drug Ecstasy at an all-day concert. They bought three pills, which each contained a double dose of Ecstasy, from defendant, who was 19 years old. The 17-year-old girl advised her friends to only take one-half of the pill because they had never taken Ecstasy. The 17-year-old took the whole pill. The other two girls took only half of their pills, but later decided to take the rest. The 15-year-old became ill and later died from an Ecstasy overdose. Defendant was charged with drug delivery resulting in death, but the trial court dismissed the charges against him. On appeal, the court affirmed, first finding that § 2506 was not unconstitutionally vague because the default culpability provision found at 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 302(c) provided a definite culpability element, malice. However, the court held that defendant remained entitled to relief because the Commonwealth failed to present sufficient evidence of malice aforethought to establish a prima facie case against him, noting that simply because he delivered an illegal drug that was potentially harmful to another did not rise to the level of malice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Commonwealth v. Ickes


13 WAP 2004


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


582 Pa. 561; 873 A.2d 698; 2005 Pa. LEXIS 945


July 14, 2004, Submitted  
May 4, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Ickes v. Flanagan, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 141822 (W.D. Pa., Mar. 7, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court dated May 24, 2002 at No. 65 CD 2001, reversing the Order of Court of Common Pleas of Bedford County dated March 21, 2000 at No. 323 for 1999. March 2, 2004 at 444 WAL 2002. Trial Court Judge: Howsare, Daniel L., President Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Pellegrini, Dan, Friedman, Rochelle S., JJ. and Flaherty, Jim, Senior Judge.
Commonwealth v. Ickes, 798 A.2d 863, 2002 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 425 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: The order of the Commonwealth Court is affirmed. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two game officers issued defendant a citation for violating 34 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 904, which required a person to produce identification upon demand of a game officer. The Commonwealth appealed the order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which held 34 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 904 unconstitutional under the Fourth Amendment of the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the Commonwealth argued that if a law could be valid under any possible circumstance, the state supreme court could not invalidate it. It also argued that hunting was a closely regulated industry; thus, all people coming in contact with game officers had reduced Fourth Amendment protections from searches. The state supreme court concluded that the statute was overly broad. The game officers did not have any reasonable suspicion that defendant was involved in contemporaneous criminal conduct. There was no crime in progress or reasonable suspicion of criminal activity afoot. The game officers were simply investigating a four-month-old complaint. Defendant was never detained by the game officers; he walked away from the encounter. The statute's impermissible applications were substantial, as it purported to give game officers the power to demand identification without reason, so long as the officer was in the performance of any duty. This power clearly reached a substantial amount of protected conduct as it infringed upon a citizen's right to be free from demands from law enforcement officials who had no articulable suspicion of wrongdoing by the citizen whatsoever.


OUTCOME: The order of the Commonwealth Court was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Brown


No. 303 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


582 Pa. 461; 872 A.2d 1139; 2005 Pa. LEXIS 908


February 11, 2002, Submitted  
April 29, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Concurring Opinion As Corrected July 6, 2005.
Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Brown, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1402 (Pa., July 6, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered April 13, 2000 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, at No. 3888-3895 July Term 1990. Trial Court Judge: Savitt, David N., Judge.
Commonwealth v. Brown, 538 Pa. 410, 648 A.2d 1177, 1994 Pa. LEXIS 496 (1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner death row inmate appealed from an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which denied his petition for relief pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9541-9546.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of murdering his father during a heated argument. Both his conviction and death sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. The inmate's PCRA petition was dismissed without an evidentiary hearing. The court affirmed, holding that 1) of the inmate's 23 issues, 11 of them had been either previously litigated or were waived; 2) while the inmate properly pled his "layered" ineffectiveness of counsel claims, he failed to prove all three prongs of the Pierce test as to each underlying issue of trial counsel's ineffectiveness, so his layered ineffective assistance claim failed; 3) the claim that the inmate was incompetent to stand trial was not waived for failure to raise it on direct appeal, but it failed because there was no evidence to support the contention; 4) the method used on direct review to determine the proportionality of the inmate's sentence did not deny him due process; 5) the inmate failed to show that the PCRA court abused its discretion in denying his requests for discovery; and 6) as the court found no errors, the inmate's claim of cumulative error also failed.


OUTCOME: The PCRA court's order was affirmed.

Payne v. Commonwealth Dep't of Corr.


No. 211 MAP 2002, No. 7 MAP 2003


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


582 Pa. 375; 871 A.2d 795; 2005 Pa. LEXIS 906


May 11, 2004, Argued  
April 29, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Direct appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court dated December 5, 2002 at No. 901 M.D. 1998 . 813 A.2d 918 (Pa. Commw. Ct. 2002).
Payne v. Commonwealth Dep't of Corr., 813 A.2d 918, 2002 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 974 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2002)Trial Court Judges: Cohn, Renee, Commonwealth Court Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Colins, James Gardner, President Judge, Smith-Ribner, Doris A., Pellegrini, Dan, Friedman, Rochelle S., Leadbetter, Bonnie B., Cohn, Renee L. and Leavitt, M. Hannah, JJ.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee inmates sued appellant Commonwealth of Pennsylvania Department of Corrections over the Department's refusal to deliver certain magazines to them. The Pennsylvania Commonwealth Court rejected challenges to Pennsylvania's Obscenity Law, a Department rule banning obscene materials, and the Prison Litigation Reform Act (PLRA), except for a section of the PLRA involving filing fees payable in prison conditions suits. Both sides appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmates alleged that a Department regulation barring their access to allegedly obscene materials violated their right to free speech under Pa. Const. art. I, § 7 and that portions of the Pennsylvania Prison Litigation Reform Act (PLRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 6601-6608, and of the Obscenity Law were unconstitutional. The supreme court agreed with the lower court that § 6602(a)-(c) of the PLRA, dealing with inmates' payment of filing fees, abrogated the supreme court's rule-making authority granted by Pa. Const. art. V, § 10(c) because the statute conflicted with Pa. R. Civ. P. 240(f). The lower court erred in finding that § 6605(a) of the PLRA, allowing the automatic dissolution of injunctions in prison condition suits, was constitutional as § 6605(a) conflicted with Pa. R. Civ. P. 1531. Other challenged provisions of the PLRA were substantive, not procedural, so Pa. Const. art. V, § 10(c) did not apply. 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5903(a)(7)-(9) of the Obscenity Law was constitutional since jurors determined if materials were "obscene" and inmates lacked the same level of constitutional protections as non-inmates. The Department's regulation was reasonable under the Turner standard.


OUTCOME: The lower court properly found unconstitutional PLRA provisions regarding payment of filing fees in prison conditions litigation. However, it erred in ruling that the portion of the PLRA that provided for the automatic dissolution of a preliminary injunction was constitutional. Its other rulings were affirmed.

Delmarva Power & Light Co. v. Commonwealth


Nos. 16 MAP 2003 & 26 MAP 2003


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


582 Pa. 338; 870 A.2d 901; 2005 Pa. LEXIS 632


May 11, 2004, Argued  
March 31, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered on January 10, 2003, at Nos. 629 & 525 MD 2001. 814 A.2d 861 (Pa. Commw. 2003). Trial Court Judges: Rochelle S. Friedman, Commonwealth Court Judge. Jess S. Jiuliante, Commonwealth Court Senior Judge. Robert E. Simpson, Commonwealth Court Judge.
PPL Energyplus, LLC v. Commonwealth, 814 A.2d 861, 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 23 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Commonwealth Court's order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant electric generation suppliers (EGSs) appealed from an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which granted summary relief to appellee Public Utility Commission Fiscal Office and ruled that the EGSs could be considered public utilities for the limited purposes of 66 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 2809(e), 2810, and that the Fiscal Office could impose 66 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 510 assessments on the EGSs.


OVERVIEW: At issue in the appeal was whether the Fiscal Office could assess the EGSs for the administrative expenses of the Public Utility Commission, the Office of Consumer Advocate (OCA), and the Office of Small Business Advocate (OSBA). The EGSs argued that the assessments could not be made because § 510, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 71, § 309-4.1, and Pa. Stat. tit. 73, § 399.45 applied only to "public utilities," and EGSs were not public utilities. The court agreed. The plain language of 66 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 102 indicated that EGSs were not to be considered public utilities except for the limited purposes of 66 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 2809, 2810. No mention was made of 66 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 510, and thus, EGSs were not to be considered public utilities for purposes of § 510 assessments. As the assessments for the OCA and the OSBA also applied only to public utilities, the Fiscal Offices assessments under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 71, § 309-4.1 and Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 73, § 399.45, were also improper.


OUTCOME: The commonwealth court's order was reversed.

Cimaszewski v. Pa. Bd. of Prob. & Parole


22 EAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


582 Pa. 27; 868 A.2d 416; 2005 Pa. LEXIS 349


October 30, 2002, Submitted  
February 24, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument denied by Cimaszewski v. Pa. Bd. of Prob. & Parole, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1036 (Pa., May 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered on 4/9/02 dismissing the petition for review filed at NO. 848 CD 2002. Trial Court Judge: Per Curiam, Commonwealth Court Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which dismissed the inmate's petition, seeking a writ of mandamus to compel respondent Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole to release the inmate on parole.


OVERVIEW: The inmate found himself in prison after he committed technical violations of his 1994 parole. Thereafter, the Board denied him parole for three consecutive years. Denial was based in part on amended 61 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 331.1 (1996), which allowed denial of parole based on concerns about the public's safety. In his appeal, the inmate made several arguments, including the argument that application of the 1996 amendment to the inmate violated the Ex Post Facto Clauses of both the U.S. and Pennsylvania Constitutions. The court held that: (1) the lower court should have reviewed the merits of the inmate's ex post facto claim but remand was not necessary; (2) under the federal decisions in Garner and Morales, the inmate's ex post facto claim had merit only if he showed that application of the 1996 amendment posed a significant risk of an increase in the inmate's punishment; (3) the inmate failed to adduce such evidence; and (4) mandamus could not be used to question the Board's reliance on an Immigration and Naturalization Service detainer in the denial of parole, or the Board's imposition of back-time in excess of the maximum presumptive range for the inmate's parole violation.


OUTCOME: The order denying the inmate relief on his mandamus petition was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Singley


No. 388 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


582 Pa. 5; 868 A.2d 403; 2005 Pa. LEXIS 350


May 12, 2004, Argued  
February 24, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Singley, 582 Pa. 437, 872 A.2d 1125, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 768 (2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Singley v. Pennsylvania, 546 U.S. 1021, 126 S. Ct. 663, 163 L. Ed. 2d 536, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 8472 (U.S., 2005)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by Singley v. Beard, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 18432 (M.D. Pa., Mar. 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered on June 4, 2001 in the CCP, Franklin County, Crim. Div. at 509 of 1999, PSM denied 05/17/2002. Trial Court Judge: Herman, Douglas W., Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Franklin County (Pennsylvania), which imposed a sentence of death following defendant's conviction on two counts of first-degree murder, two counts of criminal attempt to commit murder, one count of rape, one count of criminal trespass, and one count of theft.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to multiple crimes after he bound, raped, and killed his cousin's wife, wounded his cousin, killed his cousin's neighbor, and wounded the neighbor's wife in a senseless crime spree. He was sentenced to death. On appeal, he argued that precedent and due process under Penn. Const. art. I, § 9 did not allow a court to accept a guilty plea to first-degree murder. He also argued that counsel was ineffective for failing to request a degree of guilt hearing and for failing to seek suppression of his confession. The court found that the argument that a first-degree guilty plea could not be accepted permeated defendant's claims, but lacked any merit. Defendant's argument was based on a statement of dicta in one case and isolated lower court cases that acknowledged that line of dicta, which was not precedential authority. Since counsel considered a degree hearing, but rejected it since the prosecutor indicated he would seek the death penalty regardless, counsel was not ineffective. Moreover, appellate counsel conceded that no record evidence existed on the tactics used to obtain defendant's confession, so the presumption favoring counsel's effectiveness applied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's death sentence.

Commonwealth v. Roney


No. 354 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


581 Pa. 587; 866 A.2d 351; 2005 Pa. LEXIS 100


December 5, 2002, Argued  
January 20, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Roney v. Pennsylvania, 546 U.S. 860, 126 S. Ct. 139, 163 L. Ed. 2d 141, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 7027 (2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Commonwealth v. Roney, 2013 Pa. LEXIS 2585 (Pa., Oct. 30, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal From: the Judgment of Sentence entered October 30, 1996 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Philadelphia County at No. 866 3/3 February Term 1996. Trial Court Judge, Gary S. Glazer. Notice of Appeal Filed Below: August 16, 2001. Notice of Appeal Docketed in Supreme Court: September 24, 2001.
Commonwealth v. McGlone, 716 A.2d 1280, 1998 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2667 (Pa. Super. Ct., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Philadelphia County, Pennsylvania, convicted defendant of first-degree murder, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2502(a), and other crimes and sentenced him to death. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: While defendant and others were robbing a bank, he fatally shot a police officer. The supreme court held that eyewitness testimony identifying defendant as the one brandishing the murder weapon, coupled with ballistic and forensic evidence, was sufficient to prove he possessed the requisite specific intent and unlawfully killed the officer with deliberation. As the trial court did not hold an evidentiary hearing on defendant's claims of ineffective assistance of counsel, those claims could not be reviewed on appeal but had to be raised during the collateral review of his conviction. The "victim impact testimony" instruction mirrored the language of 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9711(d)(7) and was proper. The death penalty statute did not violate Ring or Apprendi. Under § 9711(c)(1)(iii), jurors had to determine if aggravating factors existed and outweighed any mitigating factors, and Apprendi did not impose the "beyond a reasonable doubt" standard to the weighing of these factors. The evidence established three aggravators: (1) a peace officer was killed performing her duties (2) during the perpetration of a felony, and (3) defendant knowingly created a grave risk of death to another.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Grimaud v. Commonwealth


126 MAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


581 Pa. 398; 865 A.2d 835; 2005 Pa. LEXIS 87


May 11, 2004, Argued  
January 18, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal From: the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered August 19, 2002 at No. 888 MD 1998 denying motion for summary judgment. Trial Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, Commonwealth Court President Judge, Bernard L. McGinley, Commonwealth Court Judge, Doris A. Smith-Ribner, Commonwealth Court Judge, Rochelle S. Friedman, Commonwealth Court Judge, James R. Kelley, Commonwealth Court Senior Judge, Bonnie B. Leadbetter, Commonwealth Court Judge, Joseph Doyle, Judge. Notice of Appeal Filed Below: September 13, 2002. Notice of Appeal Docketed in Supreme Court: September 16, 2002. Probable Jurisdiction Noted: December 2, 2002.
Grimaud v. Commonwealth, 806 A.2d 923, 2002 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 812 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens filed a complaint against appellee Commonwealth of Pennsylvania in the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), for a declaration that amendments to Pa. Const. art. I, § 14 and Pa. Const. art. I, § 6 were invalid. The parties filed cross-motions for summary judgment. The Commonwealth Court, sitting en banc, found the amendments valid. The citizens appealed.


OVERVIEW: Amendments to constitutional provisions were made following a vote by the electorate. On appeal, the court adopted the subject matter test for determining whether a ballot question violated Pa. Const. art. XI, § 1. As to the amendment to Pa. Const. art. I, § 14, concerning bail, the court found that the amendment was proper as (1) the ballot question did not violate the separate vote requirement of Pa. Const. art. XI, § 1 as the proposed amendments only patently affected art. I, § 14, and no other part of the Constitution; and (2) the Pennsylvania Attorney General provided a sufficient explanation of the purpose, limitations, and effects of the bail amendment, pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 25, § 2621.1. As to the amendment to Pa. Const. art. I, § 6, concerning trial by jury, the court found that the amendment was proper as (1) the single jury trial ballot question was properly submitted to the electorate; (2) the Attorney General's statement pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 25, § 2621.1 was sufficient; and (3) the court would not inquire into the internal procedures nor look beyond the recorded votes, for judicial review was precluded pursuant to the political question doctrine.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Robinson

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Lehigh County (Pennsylvania) of multiple counts of first-degree murder, attempted murder, kidnapping, aggravated indecent assault, indecent assault, and rape. The jury sentenced defendant to death for the murder convictions. The trial judge imposed sentences for the additional offenses. The trial judge vacated two death sentences for resentencing. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of assaulting four women that lived in his neighborhood in separate incidents over time. Three of the women died in the assaults. OUTCOME: The convictions and sentence were affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Williams


No. 247 CAPITAL APPEAL DOCKET


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


581 Pa. 57; 863 A.2d 505; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 3239


June 6, 2000, Submitted  
December 22, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 14, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered October 20, 1998 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County Criminal Trial Division at Nos. 2362-2367 August Term 1984. Trial Court Judge: David N. Savitt, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Williams, 524 Pa. 218, 570 A.2d 75, 1990 Pa. LEXIS 53 (Feb. 8, 1990)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County Criminal Trial Division (Pennsylvania), which denied his petition for relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9541-9546.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a co-conspirator decided to take some money from the victim, got in his car, and directed him to a secluded area where they bound and gagged him, robbed him, and beat him to death using a tire iron and a wrench. A jury convicted defendant of first degree murder, robbery, and conspiracy and sentenced him to death after finding two aggravating circumstances. The jury found no mitigating circumstances under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9711. After an unsuccessful appeal, defendant filed an unsuccessful PCRA petition. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding no merit to defendant's claims of ineffectiveness of both trial and appellate counsel. The court found that defendant had not carried his Pierce burden in relation to the underlying claim of trial counsel's ineffectiveness, and that based on the information in the pre-sentencing evaluation, defendant's alleged mental illness surfaced after his incarceration; the evaluation gave no indication of any mental impairment at the time of the murder. Accordingly, the court found that trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to rely on the report in seeking to establish mitigating circumstances during the penalty phase.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Commonwealth v. Gribble


Nos. 336 CAP & 356 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


580 Pa. 647; 863 A.2d 455; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 3135


October 10, 2002, Submitted  
December 21, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County entered 3/21/01, at Nos. 2081-2092 December Term 1992, granting in part and denying in part the petition for relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act. Trial Court Judge: James A. Lineberger, Senior Judge.
Commonwealth v. Gribble, 550 Pa. 62, 703 A.2d 426, 1997 Pa. LEXIS 2523 (1997)



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded for evidentiary hearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which denied, in part, his petition for relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq., filed after he was convicted of first-degree murder. The Commonwealth cross-appealed from that portion of the PCRA court's order granting appellant a new sentencing hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and his girlfriend were both jointly tried for and convicted of first-degree murder of a victim. Appellant was sentenced to death, and his conviction and sentence were affirmed. In appellant's subsequent PCRA claim, the PCRA court entered an order granting appellant a new penalty hearing. On appeal, the court held: (1) that appellant could not show that he was prejudiced by the joint trial because the testimony offered by his girlfriend tended to exculpate appellant, and thus, his trial counsel was not ineffective for withdrawing his motion to sever the trials; (2) that appellant's trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to object to the admission of hearsay evidence because the controlling law in existence at the time of trial held that statements admitted under the coconspirator exception to the hearsay rule did not violate the Sixth Amendment right to confrontation; and (3) that the PCRA court's summary disposition of appellant's claim that his counsel was ineffective for failing to object to the jury waiver colloquy was improper because an evidentiary hearing was necessary to determine whether appellant's waiver was knowing, voluntary, and intelligent.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the PCRA court's order and remanded the case to the PCRA court for an evidentiary hearing consistent with the court's opinion.

Commonwealth v. Hughes


No. 313 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


581 Pa. 274; 865 A.2d 761; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 3138


May 22, 2002, Submitted  
December 21, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at Hughes v. Beard, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 71252 (E.D. Pa., Sept. 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the April 4, 2001 Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Trial Division, Criminal Section, at 1688-92, January Term 1980, denying Defendant's Petition Under the Post Conviction Relief Act. Trial Court Judge: Darnell C. Jones, II, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Hughes, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 3139 (Pa., Dec. 20, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his convictions for murder and sexual assault and sentence of death, appellant challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Trial Division, Criminal Section (Pennsylvania), dismissing his petition for post-conviction relief pursuant to the Post-Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. C.S. §§ 9541-9546 (PCRA).


OVERVIEW: Appellant's claims implicated the pre-trial, guilt and penalty proceedings, and post-verdict/appeal stages. The supreme court did not believe the change in the burden of proof as to competency under Cooper constituted a watershed rule that seriously undermined the reliability of the trial's outcome and altered bedrock procedural elements. Absent an offer from appellant explaining why the maintenance of his medication was involuntary, the court would not assume counsel was ineffective for failing to object. Prior counsel was not ineffective for failing to challenge the prosecutor's cross-examination of a court-appointed psychologist. Finally, appellant argued that counsel was ineffective for failing to investigate, develop, and present substantial mitigation, in particular, evidence concerning mental illness, brain injury, and his traumatic childhood. The supreme court found a genuine factual dispute existed with respect to counsel's awareness of the proof, nature and extent of his investigation, and whether the decision to not present certain evidence was founded upon reasonable strategic concerns. Thus, an evidentiary hearing was required to allow appellant to develop this claim.


OUTCOME: The order of the PCRA court was vacated and the matter was remanded for additional proceedings consistent with the opinion.

Devlin v. City of Philadelphia


No. 43 E.D. Appeal Docket 2003


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


580 Pa. 564; 862 A.2d 1234; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 3059; 33 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2921


April 13, 2004, Argued  
December 6, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Devlin v. City of Phila., 2004 Pa. LEXIS 3060 (Pa., Dec. 6, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court of PA, entered August 29, 2002 at No. 2568 CD 2000, reversing the Orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County dated June 22, 1999, and October 10, 2000, at August Term 1999, No. 1631. Appeal Allowed October 8, 2003 at 492 EAL 2002. Trial Court Judge: Matthew D. Carrafiello. Intermediate Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, President Judge, Bernard L. McGinley, Doris A. Smith-Ribner, Dan Pellegrini, Bonnie B. Leadbetter, JJ., Joseph T. Doyle and James R. Kelley, Senior Judges. 809 A.2d 980 (Pa. Commw. 2002).
Devlin v. City of Phila., 809 A.2d 980, 2002 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 683 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a decision from the Pennsylvania Commonwealth Court, which reversed a trial court's decision that ordinances enacted regarding life partners were valid.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted several ordinances relating to life partners. Appellee individuals challenged the ordinances as invalid. A trial court ruled in favor of the city, but the appellate court reversed. The city then sought review. On appeal, the court determined that the city did not exceed its powers by enacting Philadelphia, Pa., Code § 9-1106(2)(a). Under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, §§ 13131, 13133, the city did not exercise any power that was applicable to every part of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania. Moreover, the designation of life partnership as a marital status did not mean that the city had legislated in the area of marriage because the legislation did not imbue life partners with the myriad of rights and responsibilities that was imparted on married people. However, the anti-discrimination provisions in Philadelphia, Pa., Code §§ 9-1103, 9-1105, invited people that were not residents to register as life partners. As such, the legislation was an ultra vires act. Finally, the tax exemption in Philadelphia, Pa., Code § 19-1405(6) violated Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 1 because life partners did not share the characteristics of the other individuals previously allowed the exemption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the appellate court's decision that invalidated the anti-discrimination protection for life partners and the ordinance making certain real estate transactions tax exempt. However, the court reversed the appellate court's decision insofar that it invalidated the city's decision to extend employee benefits to life partners.

Commonwealth v. Wilson


No. 230 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


580 Pa. 439; 861 A.2d 919; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 2837


July 21, 2001, Submitted  
November 19, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus granted Wilson v. Beard, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 56115 (E.D. Pa., Aug. 9, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the 5/6/98 Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Trial Division, Criminal Section, at Nos. 2950-52, September Term, 1986, denying Appellant's Petition under the Post Conviction Relief Act. Trial Court Judge: John J. Poserina, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Wilson, 538 Pa. 485, 649 A.2d 435, 1994 Pa. LEXIS 611 (1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Court of Common Pleas in Philadelphia County, Trial Division, Criminal Section (Pennsylvania), which denied his petition under the Post-Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9541- 9546, for habeas corpus relief from a verdict of death that was imposed after he was convicted for murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death for murder. He did not present any mitigating evidence at the penalty phase of his trial. After all direct appeals resulted in affirmance, defendant filed a PCRA petition, alleging, among other things, that the jury instructions were erroneous, and that counsel was ineffective for failing to challenge hearsay evidence and for failing to investigate and present mitigating evidence. The petition was denied and he appealed. The court found, first, that defendant failed to plead some claims in his PCRA petition, so those claims were waived. Second, the alleged hearsay evidence was admissible where it was a prior consistent identification or where it was used to rehabilitate a witness and where the witnesses were available for cross-examination. Third, under the law applicable to defendant, the jury instructions were constitutional. Fourth, defendant failed to show that counsel was ineffective in allowing him to waive investigation into mitigating circumstances. Defendant was advised on the record by the trial court and by counsel that he could present such evidence and counsel testified that he advised defendant of the importance of such evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's petition.

Commonwealth v. Moore


No. 316 CAP, No. 317 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


580 Pa. 279; 860 A.2d 88; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 2500


January 30, 2002, Submitted  
October 21, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended October 25, 2004.
Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Moore, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 82 (Pa., Jan. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Luzerne County entered on 9/22/00 at No. 22.
Commonwealth v. Moore, 534 Pa. 527, 633 A.2d 1119, 1993 Pa. LEXIS 244 (1993)



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed; remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was found guilty of, inter alia, first degree murder and was sentenced to death. Subsequently, the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Luzerne County (Pennsylvania), vacated the inmate's death sentence and granted him a new penalty hearing under the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9541-9546. The Commonwealth appealed. The inmate cross-appealed from the denial of his remaining claims for relief.


OVERVIEW: At the PCRA hearing, the inmate's mother, sister, and ex-wife testified concerning the inmate's traumatic and abusive childhood, including witnessing his father slash his mother's throat. While that evidence might or might not be perceived as mitigating evidence, the reason it was not provided at the sentencing hearing was not strategic; thus, the supreme court agreed with the PCRA court's determination that the jury should have been given the evidence. Also, the witnesses further testified they would have testified at the penalty phase. Thus, the record from the PCRA hearing revealed that (1) mitigating evidence witnesses existed; (2) they were available and would have testified at the penalty phase; (3) trial counsel knew of their existence; and (4) the absence of their testimony prejudiced the inmate. The supreme court found that presenting no mitigating evidence, when such evidence was arguably available, was not a reasonable tactic in the inmate's case where without the evidence, the only chance for a life sentence was if the jury did not find either of two aggravating circumstances proven. Thus, the PCRA court properly ruled a new penalty hearing was required.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the PCRA court's order granting the inmate a new penalty hearing and affirmed the denial of his request for relief on his remaining issues. The case was remanded for a new penalty hearing.

In re Nomination Papers of Nader


No. 154 MAP 2004


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


580 Pa. 22; 858 A.2d 1167; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 2241


September 10, 2004, Submitted  
September 29, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at In re Nomination Paper of Nader, 865 A.2d 8, 2004 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 874 (Pa. Commw. Ct., Oct. 13, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered August 30, 2004 at No. 568MD2004. Trial Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, Commonwealth Court President Judge, Doris A. Smith-Ribner, Commonwealth Court Judge, Charles P. Mirarchi, Jr., Commonwealth Court Senior Judge.
In re Nomination Paper of Nader, 579 Pa. 561, 858 A.2d 58, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 2151 (Pa., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Order of Commonwealth Court reversed; request for supersedeas denied; matter remanded for expedited hearings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant potential candidates challenged a decision from the order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which entered judgment in favor of appellee objectors in a dispute regarding the placement of the candidate's names on the ballot in the presidential election. The candidates filed a request for supersedeas.


OVERVIEW: The candidates wanted their names included on the ballot in Pennsylvania for the presidential election. Specifically, they wanted to appear as candidates for the independent party. The objectors, who were registered voters in Pennsylvania, filed a complaint about the candidates' nomination papers. The commonwealth court entered judgment in favor of the objectors after finding that Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 25, § 2911(e) precluded the candidates from placement on the ballot. The candidates then sought review. In reversing, the court determined that the commonwealth court's decision violated the candidates' associational rights. The Commonwealth did not advance any interest to justify excluding the candidates from the ballot as representatives of the independent party based on the fact that they had been nominated by another political party in Michigan and other states. The commonwealth court identified the correct standards set forth in case law regarding late registrations and the requirements for review of signatures and addresses. Finally, the candidates' due process rights were not violated by the Secretary of the Commonwealth's rejection of signatures.


OUTCOME: The order of the commonwealth court was reversed. The request for supersedeas was denied, and the case was remanded for expedited hearings regarding the validity of the signatures.

Commonwealth v. Noel


No. 19 WAP 2003, No. 20 WAP 2003


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


579 Pa. 546; 857 A.2d 1283; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 2182


March 3, 2004, Argued  
September 22, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Mercer County entered September 4, 2002 at No. 1020Criminal2002, appealed to Superior Court at No. 1779WDA2002 and transferred sua sponte to the Supreme Court on March 18, 2003. Trial Court Judge: Thomas R. Dobson, J.

Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Mercer County entered September 4, 2002 at No. 1023Criminal2002, appealed to the Superior Court at No. 1780WDA2002 and transferred sua sponte to the Supreme Court on March 18, 2003. Trial Court Judge: Thomas R. Dobson, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged with driving while under the influence of alcohol and public drunkenness. The Commonwealth appealed the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Mercer County (Pennsylvania), which granted defendants' petitions and dismissed the charges against them. The Superior Court (Pennsylvania) relinquished jurisdiction and transferred the appeal to the state supreme court pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 722(7).


OVERVIEW: Defendants were stopped while they were riding horses on a public highway because they appeared to be intoxicated. On appeal, the Commonwealth argued that the trial court erred in concluding that 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3103(a) was unconstitutionally vague. The statute provided that: Every person riding an animal or driving any animal-drawn vehicle upon a roadway should be granted all of the rights and should be subject to all of the duties applicable to the driver of a vehicle, except those provisions which by their very nature could have no application or where specifically provided otherwise. The state supreme court concluded that 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3103(a) was unconstitutionally vague because it was entirely unclear which provisions applied "by their very nature" to persons riding an animal and which did not. Clearly, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3103(a) did not provide a reasonable standard by which an ordinary person could contemplate his or her future conduct.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was affirmed.

City of Philadelphia v. Schweiker


No. 12 EAP 2003


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


579 Pa. 591; 858 A.2d 75; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 2186


May 12, 2004, Argued  
September 22, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered on 2/11/03 in the Commonwealth Court Dismissing the Amended Complaint at No. 343 MD 2001. Trial Court Judge: Bernard L. McGinley, Commonwealth Court Judge.
City of Phila. v. Schweiker, 817 A.2d 1217, 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 91 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a city and its mayor, sought review of the order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) that dismissed their amended complaint challenging the legality of certain amendments to Pennsylvania's Parking Authority Law after sustaining the preliminary objections filed by appellees, the Governor of Pennsylvania and the city parking authority.


OVERVIEW: The Philadelphia, Pennsylvania, Parking Authority was created by city ordinance adopted under the Parking Authority Law. As amended in 1982, the Parking Authority Law authorized cities to delegate to their parking authorities responsibility for certain parking functions. In 2001, the Governor signed into law 2001 Pa. Laws 287, No. 22 (Act 22), which codified the Parking Authority Law at 53 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 5501-5517, and amended the Parking Authority Law by adding a special provision, applicable only to Philadelphia, supplanting the mayor's appointment powers over the parking authority's governing board by giving such authority to the Governor. The provision also required the reconstituted parking authority to transfer some earnings to the Philadelphia School District. Appellants unsuccessfully challenged the legality of the amendments. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the trial court properly held that the home rule doctrine, which allowed for autonomous self-governance relative to municipal affairs, did not apply with respect to the authority, because the authority was not an agency of a municipal government, but rather, was an agent of the Commonwealth.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Northwood Constr. Co. v. Twp. of Upper Moreland


No. 12 M.D. Appeal Docket 2003


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


579 Pa. 463; 856 A.2d 789; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 2055


October 20, 2003, Argued  
September 2, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Twp. of Upper Moreland v. Northwood Constr. Co., 544 U.S. 962, 161 L. Ed. 2d 604, 125 S. Ct. 1736, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 2991 (U.S., Apr. 4, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered July 19, 2002 at 2853 C.D. 2001, affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County entered November 15, 2001 at No. 99-13429. Appeal allowed January 24, 2003 at 645 MAL 2002. Trial Court Judge: Bernard A. Moore. Intermediate Court Judges: Rochelle S. Friedman, Renee L. Cohn, JJ. and Charles P. Mirarchi Jr., Senior Judge.
Northwood Constr. Co. v. Twp. of Upper Moreland, 802 A.2d 1269, 2002 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 594 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant construction company challenged an order from the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed an order holding that appellee township could impose a business privilege tax (BPT) under Upper Moreland, Pa., Business Privilege Tax Ordinance § 1.04, on 100 percent of the company's gross receipts for work that was mostly conducted out-of-state without violating the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The company filed tax returns that reported taxable gross receipts only for that portion of its gross receipts that were attributable to its business activity within the township. It sought a refund for past overpayments. The township denied the refund and, instead, claimed that the company was responsible for additional BPT for prior years, plus interest and penalties. The company filed a civil action to recover the refund. The township counterclaimed for the additional tax. On cross-motions for summary judgment, a trial court awarded the township its requested recovery. On appeal from an affirmance of that order, the company argued that the Ordinance allowed a BPT on activities performed outside the township, which was beyond the township's authority under the Local Tax Enabling Act (LTEA), Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, §§ 6901-6924, and which violated the Commerce Clause. The court found that the BPT was authorized under the LTEA. However, since it was undisputed that the vast majority of the company's business occurred out-of-state and since the BPT was not fairly apportioned or rationally related to the company's business in the township, the BPT violated the Commerce Clause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that portion of the decision holding that the township's taxation of receipts generated from the company's out-of-state work did not violate the Commerce Clause, but it otherwise affirmed the order.

Commonwealth v. Aponte


No. 21 EAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


579 Pa. 246; 855 A.2d 800; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 1922


October 23, 2002, Argued  
August 19, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Aponte v. Pa., 160 L. Ed. 2d 792, 125 S. Ct. 886, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 33 (U.S., Jan. 10, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment entered on 9/28/01 (reargument denied on 11/28/01) affirming in part and remanding in part the Judgment of Sentence entered on 2/23/2000 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Philadelphia County at No. 99071046 1/1. Trial Court Judge: Eugene Edward Maier. Intermediate Court Judges: Joseph A. Hudock, Correale F. Stevens and Zoran Popovich.
Commonwealth v. Aponte, 788 A.2d 1024, 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3705 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which convicted defendant of possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance and conspiracy. Defendant was absent from trial as a fugitive. Because it was defendant's third drug offense, the sentencing court applied the sentencing enhancement in Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 35, § 780-115.


OVERVIEW: Because the sentencing enhancement was applied, the trial court sentenced defendant, in absentia, to 10 to 20 years' imprisonment for the possession charge, which was twice the statutory maximum otherwise authorized, as well as imposed twice the statutory maximum sentence for the conspiracy conviction. Defendant argued on appeal that § 780-115(a) violated due process under the United States and Pennsylvania Constitutions, because it raised the maximum penalty for recidivist drug offenders, making the prior convictions an element of the second or subsequent offense, without requiring they be proven beyond a reasonable doubt before a jury. The court held that § 780-115(a) was constitutional. The court found that although the fact of defendant's prior drug convictions was not required to be pled in the information charging him with possession, the information notified him of the Commonwealth's intent to seek the enhancement. Further, defendant's prior drug convictions appeared in the file and presentence report available to the sentencing court. The existence of the prior convictions was capable of objective proof, which did not require submission to a jury for determination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of sentence.

Merrell v. Chartiers Valley Sch. Dist.


No. 84 WAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


579 Pa. 97; 855 A.2d 713; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 1901


September 8, 2003, Argued  
August 18, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Appeal dismissed by Chartiers Valley Sch. Dist. v. Merrell, 902 A.2d 1024, 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 354 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered August 9, 2002 at No. 2965 CD 1999, reversing the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County entered November 3, 1999, at No. GD99-11670 and remanding. Trial Court Judge: Judith L.A. Friedman. Intermediate Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, President Judge, Bernard L. McGinley and Bonnie B. Leadbetter.
Merrell v. Chartiers Valley Sch. Dist., 806 A.2d 530, 2002 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 720 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: The Order of the Commonwealth Court is affirmed; remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a school district and members of its board of education, appealed the order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which reversed the order of the Allegheny County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), dismissing appellee applicant's complaint as untimely filed.


OVERVIEW: The applicant sought a position with the school district, but was not selected. His complaint was based on the Veterans' Preference Act, 51 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 7101-7109. On appeal, the issue was whether the board's letter indicating that it would be hiring another candidate constituted an adjudication, because if it did, the complaint was untimely and the trial court correctly dismissed it. The state supreme court concluded that the letter was informatory, not adjudicatory. Because the applicant was able to advance only to level four of the five-step hiring process, he was not among the final applicants under consideration, and the preference had not yet ripened. The applicants remaining after the fourth stage were those considered qualified for the teaching position. Therefore, the applicant was not among the most qualified candidates for the position, and the appellate court erred in concluding that the preference had become a constitutionally protected property interest. The applicant did not have a property interest in the teaching position he sought, but in the veteran's preference that only ripened when he could establish the requisite qualifications for the position.


OUTCOME: The order of the appellate court was affirmed on different grounds.

Commonwealth v. Santiago


180 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


579 Pa. 46; 855 A.2d 682; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 1895

August 17, 2004, Decided

Habeas corpus proceeding at Santiago v. Beard, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 37055 (W.D. Pa., May 5, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered on February 28, 1997, by the Honorable Jeffrey A. Manning in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division at Nos. CC 8504383 and CC 8504687. Trial Court Judge: Jeffrey A. Manning.
Commonwealth v. Santiago, 541 Pa. 188, 662 A.2d 610, 1995 Pa. LEXIS 467 (1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, which denied his petition filed pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The inmate robbed and murdered a victim and was sentenced to death. On appeal, the court vacated the judgment of sentence and remanded the matter for a new trial. Again, the jury determined that the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances and fixed the penalty at death. The inmate filed a PCRA petition, but the PCRA court denied relief. The inmate appealed, but the court affirmed the order. The inmate did not establish any of his claims that his guilt and penalty phase counsel were ineffective. Although the inmate's argument regarding his layered ineffectiveness claims were deficient, there was no need for remand to cure the deficiency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Albert v. Zoning Hearing Bd.


165 M.D. Appeal Docket 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


578 Pa. 439; 854 A.2d 401; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 1607


May 13, 2003, Argued  
July 20, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal From the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered December 31, 2001 at No. 2614 CD 2000 which affirmed the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County, Civil Division, entered October 16, 2000 (exited 10-17-2000) at No. 2000 Civil 2090. Trial Court Judge: Michael Jude Barrasse, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Doris A. Smith-Ribner, Judge. James R. Kelley, Senior Judge. Jess S. Jiuliante, Senior Judge.
N. Abington Twp. v. Albert, 787 A.2d 1135, 2001 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 973 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township residents challenged an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a zoning hearing board's granting of a zoning permit to appellee applicant to operate a halfway house for recovering alcoholics and drug-addicts in a residential zoning district.


OVERVIEW: The residents argued that the commonwealth court erred by applying an over-inclusive definition of "family" in concluding that the halfway house qualified as a single-family detached dwelling under North Abington, Penn., Zoning Ordinance § 11.122a. The court held that the commonwealth court erred in granting a license for the operation of the halfway house based on its conclusion that the facility qualified as a single-family detached dwelling under the zoning ordinance because, far from being a relatively stable and permanent assemblage, the nature of its residents was transient. In order to qualify as a "single housekeeping unit," a group of individuals in a single household had to not only function as a family within that household, but in addition, the composition of the group had to be sufficiently stable and permanent so as not to be fairly characterized as purely transient. The entire premise of the halfway house was to lodge its residents for only so long as was necessary to prepare them to return to their own families. The commonwealth court did not err in not finding that the halfway house had a profit motive that was incompatible with the single family concept.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the commonwealth court's order.

 

298 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Cruz


No. 30 EAP 2001


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


578 Pa. 263; 851 A.2d 870; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 1329


April 9, 2002, Submitted  
June 22, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of the Superior Court entered on 8/31/99 at 4363 PHL 1997 affirming the order entered on 9/25/97 in the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Criminal Division at 9012-4136 1/2.
Commonwealth v. Cruz, 747 A.2d 410, 1999 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4889 (Pa. Super. Ct., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Order reversed. Judgment of sentence vacated, and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment of a Pennsylvania Superior Court, which affirmed a common pleas court order. The common pleas court order denied the inmate's petition under the Pennsylvania Post-Conviction Review Act (PCRA). The inmate and a co-defendant had been convicted on drug charges based in large part on evidence obtained during search of the co-defendant's residence.


OVERVIEW: The search of the residence was conducted pursuant to a warrant, but both the inmate and the co-defendant filed suppression motions based on the initial warrantless entry into the home while the warrant was being obtained. The inmate's direct appeal was unsuccessful and a grant of leave to appeal to the supreme court was dismissed as improvidently granted. On the other hand, the co-defendant was granted leave to appeal and her appeal resulted in relief from her conviction, based in part on the illegal initial entry into the home. In his PCRA petition, the inmate asserted that his Pa. Const. art. I, § 8 rights were violated by the disparate treatment he received on direct review. The court agreed, holding that (1) both the inmate and the co-defendant were identically situated during the course of the criminal trial and direct appeal proceedings; (2) there was no basis for the difference in treatment afforded the inmate on direct appeal; (3) res judicata did not prohibit him from raising the illegal search issue; and (4) the inmate was entitled to relief under the holding in the co-defendant's case, and under the specific circumstances of the case, collateral review was available.


OUTCOME: The superior court's order was reversed, the inmate's judgment of sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

Commonwealth v. Cruz


180 MAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


578 Pa. 325; 852 A.2d 287; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 1342


April 24, 2003, Submitted  
June 22, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Memorandum Opinion and Order of the Superior Court at No. 528 MDA 2001, dated February 13, 2002, affirming the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Adams County, dated February 28, 2001 at No. CC-204-93. Trial Court Judge: Oscar F. Spicer, Senior Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Michael T. Joyce, Debra Todd, and Phyllis W. Beck, JJ.
Commonwealth v. Cruz, 797 A.2d 1022, 2002 Pa. Super. LEXIS 900 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered a negotiated, counseled plea of nolo contendere to three counts of murder. He was sentenced to three consecutive terms of life imprisonment by the trial court. Defendant did not file post-sentence motions and did not pursue a direct appeal. Defendant later filed a petition for post conviction relief. The motion court dismissed the petition. The Pennsylvania Superior Court affirmed the dismissal. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed three people, wounded four people, and tried to commit suicide by shooting himself in the head. However, defendant survived his attempted suicide. Defense counsel negotiated a plea because he said defendant was unable to discuss the facts of his case in a sensible way. After conducting a waiver colloquy with defendant, the trial court accepted the plea. Defendant's post conviction petition was dismissed as time-barred under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9545 of the Pennsylvania Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq. Defendant claimed that his alleged mental incapacity rendered the facts upon which his substantive PCRA claims would be based unknowable to him until the point at which he became competent, and thus qualified him for review under the PCRA's after-discovered evidence exception to the PCRA time-bar. The supreme court found that in light of the language of the exception, defendant should have been afforded an opportunity to attempt to prove that he was incompetent at the relevant times and that such incompetence qualified under the after-discovered evidence exception to the PCRA time-bar.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated, and the matter was remanded to the motion court for a limited hearing addressing defendant's claims: (1) that he was and remained incompetent throughout the period during which his right to file a post conviction petition lapsed; and (2) that his then-current petition was timely filed within 60 days of his becoming sufficiently competent to ascertain the facts upon which his underlying claims were predicated.

Probst v. DOT, Bureau of Driver Licensing


No. 81 MAP 2001


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


578 Pa. 42; 849 A.2d 1135; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 1150


May 15, 2002, Argued  
May 26, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Clinton County, Civil Division entered February 15, 2001 at No. 2000-01482. Trial Court Judge: J. Michael Williamson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part. Case transferred.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth brought a direct appeal pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 722(7) from an order of the Court of Common Plea of Clinton County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), that sustained petitioner serial drunk driver's appeal from respondent Pennsylvania Department of Transportation's revocation of his license pursuant to conditions set by Act 63, former Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 7001-7003, and holding that act unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: By the time the Commonwealth appealed the trial court's invalidation of Act 63, the high court had already invalidated it on separation of powers grounds. After determining that the trial court had jurisdiction to review the department's action under both 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1550(a) and 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 933(a)(1)(ii), so that its own assumption of appellate jurisdiction was proper, the high court proceeded to the merits of the equal protection challenge. The driver had argued that because an ignition interlock system, on which early reinstatement of his driving privileges was conditioned, cost more than a thousand dollars to install, the statute impermissibly discriminated on the basis of wealth. The court held, first, that under federal and Pennsylvania equal protection case law, financial need, by itself, did not necessarily identify a suspect class, and that driving was not, in any case, a right. Therefore, it looked only to whether the law had a rational relationship to a legitimate governmental objective. Prevention of drunk driving was obviously a legitimate objective, so the statute survived the challenge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the order based on separation of powers grounds and reversed the portion based on equal protection. It transferred the appeal to an intermediate court for determination of additional issues raised by the Commonwealth but insufficiently argued for decision.

Tucker v. Phila. Daily News


No. 47 EAP 2001


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


577 Pa. 598; 848 A.2d 113; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 1193; 32 Media L. Rep. 1705


October 21, 2002, Argued  
April 29, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Amended June 17, 2004.
Reargument denied by Tucker v. Phila. Daily News, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 1489 (Pa., June 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal From the judgment of the Superior Court, entered July 12, 2000, reargument denied, September 6, 2000, at No. 2121 EDA 1999, which reversed and remanded the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division, at No. 003644 July Term 1998, entered June 16, 1999. Trial Court Judge: Flora Barth Wolf. Intermediate Court Judges: Vincent A. Cirillo, Stephen J. McEwen Jr. President Judge Emeritus and Joseph A. Hudock.
Tucker v. Phila. Daily News, 2000 PA Super 183, 757 A.2d 938, 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1500 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part, and complaint is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, a husband and wife, sued appellant newspapers in the court of common pleas, for defamation. The court of common pleas sustained the newspapers' preliminary objections and dismissed the complaint. The husband and wife appealed. The Superior Court of Pennsylvania reversed and remanded the matter for further proceedings. The newspapers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband and wife were public figures. The wife led a crusade against "gangsta rap" music. She sued a gangsta rap artist and recording companies that marketed such music after the artist made recordings with lyrics about the wife. The husband and wife listed loss of consortium as one of their damages. The husband and wife alleged that the newspapers printed defamatory articles about the lawsuit and held them up to public ridicule, as they reported that the husband and wife sought damages because the lyrics diminished their sex life. The husband and wife claimed their attorney told newspapers that the loss of consortium claim did not include a claim for loss of sexual relations. On appeal, the court found the complaint, albeit barely, alleged that the statements were capable of a defamatory meaning. However, because the pleading was impermissibly vague, the supreme court dismissed it with leave to replead if the husband and wife were able to allege, in good faith, that their attorney unequivocally told the newspapers before the articles were printed that the husband and wife were not seeking damages for loss of sexual relations.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the complaint was dismissed. The husband and wife were granted leave to replead only to the extent they were able to allege that, before the newspapers printed the articles, the husband and wife or their representative unequivocally told the newspapers that their loss of consortium claim did not include a claim that the lyrics damaged their sex lives.

Shambach v. Bickhart


No. 951 MAL 2003


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


577 Pa. 384; 845 A.2d 793; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 659


February 17, 2004, Submitted  
March 26, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Corrected March 30, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Allowance of Appeal from the order of the Commonwealth Court, dated December 24, 2003, reversing the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Snyder County, dated November 26, 2003. Trial Court Judge: Harold F. Woelfel Jr., President Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Rochelle S. Friedman, M. Hannah Leavitt, JJ. and James R. Kelley, Senior Judge.
In re Pa. Election for Snyder County Comm'r, 841 A.2d 593, 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 967 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant loser in a recount of votes in a county commissioner election challenged a decision of the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania that reversed a trial court's order and declared appellee winner to have won in a recount. He argued that in allowing write-ins, the intermediate court had improperly construed § 1112-A(b)(3) (Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 25, § 3031.12(b)(3)) of the Pennsylvania Election Code, Pa. Stat. Ann tit. 25, §§ 2600-3591.


OVERVIEW: Section 1112-A(b)(3) provided highly specific information about how write-ins could be entered on ballots indicating that write-ins were only appropriate when a candidate's name did not appear on the ballot. When the winner and loser were tied in the initial count of optical scan ballots used in the election, and a recount was conducted, the winner appeared to have won if a number of write-ins were counted. The trial court held that under § 112-A(b)(3), those votes were invalid. The high court agreed with the intermediate court that since election laws were to be liberally construed to safeguard voting rights and since there was no question as to the voters' intent and since there was no possibility of fraud or accidental double-voting where an optically scanned ballot had to be checked for stray marks in any case, it was proper to count the votes. Moreover, the statute did not indicate that such write-ins were invalid, only that they were not done in the proper way.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the intermediate court.

MCI WorldCom, Inc. v. Pa. PUC


No. 1 EAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


577 Pa. 294; 844 A.2d 1239; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 562


October 21, 2002, Argued  
March 22, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered October 25, 2000 at 2916 CD 1999, affirming the Order of the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission entered September 30, 1999 at Nos. P-00991648 -- P-00991649. 763 A.2d 440 (Pa. Cmwlth 2000). Intermediate Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, President Judge, Bernard L. McGinley, Rochelle S. Friedman, Bonnie B. Leadbetter, JJ., Joseph T. Doyle, Senior Judge, James R. Kelley, Senior Judge and Jim Flaherty, Senior Judge.
Bell Atlantic-Pennsylvania, Inc. v. PUC, 763 A.2d 440, 2000 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 592 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Vacated for lack of jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a new entrant into the local telecommunications market, challenged an en banc decision of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the order of appellee, the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission (PUC), setting rates for access to an incumbent local exchange carrier's network for local telephone service under the Telecommunications Act of 1996.


OVERVIEW: The new entrant requested resale or access to unbundled network elements (UNE) from the incumbent carrier, and the PUC approved the incumbent carrier's rates. The new entrant contended that the commonwealth court lacked jurisdiction to review the UNE rates. The court agreed and held that (1) the federal district court had jurisdiction to review the appeal from the PUC's order because the PUC's ruling regarding the UNE rates plainly constituted a determination regarding an interconnection agreement under 47 U.S.C.S. § 252(e)(6); (2) the jurisdiction of the federal district court over the PUC's decision was exclusive because, reading §§ 252(e)(4) and 252(e)(6) together, as they were meant to be, it was clear that jurisdiction over matters involving appeals from state commission decisions on interconnection agreements rested exclusively in federal courts; and (3) Congress had authority under the Commerce Clause to enact § 252 and prohibit state court review of interconnection agreements, and such action did not exceed Congress's authority under the Commerce Clause, nor the Tenth Amendment. Thus, the commonwealth court did not have jurisdiction to review the PUC's decision.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the commonwealth court's order affirming the PUC's order setting rates for access to the local telephone network.
