In re Canvass of Absentee Ballots of Nov. 4, 2003 Gen. Election


Nos. 71 WAP 2003 & 72 WAP 2003


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA, WESTERN DISTRICT


577 Pa. 231; 843 A.2d 1223; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 431


January 14, 2004, Submitted  
March 8, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of Commonwealth Court entered December 18, 2003, at Nos. 2649 and 2650 CD 2003, affirming the Order of the Allegheny County Court of Common Pleas entered November 26, 2003, at GD 03-022785 and GD 03-022803. Trial Court Judge: Joseph M. James, President Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, President Judge, Bernard L. McGinley, Doris A. Smith-Ribner, Dan Pellegrini, Rochelle S. Friedman, Bonnie B. Leadbetter and Robert E. Simpson, JJ. 839 A.2d 451 (Pa. Cmwlth. 2003) (en banc).
In re Canvass of Absentee Ballots of November 4, 2003, 839 A.2d 451, 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 963 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A county elections board voided certain absentee ballots cast in the November 4, 2003, general election. The Allegheny County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) held that absentee ballots delivered by third persons were valid and should be counted. The Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) affirmed the trial court's decision. The state supreme court granted allocatur. Appellants and appellees were certain candidates and voters.


OVERVIEW: The absentee ballots at issue were hand-delivered to the county elections board by third persons on behalf of non-disabled voters. On appeal, the issue was whether non-disabled absentee voters could have third persons hand-deliver their ballots to the elections board under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 25, § 3146.6(a), where the board indicated that the practice was permitted. The state supreme court concluded that Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 25, § 3146.6(a)'s "in person" delivery requirement was mandatory, and that absentee ballots delivered in violation of the provision were invalid, notwithstanding the board's erroneous instructions to the contrary. Under the statute's plain meaning, a non-disabled absentee voter had two choices: send the ballot by mail, or deliver it in person. Third-person hand-delivery of absentee ballots was not permitted. To ignore Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 25, § 3146.6(a)'s clear instructions regarding in-person delivery would undermine the statute's very purpose as a safeguard against fraud. The state supreme court concluded that its precedent was clear, and it could not simply ignore substantive provisions of the Pennsylvania Election Code.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Commonwealth Court was reversed in so far as it held that certain absentee ballots delivered on behalf of non-disabled absentee voters were valid.

Ieropoli v. AC&S Corp.


No. 117 EM 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


577 Pa. 138; 842 A.2d 919; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 146; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P16,877


October 22, 2002, Argued; December 29, 2003, ReSubmitted  
February 20, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Sub nomine at Mauger v. A.W. Chesterton, Inc., 2007 Phila. Ct. Com. Pl. LEXIS 193 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County dated June 11, 2002 at No. 2098, December Term 2000 and No. 0001, October Term 1986. Trial Court Judge: Allan L. Tereshko, Judge.
Crown, Cork & Seal (In re Asbestos Litig.), 2002 Phila. Ct. Com. Pl. LEXIS 104 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a worker suffering from asbestos-related disease and his wife, appealed from an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) that granted a global motion, by defendant former merger partner of an asbestos manufacturer, for summary judgment based on a limitation of successor liability enacted by 15 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1929.1. They argued that the statute as applied to them violated Pa. Const. art. I, § 11.


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted § 1929.1 in an effort to provide some protection to innocent acquirers of companies that were eventually held liable as asbestos manufacturers. The worker and his wife sued many manufacturers of asbestos as possible contributors of asbestos to which he had been exposed at work. The merger partner, for only a few weeks, owned that division of a company it acquired that had at one time manufactured asbestos products. Because of the seriousness of the constitutional challenge and the legislation, the high court exercised extraordinary jurisdiction to grant direct review. The Remedies Clause of Pa. Const. art. I, § 11 operated to protect litigants against retrospective abolition of claims that had already accrued as causes of action. It applied when the effect of retrospective application of legislation eliminated a remedy altogether. Therefore, while the court did not invalidate the whole statute, it held that it could not be applied to cut off the rights of the worker, whose claim against the merger partner had accrued, even though he still had claims against other manufacturers. Each of his claims was separate, and required a remedy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment.

DOT v. Taylor


No. 52 WAP 2000


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


576 Pa. 622; 841 A.2d 108; 2004 Pa. LEXIS 25


March 7, 2001, Submitted  
January 20, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered February 1, 2000, at No. 1016PGH1998, affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, entered March 9, 1998, at No. CC 9610950. Trial Court Judge: John A. Zottola, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Joseph A. Del Sole, President Judge, Joseph A. Hudock, Kate Ford Elliott, John L. Musmanno, Joan Orie Melvin, Zoran Popovich, James R. Cavanaugh and Justin M. Johnson, JJ. 2000 PA Super 27, 746 A.2d 626 (Pa. Super. 2000).
DOT v. Taylor, 2000 PA Super 27, 746 A.2d 626, 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 75 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Order reversed. Subpoena quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant department of transportation (DOT) sought review from the order of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the order of the lower court denying its motion to quash appellee's subpoena duces tecum and directing the DOT to produce the items that were covered by 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3754(b). The trial court had stayed its order and certified the question of the applicability of the statutory privilege for interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether the statutory privilege set forth in § 3754(b) justified the DOT in moving to quash appellee's subpoena, which sought the DOT's accident reports, safety studies, and accident investigations for the purpose of preparing his defense in a criminal prosecution. The lower courts construed the privilege not according to its plain language, but in a narrower fashion dictated by their view of the statute's alleged purpose. So construed, the lower courts held that the statutory privilege did not extend to the request made by appellee. The instant court held the DOT's documents were privileged under § 3754(b) and the statute, so applied, was not unconstitutional. To allow discovery of these accident reports and studies in collateral matters would have directly countered the statutory mandate of promoting a safe and efficient highway system by providing the DOT with unbiased and accurate information unfettered by involving its employees and consultants in collateral legal actions or other proceedings of any type. Such restriction was an appropriate manner designed to achieve important governmental objectives: a safe and efficient highway system in Pennsylvania.


OUTCOME: The order of the Superior Court was reversed and the subpoena was quashed.

Lehman v. Pa. State Police


No. 60 MAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


576 Pa. 365; 839 A.2d 265; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 2603


December 4, 2002, Argued  
December 30, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered 8-17-2001 at No. 2446 CD 2000 affirming the Order of the Office of Attorney General dated 10-2-2001. Intermediate Court Judges: Colins, James Gardner, President Judge. McGinley, Bernard L., Judge. Smith-Ribner, Doris A., Judge. Pellegrini, Dan, Judge. Leadbetter, Bonnie B., Judge. Doyle, Joseph T., Senior Judge. Kelley, James R., Senior Judge.
Lehman v. State Police, 782 A.2d 623, 2001 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 620 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part. Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a person convicted of larceny, could not purchase a firearm due to § 922 (18 U.S.C.S. § 922) of the Federal Gun Control Act (GCA), according to appellee, the Pennsylvania State Police (PSP). He challenged the denial administratively, and before the Commonwealth Court. He appealed the Commonwealth Court's decision.


OVERVIEW: In 1962, appellant was convicted of larceny for stealing a case of beer. During an attempt to buy a rifle, a PSP background check revealed the conviction, and his purchase was denied. Appellant sought a hearing because a larceny conviction was not a disqualifying offense under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6105(b). Before the hearing, the PSP informed him the real basis for his denial was § 922 of the GCA. An administrative law judge (ALJ) affirmed the denial under the GCA and the Pennsylvania Uniform Firearms Act. The lower court deemed all of appellant's constitutional claims, with the exception of the ex post facto issue, to be waived. The instant court considered whether § 922(g) was an ex post facto law and whether the lower court erred in not addressing all of appellant's constitutional claims. The PSP's waiver argument overlooked two inconvenient facts: the distinction between facial and "as applied" challenges under 2 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 703(a) was not expressly established at the time of appellant's hearing, and the ALJ specifically disclaimed-having jurisdiction to hear any of appellant's constitutional claims. Thus, the court could not apply the waiver rule.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed in part and reversed in part. The case was remanded to the Commonwealth Court with directions to remand to the ALJ for further proceedings. Appellant was given the opportunity on remand to present his other constitutional challenges to the application of the GCA to his case.

Nixon v. Dep't of Pub. Welfare


No. 004 MAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


576 Pa. 385; 839 A.2d 277; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 2604


April 8, 2003, Argued  
December 30, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered December 11, 2001 at No. 359 M.D. 2000. Trial Court Judges: Bernard L. McGinley, Doris A. Smith-Ribner, Dan Pelligrini and Rochelle S. Friedman, Commonwealth Court Judges, James R. Kelley and Jim Flaherty, Commonwealth Court Senior Judges, and Joseph Doyle, Judge.
Nixon v. Commonwealth, 789 A.2d 376, 2001 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 882 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, the Department of Aging, the Department of Public Welfare, and the Department of Health, challenged an order of a commonwealth court (Pennsylvania), which declared the criminal records chapter, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 35, §§ 10225.501-10225.508, of the Older Adults Protective Services Act (OAPSA), Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 35, §§ 10225.101-10225.5102, unconstitutional as applied to appellee employees.


OVERVIEW: The employees and appellee, a nonprofit corporation that administered programs under the OAPSA, contended that the criminal records chapter, which prohibited the employment of convicted criminals who were not working in a facility or who had worked in a facility for less than a year, violated their rights to due process under Pa. Const. art. I, § 1. The commonwealth court granted summary relief to appellees. Affirming, the court held that (1) the right to engage in a particular occupation was protected by art. I, § 1, but it was not a fundamental right; thus, the criminal records chapter was subject to a rational basis test; (2) although the goal of protecting the Commonwealth's vulnerable citizens from those deemed incapable of safely providing for them was legitimate, there was no basis to distinguish between caretakers with convictions who had held a job for a year before the effective date of the chapter, from those who had not; and (3) the criminal records chapter, particularly with regard to its application to the employees, did not bear a real and substantial relationship to the Commonwealth's interest in protecting the elderly, disabled, and infirm from victimization.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commonwealth court's decision, although for different reasons, and held that the chapter was unconstitutional because it infringed on the employees' rights to pursue an occupation.

In re Realen Valley Forge Greenes Assocs.

Related proceeding at Realen Valley Forge Greenes Assocs. v. Timoney, 2009 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 280 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered on 6/4/02 at No. 2782 CD 2000 affirming the Order of Montgomery County CCP, Civil Division, entered 12-01-2000 at No. 99-16287. Trial Court Judges: Ken H. Albright and William J. Furber, Jr., JJ. Intermediate Court Judges: Bonnie B. Leadbetter, Judge, Joseph T. Doyle, Senior Judge and Jim Flaherty, Senior Judge.
Timoney v. Upper Merion Twp., 66 Fed. Appx. 403, 2003 U.S. App. LEXIS 10584 (3d Cir. Pa., 2003)
In re Realen Valley Forge Greenes Assocs., 799 A.2d 938, 2002 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 438 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2002)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a potential purchaser of property, challenged an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a trial court's decision that approved of a town zoning board's rejection of the purchaser's challenge to the agricultural zoning designation of golf club property. The purchaser contended that the designation constituted unlawful spot zoning and special legislation.


OVERVIEW: The property, containing about 135 acres, was open space located adjacent to the region's primary highways and to one of the most intensely developed commercial areas in the region. The zoning board rejected the purchaser's challenge on the ground that the difference in zoning treatment between the agriculturally designated property and the adjoining properties, all of which were designated for intense, commercial development, was justified by, inter alia, the road frontage, adjoining and existing uses, and the large size of the property. Reversing, the court held that the agricultural designation, which was designed to "freeze" the property's substantially undeveloped state in order to serve the public interest as "green space," constituted unlawful "reverse spot zoning" because the large size of the tract was not determinative and, apart from a bare assertion that it was so, neither the zoning board nor the courts below offered authority to support the proposition that the location of the highways made agricultural zoning appropriate for the property while the properties on the opposite side of the same roadways were appropriately zoned for intense, commercial use.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the intermediate appellate court upholding the validity of the zoning designation and remanded to the court of common pleas for further proceedings.


 

310 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Maldonado


No. 130 MAP 2001


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


576 Pa. 101; 838 A.2d 710; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 2404


December 23, 2002, Submitted  
December 18, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Centre County, Criminal Division, entered on 8/13/01 at No. 2000-1620. Trial Court Judge: Charles C. Brown Jr., President Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Centre County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which ruled that the statutory procedure for determining whether defendant was a sexually violent predator under the Registration of Sexual Offenders Act (Megan's Law), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9791-9799.7, was inconsistent with the Fourteenth Amendment's Due Process Clause.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered pleas on several misdemeanor-one indecent assault charges, a predicate offense triggering a Megan's Law assessment of whether defendant was a sexually violent predator. The trial court refused to order the assessment, holding that the Law used an improper evidentiary standard. The question before the supreme court was whether sexually violent predator status had to be proven beyond a reasonable doubt. The supreme court ruled that it did not and that the "clear and convincing evidence" standard outlined in Megan's Law was an appropriate standard of proof. Proof beyond a reasonable doubt was too burdensome in view of the Commonwealth's need to protect its citizens from individuals who had committed a predicate offense and who additionally suffered from a volitional impairment making them likely to recidivate. That standard was properly reserved for criminal prosecutions. And, although an individual adjudicated as a sexually violent predator might suffer a substantial imposition upon his liberty interests, the harm to the public of erroneous exclusion of a sexually violent predator supported the clear and convincing standard and was consistent with due process.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the trial court's order and remanded the case for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

S. Newton Twp. Electors v. S. Newton Twp. Supervisor


No. 146 MAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


575 Pa. 670; 838 A.2d 643; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 2361


September 8, 2003, Argued  
December 17, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County, entered September 6, 2002, at No. 02-1916. Trial Court Judge: George E. Hoffer, President Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant residents filed a pro se complaint seeking to remove appellee official from his position as township supervisor pursuant to Pa. Stat. tit. 53, § 65503 for dereliction of his duties. A three-judge panel sustained the official's preliminary objections and dismissed the action. The Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County, Pennsylvania, agreed with the official, finding § 65503 was unconstitutional. The residents appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the residents contended the trial court erred in finding that Pa. Stat. tit. 53, § 65503 conflicted with Pa. Const. art. VI, § 7, and that it was thus unconstitutional. The supreme court found the fact that § 7 did not explicitly spell out the manner in which § 7 was to be invoked did not make the method of removal unclear. Moreover, even if the constitutional removal method was not as practical as the one provided for in Pa. Stat. tit. 53, § 65503, the supreme court could not disregard a controlling constitutional provision. Although legislation that regulated the manner and causes of removal of township supervisors existed prior to the 1874 Pennsylvania Constitution, this fact did not make § 65503 constitutional, as it was not until after the 1874 Pennsylvania Constitution that there was legislation allowing for the removal of township supervisors for neglect in performing duties. As such, the supreme court held that the provisions of § 65503 were violative of Pa. Const. art. VI, § 7.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

312 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


In re Adoption of S.A.J. (In re S.S.)


No. 163 MAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


575 Pa. 624; 838 A.2d 616; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 2363


May 13, 2003, Argued  
December 17, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court, entered March 19, 2002, at No. 899MDA2001, reversing and remanding the Judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Orphans' Court Division, entered May 2, 2001 at No. 76828. 812 A.2d 1230 (Pa. Super. 2002). Trial Court Judge: Peter W. Schmehl, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Correale F. Stevens, Phyllis W. Beck and James R. Cavanaugh, JJ.
In re Adoption of S.A.J., 2002 PA Super 73, 797 A.2d 299, 2002 Pa. Super. LEXIS 332 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant putative father challenged an order of the superior court (Pennsylvania), which reversed and remanded a judgment of the court of common pleas and which held that the putative father was judicially estopped from challenging a child's adoption by the mother's husband because he had previously denied paternity at a prior child support proceeding and had successfully avoiding paying child support for 12 years.


OVERVIEW: Eleven years before the adoption, the putative father filed for partial custody of the child and made visits for approximately one year until the mother filed for child support. The putative father then denied paternity and did not help in any way, visit, provide support, or make any demands to be part of the life of child. Affirming, the court held that: (1) the putative father was barred from asserting paternity by the doctrine of judicial estoppel because he did not adequately explain the contradiction between his judicial statements and his denial of paternity was successfully asserted in the child support action; (2) the needs of the child, which was the court's paramount concern, favored her adoption by her mother's husband who had supported her for 10 years; (3) the putative father's assertion of paternity was also barred by the doctrine of equitable estoppel; and (4) although the mother made inconsistent statements, the paternity was actually unknown, and there was no evidence that the mother and her husband's failure to obtain the consent of the putative father constituted "fraud or deceit," so as to bar judicial estoppel for violation of the clean hands doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the superior court.

Hydropress Envtl. Servs. v. Twp. of Upper Mount Bethel


No. 112 MAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


575 Pa. 479; 836 A.2d 912; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 2195


April 8, 2003, Argued  
November 25, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court, entered March 7, 2002 at No. 1436 CD 2001, affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County, entered May 30, 2001 at No. C0048-CV-2000-009008. Trial Court Judges: McFadden, F. P. Kimberly, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: McGinley, Bernard L., Judge, Friedman, Rochelle S., Judge, Mirarchi Jr., Charles P., Senior Judge.
Twp. of Upper Mt. Bethel v. Hydropress Envtl. Servs., 796 A.2d 440, 2002 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 190 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township sought review from an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee biosolids processor in its declaratory judgment action, wherein Upper Mount Bethel, Pa., Ordinance 2001-01 was held invalid, the township was permanently enjoined from enforcing it, and the processor was allowed to resume its operations.


OVERVIEW: The biosolids processor was a New Jersey corporation that obtained a beneficial use order approval from the Pennsylvania Department of Environmental Protection, allowing it to spread its biosolids on agricultural lands in Pennsylvania. The approval was suspended and the processor was given permission to conduct demonstration projects, which it intended to do within the township upon proper approvals being obtained. The township passed Ordinance 2001-01, which attempted to locally regulate land application of sludge-derived products. The processor contended that the ordinance was illegal because the matter was preempted by the Solid Waste Management Act (SWMA), Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 35, §§ 6018.101-.1003. Initially, the court determined that the processor had standing because its interest was direct, substantial, and immediate. The court found that while the SWMA did not preempt local regulation in that area, the township had exceeded its authority by imposing standards, such as imposing road user charges, that went beyond those necessary to protect the general welfare. Such excess power was not within the grant of powers to the township by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order to the extent that it affirmed the trial court's order that declared the ordinance invalid in its entirety and permanently enjoined the township from enforcing it. The court affirmed the order to the extent that the trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the processor, which in effect permanently enjoined enforcement of certain portions of the ordinance.

In re Forrester


161 MAP 2001


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


575 Pa. 365; 836 A.2d 102; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 2180


May 15, 2002, Argued  
November 20, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered on 5/2/01 at No. 1299 CD 2000 which affirmed the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Franklin County, Civil Division, entered on 5/4/00 at No. 1997-390. Trial Court Judge: John R. Walker, President Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, President Judge, James R. Kelley, Senior Judge and Samuel L. Rodgers, Senior Judge.
In re Forrester, 773 A.2d 219, 2001 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 277 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant farm owners sought review of the order of the Pennsylvania Commonwealth Court finding that appellee landlocked property owner established the necessity sufficient to entitle the landlocked property owner to have a private road opened leading to his property and finding that no approval was needed from the Pennsylvania Agricultural Lands Condemnation Approval Board prior to opening the private road.


OVERVIEW: The landlocked property owner's land was landlocked, and he sought to locate and open a private road from his property over farmland owned by the farm owners. The farm owners' land was located in an agricultural security area as defined by the Pennsylvania Agricultural Area Security Law, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 3, § 901 et seq. The farm owners argued that the private road could not be opened without the approval of the Pennsylvania Agricultural Lands Condemnation Approval Board. The Pennsylvania Supreme Court found that the Board did not need to grant approval prior to the opening of a private road on land within an agricultural security area. The supreme court found that the opening of a private road did not constitute an exercise of eminent domain power under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 3, § 913, as the public was not to be the primary beneficiary of the private road. As a result, the opening of the private road pursuant to the Pennsylvania Private Road Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 36, § 2731 et seq., did not constitute a taking that was subject to the protections under the Pennsylvania Agricultural Area Security Law.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Melvin v. Doe


Nos. 50-51 WAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


575 Pa. 264; 836 A.2d 42; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 2162; 32 Media L. Rep. 1599


March 3, 2003, Argued  
November 19, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered November 20, 2001, at Nos. 211516WDA2000, reversing the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, entered November 15, 2000, at Nos.GD99-10264 and 99-16190. Trial Court Judge: R. Stanton Wettick Jr., Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Joseph A. Del Sole, President Judge, Justin M. Johnson, Judge and John G. Brosky, Judge.
Melvin v. Doe, 2001 PA Super 330, 789 A.2d 696, 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3443 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, unidentified individuals, sought review from an order of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which quashed their appeal from a trial court's order, requiring them to reveal their identities to appellee former judge. The judge sought their identities in connection with a statement that they published on an internet webpage about him, which he alleged was defamatory.


OVERVIEW: The individuals published a statement about the judge on a webpage, indicating that he had engaged in misconduct by lobbying for the appointment of an attorney to a judgeship. The judge commenced a defamation action and sought to discover the identities of the individuals who authored the page. The trial court denied the individuals' motion for summary judgment, and denied their motion for a protective order against such disclosure. It ordered the individuals to reveal their identities, subject to a confidentiality order. The superior court quashed the appeal, finding that the summary judgment denial was not a collateral order and that the protective order was not appealable. On further appeal by the individuals, the supreme court found that the summary judgment order did not qualify as a collateral order, nor was it a final order. However, it found that the discovery order relating to the denial of the protective order was an exception to the final order rule and came within the collateral orders that were appealable under Pa. R. App. P. 313. The court noted that a significant possibility of trespass upon the individuals' First Amendment rights required review of that order.


OUTCOME: The supreme court vacated the superior court's order that quashed the individuals' appeal, and remanded the matter to that court for consideration of the constitutional question raised.

City of Philadelphia v. Commonwealth


Nos. 5-9 EAP 2003


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


575 Pa. 542; 838 A.2d 566; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 2050


May 14, 2003, Argued  
November 7, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered on 2/18/03 granting Petitioners' Motion for Preliminary Injunction at No. 45 M.D. 2003

.
City of Philadelphia v. Commonwealth, 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 977 (Pa. Commw. Ct., Feb. 19, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Declaratory relief granted. Act 230 declared unconstitutional. Mandate stayed for ninety days.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, the Commonwealth, the governor, and various legislators and agencies, sought review from an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which granted the motion of petitioners, a city and its mayor, in both his representative and individual capacities, for a preliminary injunction against the implementation of 2002 Pa. Laws 230 (Act 230) which, inter alia, reorganized the governance of the Pennsylvania Convention Center.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners filed a declaratory judgment action and sought injunctive relief as to Act 230, alleging that it would harm the region's economy and the city's reputation, their ability to bargain with its uniformed personnel, and their home-rule rights. The trial court determined that the legislation was passed in a manner that entitled petitioners to relief under Pa. Const. art. III, § 3, and a preliminary injunction was granted. On appeal, the court initially found that petitioners had standing as their interests were direct and sufficiently immediate, the enrolled bill doctrine did not preclude judicial review, and all of the necessary parties required by 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7540(a) were joined. The appellate court reviewed the history of Pa. Const. art. III, § 3 and the purposes of its requirements of a single-subject and clear expression. It found that Act 230 contained a myriad of subjects having little relationship to one another, which violated the single-subject rule. Although parts of Act 230 constituted a codification and compilation, which was excluded from the requirements of Pa. Const. art. III, § 3, there were substantive changes which went beyond the exemption.


OUTCOME: Petitioners were awarded declaratory relief directing that the statute under consideration was unconstitutional. The court stayed its mandate for a period of 90 days.

Commonwealth v. Mockaitis


No. 32 MAP 2001


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


575 Pa. 5; 834 A.2d 488; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 1908


November 14, 2001, Argued  
October 16, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County entered on February 12, 2001 at No. 001692. Trial Court Judge: Edgar B. Bayley, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Mockaitis, 54 Pa. D. & C.4th 115, 2001 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 398 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed the order of the Cumberland County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) granting limited post-sentence relief following defendant's drunk driving conviction. The trial court granted relief only to the extent that it vacated its original directive that ordered defendant to install an approved ignition interlock system on each of his motor vehicles as a condition precedent to restoration of his operating privileges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of his second drunk driving offense. As a result, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7002(b) required the trial court to order installation of interlock ignition systems on defendant's vehicles and to certify to the department of transportation that the systems had been installed. The supreme court found that the imposition of such responsibilities under 2000 Pa. Laws 63, codified at 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7001 et seq., violated the separation of powers provision of the Pennsylvania Constitution. The provisions in 2000 Pa. Laws 63 that delegated to the courts the executive responsibility of regulating whether and when repeat drunk driving offenders were entitled to conditional restoration of their operating privileges were more properly vested in the department of transportation, a part of the executive branch. The unconstitutional provisions, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 7002(b), 7003(1), (5), could be severed from the remainder of 2000 Pa. Laws 63. The remaining provisions still authorized the department to impose an ignition interlock restriction, and the Commonwealth had available to it ample means of enforcing that provision.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Mumia Abu-Jamal

US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Abu-Jamal v. Pennsylvania, 541 U.S. 1048, 124 S. Ct. 2173, 158 L. Ed. 2d 742, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 3504 (2004)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Commonwealth v. Abu-Jamal, 2008 Pa. LEXIS 98 (Pa., Feb. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order entered on 12/11/2001 denying PCRA relief at Nos. 1357-1259 Jan T 1982 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Philadelphia County. Trial Court Judge: Pamela Pryor Dembe, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Abu-Jamal, 553 Pa. 485, 720 A.2d 79, 1998 Pa. LEXIS 2364 (1998)



DISPOSITION: Order Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the order of the Philadelphia County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), denying his petition for relief pursuant to the Pennsylvania Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of the first-degree murder of a police officer and was sentenced to death. The inmate's judgment of sentence became final on June 10, 1991. The inmate filed the instant petition on July 3, 2001. The petition was not timely filed pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9545(b)(1), because it was not filed within a year of the date the judgment became final. The inmate asserted that he failed to raise the claim previously as a result of unconstitutional interference by governmental officials, which was an exception to the time bar pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9545(b)(1)(i). In asserting this claim, the inmate alleged that his Pennsylvania Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq., counsels failed to investigate the claim that a hit man admitted to killing the police officer. The inmate's argument that his PCRA counsels were agents of the Commonwealth due to their failure to investigate the claim failed, as the Commonwealth was not a beneficiary of poor defense lawyering. Furthermore, the inmate was just making a thinly veiled ineffective assistance of counsel claim, which could not circumvent the timeliness requirement.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Shaulis v. Pa. State Ethics Comm'n


44 MAP 2000


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


574 Pa. 680; 833 A.2d 123; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 1792


October 10, 2000, Submitted  
October 1, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of Commonwealth Court entered October 20, 1999 at No. 991CD99, reversing the decision of the State Ethics Commission. Intermediate Court Judges: Doyle, Joseph T., President Judge, Colins, James Gardner, Judge, McGinley, Bernard L., Judge, Pellegrini, Dan, Judge, Kelley, James R., Judge, Flaherty, Jim, Judge, Leadbetter, Bonnie B., Judge.
Shaulis v. Pennsylvania State Ethics Comm'n, 739 A.2d 1091, 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 824 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Pennsylvania State Ethics Commission sought review from an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which reversed the decision of the State Ethics Commission and held that § 1103(g) of the Public Official and Employee Ethics Act, 65 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1103(g), was unconstitutional as applied to appellee attorney because, inter alia, it violated Pa. Const. art. V, § 10(c).


OVERVIEW: The attorney worked for the Pennsylvania Department of Revenue. Just prior to her retirement, she requested advice from the Commission as to whether 65 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1103(g) barred her from publishing, during the first year of her retirement, articles or books about Pennsylvania state taxes. The Commission held that § 1103(g) was a valid regulation that did not violate the exclusive jurisdiction of the Supreme Court of Pennsylvania to regulate the conduct of attorneys. On appeal by the attorney, the Commonwealth Court held § 1103(g) unconstitutional as applied to the attorney. On further appeal, the court initially found that the decision of the Commission was a "final order" pursuant to 65 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1108, and accordingly it was appealable. Further, the attorney had standing to raise the issue, as she had a direct interest in the outcome. The court agreed that 65 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1103(g) was unconstitutional as applied to the attorney, in that it purported to regulate former employees and it was directed specifically at attorneys. Accordingly, it violated Pa. Const. art. V, § 10(c) as to the Supreme Court of Pennsylvania's exclusive jurisdiction over such conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Commonwealth v. Bavusa


48 EAP 2000


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


574 Pa. 620; 832 A.2d 1042; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 1766


October 29, 2002, Submitted  
September 29, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of the Superior Court entered 3/21/00 at No. 2527 PHL 1998 which affirmed judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division entered 5/13/98, at No. 9801-0815. Trial Court Judge: Barbara A. Joseph, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Michael T. Joyce, Judge, Patrick R. Tamilia, Judge and Zoran Popovich, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Bavusa, 2000 PA Super 85, 750 A.2d 855, 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 296 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the trial court's judgment, convicting appellant of violating §§ 6106, 6108 of the Uniform Firearms Act, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 6106(b), 6108. Appellant's challenge concerned only his conviction for violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6106(b).


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended that the amendments to 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6106 were additional elements and that because the Commonwealth failed to prove them, there was insufficient proof to support his conviction. However, the trial court held that the amendatory clauses were meant to be considered as statutory factors in determining the gradation of the offense, rather than as additional elements. The superior court affirmed the trial court's conviction and interpretation of the statute. On further appeal, the court found that the amendments to § 6106 were construed and intended as sentencing factors. Although appellant's constitutional arguments were not preserved, the court reviewed them in the context of statutory construction. The court found that the avoidance canon, in order to maintain the constitutionality of the legislation at issue, supported the construction of the additional clause as sentencing factors, and also, that they were not intended to be affirmative defenses. The court found that appellant's contemporaneous conviction under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6108 supported the felony grading of his conviction under 18 Pa. Const. Stat. § 6106(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Commonwealth v. Williams


No. 61 WAP 2001, No. 64 WAP 2001


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


574 Pa. 487; 832 A.2d 962; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 1746


April 8, 2002, Argued  
September 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Commonwealth v. Linton, 579 Pa. 181, 855 A.2d 761, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 1905 (2004)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Commonwealth v. Williams, 2005 PA Super 217, 877 A.2d 471, 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1469 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, Criminal Division, entered June 26, 2001 at No. 2416 of 2000. Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, Criminal Division, entered September 1, 2001 at No. 695 of 2001. Trial Court Judge: Shad F. Connelly, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two defendants were convicted of an offense triggering an adjudication of sexually violent predator status under Pennsylvania's Registration of Sexual Offenders Act (Megan's Law II), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9791-9799.7, and they filed motions for extraordinary relief. The Court of Common Pleas of Erie County (Pennsylvania), Criminal Division, found that portions of Megan's Law II were unconstitutional, and the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania appealed.


OVERVIEW: A trial court found two defendants guilty of sexually assaulting two minors in unrelated incidents. After defendants were convicted, they each filed a motion for extraordinary relief, arguing that the sexually violent predator provisions of Megan's Law II violated the United States and Pennsylvania Constitutions. The trial court declared the provisions unconstitutional, and the Commonwealth appealed. The state supreme court held that (1) the provisions of Megan's Law II which required sexually violent predators to register with state police, to notify state police when they moved, and to obtain counseling were nonpunitive, protected members of society, and were constitutional; (2) the provision of Megan's Law II which allowed authorities to provide information about persons who were determined to be sexually violent predators to people who requested that information was constitutional; but (3) the provision of Megan's Law II which allowed the Commonwealth to incarcerate a sexually violent predator who did not comply with the notification, registration, and counseling provisions was unconstitutional because it was manifestly in excess of what was needed to ensure compliance.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

Stackhouse v. Pa. State Police


No. 131 MAP 2001


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


574 Pa. 558; 832 A.2d 1004; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 1776


April 29, 2003, Argued  
September 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by, in part, Sub nomine at Stackhouse v. Commonwealth, 2006 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 60 (Pa. Commw. Ct., Feb. 8, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered on 8/27/01 at No. 430 MD 2001 dismissing the appeal.



DISPOSITION: Remanded to Court of Common Pleas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee appealed the order of the Pennsylvania Commonwealth Court dismissing the employee's action that was transferred from the common pleas court, which found that exclusive jurisdiction of the employee's tort action against appellees, the Pennsylvania State Police, the Pennsylvania State Police Commissioner, and the Pennsylvania State Police Deputy Commissioner, was in the Commonwealth Court.


OVERVIEW: The employee alleged that investigators, in an investigation undertaken by the state police as to the employee's job promotion application, were permitted to delve improperly into the employee's personal affairs. In counts two and three, the employee alleged defamation and invasion of privacy by the commissioner outside the scope of his authority. Count one of the complaint sought relief against the state police and against the commissioner and his deputy in their official capacities in the form of a declaratory judgment and an injunction. Counts two and three were trespass claims. The government formerly enjoyed immunity from such claims. The common pleas court, pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 761(a)(1)(v), generally had jurisdiction over such claims. The commonwealth court did not have ancillary jurisdiction over the case pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 761(c) on grounds that count one fell under commonwealth court jurisdiction. The count one claims for declaratory and injunctive relief premised upon the same events as counts two and three did not transform the complaint from one sounding in trespass into an action within the commonwealth court's original jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the common pleas court for proceedings consistent with the supreme court's opinion.

 

323 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Mayfield


No. 11 MAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


574 Pa. 460; 832 A.2d 418; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 1742


May 13, 2003, Argued  
September 24, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of Montgomery County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, entered 12-10-2001 at No. 1468-01. Trial Court Judge: Maurino J. Rossanese, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with three counts of institutional sexual assault, in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3124.2. She moved to quash the bills of information and have the charges dismissed. The Montgomery County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), granted the motion, finding that the statute was unconstitutional for lacking an express mens rea requirement. The Commonwealth appealed directly to the state supreme court.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issue was whether 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3124.2 was unconstitutional. Specifically, defendant argued that the terms "inmate" and "employee" were vague. The state supreme court concluded that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The statute's plain language revealed the legislature's intent to prohibit sexual contact between correctional staff and inmates. Defendant, as a corrections officer, was unquestionably an "employee" of a correctional facility. The persons with whom she allegedly had sexual contact were indisputably "inmates" at that facility. Defendant's alleged conduct was precisely what the legislature intended to proscribe when it enacted the statute. In addition, the statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad because it did not punish a substantial amount of constitutionally protected conduct. Rather, the statute regulated conduct that fell within the scope of otherwise valid criminal laws that reflected legitimate state interests. Finally, the statute was not unconstitutional for lacking an express mens rea requirement because applying 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 302(c) to require at least recklessness rendered the statute perfectly constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed, and the case was remanded for trial.

 

324 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Hall


No. 69 WAP 2001


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


574 Pa. 233; 830 A.2d 537; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 1437


March 6, 2002, Argued  
August 18, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court, entered January 9, 2001, at No. 2061WDA1999 affirming the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, entered April 22, 1997 at No100606180. Trial Court Judge: Raymond A. Novak, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Michael T. Joyce, Joan Orie Melvin and John P. Hester, JJ.
Commonwealth v. Hall, 776 A.2d 291, 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 707 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought and was granted reinstatement of his appeal rights nunc pro tunc via a petition he filed under the Pennsylvania Post-Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq., which resulted in the affirmance by the Pennsylvania Superior Court of defendant's conviction by the trial court of aggravated assault and recklessly endangering another person. Defendant was granted limited review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction. The state's highest court held that adequate circumstantial evidence proved that defendant intended to inflict serious bodily injury upon a police officer. The officer testified that defendant pointed a gun in his direction and fired two shots from a distance which increased the danger of serious bodily injury or death. Defendant fired the shots at the officer after realizing the officer had observed defendant firing his gun multiple times at another man. That defendant had no license for the gun, combined with a permissive inference instruction, provided the jury with further reason to reject defendant's accidental shooting claim. The instruction permitting an inference of criminal intent from defendant's failure to license the gun was within the Due Process Clause and Pa. Const. art. I, § 9. The jury could rationally draw an inference of criminal intent from the fact that the gun defendant fired was unlicensed. The fact that the gun was not lawfully purchased or licensed rationally supported an inference that it was intended to be used precisely as it was used, unlawfully against other people.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

Harrisburg Sch. Dist. v. Zogby


Nos. 1, 2, 7, 12 & 14 MAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


574 Pa. 121; 828 A.2d 1079; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 1254


April 8, 2003, Argued  
July 22, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court, entered January 3, 2002, at No. 550 M.D. 2000 789 A.2d 797 (Pa. Cmwlth. 2002). Trial Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, Commonwealth Court President Judge, Bernard L. McGinley, Commonwealth Court Judge, Doris A. Smith-Ribner, Commonwealth Court Judge, Dan Pelligrini, Commonwealth Court Judge, James R. Kelley, Commonwealth Court Senior Judge, Bonnie B. Leadbetter, Commonwealth Court Judge and Joseph Doyle, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: James Gardner, President Judge, Bernard L. McGinley, Judge, Dan Pellegrini, Judge, Bonnie B. Leadbetter, Judge, Joseph T. Doyle, Senior Judge and James R. Kelley, Senior Judge.
Harrisburg Sch. Dist. v. Zogby, 789 A.2d 797, 2002 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2002).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for entry of judgment in favor of Appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant public officials appealed from an order of the Pennsylvania Commonwealth Court granting judgment on the pleadings to plaintiffs, a local school district, parents, and others (the challengers), in an action seeking injunctive relief and a declaration that the Pennsylvania Education Empowerment Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 24, §§ 17-1701-B through 17-1716-B, was unconstitutional as applied to Harrisburg, Pennsylvania.


OVERVIEW: The Act allowed for Commonwealth takeovers of poorly performing school districts, but allowed greater local control of the effort in very large cities. In an effort to allow such a mayor-led effort in the state capital, a smaller city, the statute allowed, at Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 24, § 17-1701-B, for a pilot program in cities that had certain characteristics that only applied to the capital, although others could qualify if their school districts performed badly. The high court held that the provision did not violate anti-special legislation, equal protection guarantees of the United States or Pennsylvania Constitutions, because the provision rationally related to the goal of properly educating all children and other cities could become a member of the eligible class of cities as well. Pa. Const. art. IX, § III and Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, § 41412 protected cities against changes in their form of government, but giving a mayor additional responsibilities for schools was hardly the sort of radical change at which the constitutional and statutory provisions were directed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter for entry of judgment in favor of the public officials.

Commonwealth v. Belak


No. 91 WAP 2001, No. 92 WAP 2001


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


573 Pa. 414; 825 A.2d 1252; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 1010


September 9, 2002, Argued  
June 17, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Belak, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 1464 (Pa., Aug. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered December 5, 2000, at No1009WDA1999, vacating the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County, Criminal Division, entered June 4, 1999, at Nos. 3698, 3699 C 1998, and remanding. Trial Court Judges: McCormick, Jr., Richard E., Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Lally-Green, Maureen, Judge, Hester, John P., Judge, Kelly, John T., Judge.
Commonwealth v. Belak, 769 A.2d 1200, 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4937 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment of sentence reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth filed a petition for allowance of appeal of the order of the Pennsylvania Superior Court vacating defendant's judgment of sentence and remanding for resentencing. Defendant filed a cross-petition for allowance of appeal, claiming that the superior court erred in rejecting his claims of ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of burglary and other related offenses. Defendant was sentenced, pursuant to former 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9714 (1998), to the mandatory minimum of 25 years' imprisonment and the mandatory maximum of 50 years' imprisonment. The Pennsylvania Supreme Court previously found that former 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9714(a)(1) (1998) was unconstitutional. Defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claims were to be reviewed on collateral review rather than on direct appeal. The superior court erred in relying on the supreme court's previous finding that former 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9714(a)(1) was unconstitutional in reversing defendant's sentence, because defendant was sentenced under former 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9714(a)(2) (1998). The trial court's sentence of defendant to the mandatory minimum of 25 years in prison was only consistent with former § 9714(a)(2). Former 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9714(a)(2) was severable from former 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9714(a)(1), as former 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9714(a)(2) was independent of and separable from former 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9714(a)(1).


OUTCOME: The order was reversed insofar as it vacated defendant's judgment of sentence and remanded for resentencing. The judgment of sentence was reinstated. The order was vacated insofar as it rejected defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claims and those claims were dismissed without prejudice to defendant to raise those claims on collateral review.

Commonwealth v. Watkins


No. 334 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


577 Pa. 194; 843 A.2d 1203; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 969


September 9, 2002, Argued  
June 6, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 18, 2003. As Corrected April 5, 2004.
Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Watkins, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 729 (Pa., Mar. 23, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Watkins v. Pennsylvania, 543 U.S. 960, 125 S. Ct. 450, 160 L. Ed. 2d 324, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 7179 (2004)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Commonwealth v. Watkins, 2012 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 383 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Allegheny County entered on 12/13/96* at No. 9415480. See order, dated 2/28/01, directing written notice of judgment be transmitted since an appeal was never filed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Allegheny County, Pennsylvania, convicting defendant of three counts of first-degree murder and sentencing defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's ex-girlfriend was on the telephone with a friend when defendant arrived at the ex-girlfriend's home. The friend heard a struggle. Shortly thereafter, the dead bodies of the ex-girlfriend, her 18-day-old baby, and a nine-year-old boy were found in the house. The victims died of multiple gunshot wounds. Defendant was arrested in New York City. As defendant and the homicide detectives drove toward the trial court's jurisdiction, defendant raised the issue of the killings. The detective advised defendant of his Miranda rights. Defendant confessed to the three murders. At the hearing on defendant's motion to suppress the confession, defendant denied having spoken to the detective about the murders. Whether defendant confessed was an issue of credibility. Because there was competent proof that defendant made the statement, the trial court was not required to suppress the statement based solely on defendant's claim that he never made or signed it. The circumstances of the drive from New York City did not establish that the confession was coerced. The detective testified, and defendant confirmed, that no attempt was made to coerce defendant into confessing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Freeman


No. 234 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Direct Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Trial Division, Criminal Section, No. 886 October Term 1996. Trial Court Judges: Poserina, Jr., John J., Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence of the Philadelphia County Court of Common Pleas, Trial Division, Criminal Section (Pennsylvania), imposing a sentence of death upon defendant after convicting defendant of two counts of first-degree murder in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2502(a), and possession of an instrument of crime in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 907.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the female victim had previously been involved in a romantic relationship. The female and male victims became involved in a relationship. Defendant rented two cars. He requested his paycheck at his employer's main office. Defendant told his daughter that he was going to kill the male victim. In curtailing what had been an expansive relaxed waiver rule applied in capital cases, the supreme court held that, as a general rule on capital direct appeals, claims that were not properly raised and preserved in the trial court were waived and unreviewable. There was sufficient evidence to convict defendant of first-degree murder under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 2502(a). The evidence of defendant's preparations established premeditation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Bomar


No. 276 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


573 Pa. 426; 826 A.2d 831; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 920


October 16, 2001, Argued  
May 30, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended June 18, 2003.
Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Bomar, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 1238 (Pa., July 17, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bomar v. Pennsylvania, 540 U.S. 1115, 124 S. Ct. 1053, 157 L. Ed. 2d 906, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 190 (2004)
Subsequent appeal at Commonwealth v. Bomar, 880 A.2d 3, 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2588 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Direct Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Criminal Division, No. 5045-97. Trial Court Judges: Hazel, Frank T., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought direct appeal as of right of a judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), that sentenced him to death after a jury found him guilty of first-degree murder, rape, aggravated assault, kidnapping, and abuse of a corpse. Most of his claims related either to denial of his motion to suppress or to alleged ineffectiveness of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been convicted of murder and other violent offenses before he was charged with a brutal abduction, rape, murder, and abuse of the corpse of a young woman. He first argued that his statements to police were inadmissible, but the high court agreed that circumstances supported the determination that defendant had voluntarily waived his Miranda rights. Defendant's statements to another prisoner while he was incarcerated on another matter were not subject to a right to counsel. The limits the trial court placed on voir dire did not deprive defendant of his right to trial by jury. The victim's mother's testimony during the guilt phase related only to damage sustained by her car the night of the murder, not to the impact of the victim's death. The jury was entitled to know the underlying circumstances of defendant's past crimes. None of the claims of ineffective assistance of counsel survived the Strickland test, and there was no reason to conduct a post-trial mental examination of defendant. Since the former statute under which defendant received enhanced sentences for his non-murder crimes had been held unconstitutional, defendant would have to be resentenced on remand.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of sentence of death, but vacated the judgments of sentence for rape, kidnapping, and abuse of corpse, and remanded for resentencing on those offenses.

Commonwealth v. Morris


No. 289 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


573 Pa. 157; 822 A.2d 684; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 710


October 17, 2001, Argued  
May 1, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part, Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, in part, Stay granted by Morris v. Beard, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 44707 (E.D. Pa., June 20, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Emergency Application for Stay of Execution and Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Section, dated December 21, 1999 at Nos. 409-413, denying.
Commonwealth v. Morris, 565 Pa. 1, 771 A.2d 721, 2001 Pa. LEXIS 807 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Prior order granting stay of execution vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellant inmate's first-degree murder and robbery convictions, death sentence, and the denial of his first post-conviction relief petition were affirmed, he filed a second post-conviction relief petition in the Philadelphia County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal (Pennsylvania). The trial court denied his petition but granted a stay of execution, which the supreme court vacated. He then filed an emergency petition for stay of execution.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's stay of execution did not conform to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9545(c). The supreme court held it would respect the legislature's parameters in § 9545(c) when exercising its power to grant a stay of execution involving the inmate's second post-conviction relief petition. It was unnecessary to continue a stay of his execution to consider questions of the timeliness of his petition. It was inappropriate to adopt a "non-frivolous" standard whereby a stay of execution would be issued if an inmate filed a post-conviction petition that was not frivolous. To continue the stay of execution, the inmate had to meet the requirements of § 9545(c), showing his petition was timely and he had a strong likelihood of success on the merits. His petition was not timely, and the exception to the time requirement in § 9545(b)(ii) did not apply, as he argued prior counsel was ineffective, which was not a newly discovered "fact." He could not show his other claims of after-discovered evidence and governmental interference. As a result, the court had no jurisdiction to review his claim, and the stay of execution could not be continued.


OUTCOME: The stay of the inmate's execution was vacated and the denial of his second petition for post-conviction relief was affirmed.

Pentlong Corp. v. GLS Capital, Inc.


No. 85 WM 2001


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


573 Pa. 34; 820 A.2d 1240; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 383


November 15, 2001, Argued  
March 19, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended May 23, 2003.
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by, in part Pentlong Corp. v. GLS Capital, Inc., 2013 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 264 (Pa. Commw. Ct., July 15, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered July 5, 2001 at No2119CD2000, affirming in part, and reversing and remanding in part, the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, entered August 14, 2000 at NoGD98-5800. Trial Court Judge: Robert P. Horgos, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, President Judge, Doris A. Smith-Ribner, Dan Pellegrini, Rochelle S. Friedman, Bonnie B. Leadbetter, JJ., Joseph T. Doyle and James R. Kelley, Senior Judges.
Pentlong Corp. v. GLS Capital, Inc., 780 A.2d 734, 2001 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 447 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a county and a tax lien assignee, sought review from an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded in part an order of the common pleas court that dismissed a class action brought by appellee taxpayers in their action alleging unjust enrichment and fraudulent scheme by the assignee to assess, bill, and collect unauthorized amounts on the assigned tax liens.


OVERVIEW: The county assigned its title and rights to a large number of tax liens. The assignee required that delinquent taxpayers pay the tax amount as well as penalties, 12 percent interest, costs, and counsel fees. The common pleas court dismissed the complaint, holding that the taxpayers failed to exhaust their administrative remedies under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, §§ 7182, 7184. It also held that the county could assign the liens as well as the right to charge the additional amounts. On appeal, the commonwealth court found that exhaustion of remedies was not required and reversed the dismissal, and also held that the assignment was proper. However, it found that the maximum chargeable interest rate was 10 percent and there was no right to collect counsel fees. On further appeal, the court held that exhaustion of remedies was not required because this was not a routine challenge to the liens and equity was available. The court found that interest at 12 percent was collectible under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 5648, that there was no right to collect counsel fees under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, §§ 7106(a), 7187, and 7271, and that costs were collectible under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 53, § 7103.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the reversal of the dismissal of the complaint, reversed the finding that only 10 percent interest was collectible, affirmed the finding that counsel fees were not collectible, and remanded the matter for a further determination as to the amount of costs that were collectible.

Commonwealth v. Craven


18 WAP 2000, 19 WAP 2000


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


572 Pa. 431; 817 A.2d 451; 2003 Pa. LEXIS 246


March 4, 2002, Argued; March 4, 2002, Submitted  
March 4, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, entered on March 9, 2000 and March 30, 2000, at No. CC 9910766. Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, entered on March 9, 2000, at No. CC 9910764. Trial Court Judge: David R. Cashman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed the order of the Allegheny County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), granting the petition for habeas corpus filed by petitioner on the ground that 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5511(h.1)(6) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: When the police officers saw two bleeding pit bull dogs and equipment commonly used to train dogs for dogfighting, the officers seized a video camera and two videotapes. One videotape contained two recorded dogfights. Petitioner was clearly seen on the dogfight videotape standing above the fighting ring with his arms crossed, watching the fight. Based on petitioner's attendance at the dogfight, he was charged with violating 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5511(h.1)(6). In finding that § 5511(h.1)(6) was unconstitutional, the trial court found that it failed to place ordinary individuals on notice as to what conduct violated § 5511(h.1)(6). The trial court found that § 5511(h.1)(6) eliminated a mens rea requirement for culpability and imposed strict liability for mere presence at the fight. Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5511(h.1)(6) was neither unconstitutionally vague nor overbroad, as it did not impose strict liability on a person merely for being present at a dogfight. Rather, it criminalized a person's conscious decision to attend an illegal animal fight as a spectator, and by doing so, put individuals on sufficient notice as to what conduct was proscribed.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and remanded.

Winklespecht v. Pa. Bd. of Prob. & Parole


57 MM 2001


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


571 Pa. 685; 813 A.2d 688; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 3117


November 20, 2001, Submitted  
December 31, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus granted, Remanded by Winkelspecht v. Pa. Bd. of Prob. & Parole, 2003 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 27117 (M.D. Pa., Oct. 22, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Writ of Habeas Corpus.



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate petitioned the court for writ of habeas corpus and challenged defendant Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole's decision to deny him parole, and claimed this denial violated the ex post facto clause of the United States Constitution. U.S. Const. art. I, § 10.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was sentenced to 7-20 years imprisonment for rape and involuntary deviate sexual intercourse, and to a consecutive term of five years probation for aggravated assault. He was denied parole six years later. Although the inmate couched his underlying claim as an ex post facto violation, clearly his punishment was not increased by the changing of the statute under which his parole was determined, which was Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 61, § 331.1. The rewording of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 61, § 331.1 did not create a substantial risk that parole would be denied any more frequently than under the previous wording, nor did the addition of this language create a new offense or increase the penalty for an existing offense. Reordering of considerations for necessary decisions within an unchanged penalty did not rise to an ex post facto violation. Therefore, the inmate's claims did not raise an ex post facto issue. As the inmate failed to articulate a true constitutional claim, no relief was due, and the court left for another day the question of the propriety of habeas corpus as a remedy in the instant situation.


OUTCOME: The inmate's petition for writ of habeas corpus was denied.

 

334 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Scolieri


25 WAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


571 Pa. 658; 813 A.2d 672; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 3127


September 11, 2002, Argued  
December 31, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered December 28, 2001, at No. 45WDA2001, affirming the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, entered December 5, 2000, at No. CC200003931.
 Commonwealth v. Scolieri, 792 A.2d 1287, 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3652 (Pa. Super. Ct. 2001).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), convicted defendant of violating 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6310.1(a), which involved selling or furnishing liquor or malt or brewed beverages to minors. The Superior Court (Pennsylvania) affirmed the judgment of sentence. The state supreme court granted allocatur.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issue was whether 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6310.1(a) required the Commonwealth to prove that defendant knew that the purchaser was a minor. The state supreme court concluded that the superior court acted beyond its authority by permitting liability to attach where a defendant "should have known" that the purchaser was a minor because doing so improperly broadened the mens rea requirement of the statute. Because the Pennsylvania General Assembly had set forth the mens rea requirement of a knowing and intentional sale to a person who was a minor and no other contrary purpose of the mens rea requirement plainly appeared, the state supreme court held that conviction of the charged offense required proof that the sale to the minor was knowingly and intentionally undertaken. Because the trial court found that the Commonwealth failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant knew that the person to whom he was selling was less than 21 years of age, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6310.1(a) was not violated. The Commonwealth failed to prove the mens rea requirement of the statute.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was overturned and the order of the superior court was reversed.

Purple Orchid, Inc. v. Pa. State Police


No. 35 EAP 1999


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


572 Pa. 171; 813 A.2d 801; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 3135


October 18, 2000, Submitted  
December 31, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Rising Sun Entm't, Inc. v. Bureau of Liquor Control Enforcement, 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 517 (Pa. Commw. Ct., July 17, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court dated December 3, 1998 at No. 440 C.D. 1998, affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County dated December 31, 1997 at No. 9703-0440. 721 A.2d 84 (Pa. Cmwlth. 1998). Trial Court Judge: Stephen E. Levin, Senior Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Charles A. Lord, Senior Judge, Bernard L. McGinley and Dan Pellegrini, JJ.
Purple Orchid v. Pennsylvania State Police, Bureau of Liquor Control Enforcement, 721 A.2d 84, 1998 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 887 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cabaret owner was cited for violating Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 47, § 4-493(10) by employing topless dancers. An administrative law judge affirmed the citation, as did appellee liquor control board, the trial court, and the Pennsylvania commonwealth court. The owner appealed, arguing that § 4-493(10) violated his right to freedom of expression under the First Amendment.


OVERVIEW: After the owner's dancers removed their tops, leaving their breasts covered only by transparent liquid latex, the owner was cited for violating § 4-493(10)'s ban on "lewd entertainment," which had been interpreted by enforcement officials as requiring dancers to cover themselves, at a minimum, with pasties and a g-string. The supreme court found that § 4-493(10) was a content-neutral law aimed at minimizing the negative secondary effects of nude dancing, and thus was to be evaluated under the United States Supreme Court's four-prong O'Brien test. It found § 4-493(10) to be constitutional, as all four prongs of O'Brien were satisfied: (1) preventing negative secondary effects associated with nude dancing fell within the constitutional power of the government; (2) the law furthered the important government interest in preventing such negative secondary effects; (3) the government interest was unrelated to the suppression of free expression; and (4) the restriction on free expression was no greater than was essential, as § 4-493(10) did not bar nude dancing outright, and even in licensed liquor establishments, the dancers remained free to perform wearing pasties and g-strings.


OUTCOME: The decision of the commonwealth court was affirmed.
