Commonwealth v. Johnson


361 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


572 Pa. 283; 815 A.2d 563; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 3006


July 22, 2002, Submitted  
December 27, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Johnson, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 208 (Pa., Feb. 21, 2003)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Commonwealth v. Johnson, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 3118 (Pa., Dec. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered October 25, 2001 in the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Criminal Division, dismissing PCRA relief at No. 118-97. Trial Court Judge: Scott D. Keller, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Johnson, 556 Pa. 216, 727 A.2d 1089, 1999 Pa. LEXIS 862 (1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's first-degree murder conviction and death sentence were affirmed on direct appeal, he petitioned the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), for relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq. The trial court dismissed his petition, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered two people. The supreme court held that race-neutral driver's license lists, used as a jury pool basis, did not deny defendant an impartial jury. Counsel did not have to try to rehabilitate jurors who could not impose the death penalty, acted reasonably in conceding defendant's presence at the crime scene, and did not err by not raising diminished capacity, as defendant would not make a required criminal liability admission. After defendant killed one victim, he was not entitled to a 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9711(e)(1) mitigation instruction that he had no criminal history, despite such a stipulation, which did not extend to both murders. An instruction that defendant, as a murder accomplice, could not be sentenced to death absent proof of intent to take life or contemplation that life would be taken, was unnecessary as his intent to kill, supporting first-degree murder, had been found. The aggravating circumstance of 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9711(d)(14), regarding drug activity, was not void for vagueness as it adequately told the jury what it had to find. The circumstance was not overbroad, as it genuinely narrowed those eligible for the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Tiger Schulmann's Karate Ctrs.


No. 57 MAP 2001


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


571 Pa. 413; 812 A.2d 614; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 2757


April 8, 2002, Argued  
December 19, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered April 6, 2001 at No. 5 MD 1997. 771 A.2d 107 (Pa. Cmwlth. 2001). Trial Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, Commonwealth Court President Judge, Rochelle S. Friedman, Commonwealth Court Judge and Joseph F. McCloskey, Commonwealth Court Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed an order by the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee karate centers, claiming that the trial court erred in analyzing what the "primary purpose" of the centers' business was.


OVERVIEW: The Commonwealth alleged that the centers were operating health clubs in violation of the Health Club Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 73, § 2161 et seq. (1989). The state supreme court held that although the centers included the word "fitness" in their trade name and their advertisements at times stressed the physical fitness benefits of their program, the record lacked evidence of any fitness program offered by the centers other than martial arts/karate instruction. Because the primary purpose of their business was martial arts/karate instruction for self-defense, self-discipline, and self-confidence, with an only accompanying benefit of physical fitness, the business was not a "health club" pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 73, § 2162. Therefore, the trial court did not err in granting summary judgment to the centers.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Pap's A.M. v. City of Erie


Nos. 16 & 17 WAP 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


571 Pa. 375; 812 A.2d 591; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 2806


August 30, 2000, Submitted  
December 19, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered on March 27, 1996, at Nos. 445CD1995 and 446CD1995, reversing the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County entered on January 18, 1995, at No. 1994-60059. Order reversed on October 21, 1998, Pap's A.M. v. City of Erie, 553 Pa. 348, 719 A.2d 273 (1998) Remand from the United States Supreme Court entered on March 29, 2000, at No. 981161,City of Erie v. Pap's A.M., 529 U.S. 277, 146 L. Ed. 2d 265, 120 S. Ct. 1382 (2000). Trial Court Judge: Shad F. Connelly, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Doris A. Smith-Ribner, Judge, Joseph T. Doyle, Senior Judge and Charles P. Mirarchi Jr., Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Prior order reinstated on state grounds. Commonwealth Court order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant business operated an establishment with nude dancing. Appellee city and the City Council of Erie, Pennsylvania enacted a public indecency ordinance that made it a summary offense to appear in public in a state of nudity. The trial court's order, regarding the ordinance's constitutionality, was reversed by order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania). The case was remanded following reversal by the United States Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: The highest state court found that it was left with a circumstance where it had to decide a Pennsylvania constitutional question where the federal law was fluid and changing and not entirely clear. In doing so, the court found that Pa. Const. art. I, § 7, provided greater protection for speech and conduct than did U.S. Const. amend. I. It approached the ordinance at issue in the instant case in a common sense fashion. An obvious purpose of the ordinance was to directly burden the freedom of expression itself, i.e., the erotic message of the dance. The highest state court detected a content-based motivation to suppress the expressive nature of the dance. As such, the court found that an intermediate level of scrutiny was inappropriate. Although the expression at issue was not political speech, the court was nevertheless satisfied that it was communication within the contemplation of Pa. Const. art. I, § 7. While curbing crimes such as prostitution and rape was a compelling government interest, the ordinance was not narrowly tailored to meet this compelling interest. The goals could be achieved by less restrictive means, without burdening the guaranteed right to expression.


OUTCOME: The highest court found that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The order of the lower appellate court was reversed, and a portion of the ordinance was severed.

 

339 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Mouzon


No. 43 EAP 2001


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


571 Pa. 419; 812 A.2d 617; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 2758


April 9, 2002, Argued  
December 19, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Decision reached on appeal by Commonwealth v. Mouzon, 2003 PA Super 249, 828 A.2d 1126, 2003 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1870 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered May 23, 2001 at No. 2301 EDA 1999, affirming the Judgment of Sentence entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County entered June 23, 1999 at Nos. 9804-0203 1/2, 9804-0413 1/1 and 9804-0915 2/2. Trial Court Judge: Ricardo C. Jackson, Senior Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Correale F. Stevens, Maureen Lally-Green, and Phyllis W. Beck, JJ.
Commonwealth v. Mouzon, 778 A.2d 1245, 2001 Pa. Super. LEXIS 899 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the Pennsylvania Superior Court's affirmance of a sentence imposed by a trial court upon his conviction of eight counts of robbery, eight counts of possessing an instrument of crime, and seven counts of conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his sentence imposed upon his conviction of eight counts of robbery, eight counts of possession of an instrument of crime, and seven counts of conspiracy. Although the sentence was within the statutory legal limits, but beyond the aggravated range of the sentencing guidelines, defendant asserted that the sentence was excessive. The intermediate appellate court rejected defendant's challenge for failure to raise a substantial question of law, since his sentence was within the statutory limits. The high court rejected the Commonwealth's assertion that defendant failed to raise his issue before the trial court. The court held that defendant could not challenge the trial court's dismissal for failure to raise a substantial question of law until it actually dismissed his challenge. That court found that 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9781 did not give a court the discretion to exclude an entire class of sentence challenges from the opportunity for appellate review on their merits, and held that the intermediate court's dismissal did not constitute an appellate review on the merits, and that defendant was entitled to bring an excessiveness challenge against his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the intermediate court's judgment and remanded the matter to that court for further consistent proceedings.

 

340 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Marshall


No. 226 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


571 Pa. 289; 812 A.2d 539; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 2729


November 9, 1999, Submitted  
December 18, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part Marshall v. Beard, 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 17507 (E.D. Pa., Aug. 26, 2004)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Commonwealth v. Marshall, 2008 Pa. LEXIS 706 (Pa., May 20, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Glazer, J.), dated March 13, 1998, denying Appellant relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act. Judges: C.C.P. - Hon. Gary S. Glazer.
Commonwealth v. Marshall, 537 Pa. 336, 643 A.2d 1070, 1994 Pa. LEXIS 160 (1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his petition for relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act (Act), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq., without a hearing. The areas of law were the timeliness of the petition, whether petitioner waived issues by failing to raise them earlier, whether his claims were previously litigated, and whether his prior counsel were ineffective.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, who had been sentenced to death for two murder convictions, raised more than 20 claims for relief. On appeal, the court held that the petition was filed in a timely manner, because it was filed within one year of the effective date of the 1995 amendments to the Act, which incorporated the timeliness requirements into 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9545 of the Act. However, pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9544(b), 15 of petitioner's claims had been waived by his failure to raise the issues before trial, at trial, on direct appeal, or in a prior state postconviction proceeding. Pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9543(a)(3), he had the burden of proving by a preponderance of the evidence that his allegations of error had not been waived. Likewise, pursuant to § 9543(a)(3), the court refused to consider an ineffectiveness of counsel claim that had been previously litigated. Another such claim failed on the merits, because petitioner failed to establish that his prior counsel had no reasonable basis for failing to investigate and present mental health mitigation at petitioner's penalty phase hearings. None of petitioner's other claims of ineffectiveness of counsel had merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying petitioner relief under the Act.

 

341 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Wharton


No. 170 Capital Appeal Docket.


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


571 Pa. 85; 811 A.2d 978; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 2426


March 2, 1999, Submitted  
November 25, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 3, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County entered June 23, 1997 at Information Nos. 2258-1/2 February Term, 1984. & 04021/1 May Term 1984 & 2643-1/1 May Term 1984.
Commonwealth v. Wharton, 542 Pa. 83, 665 A.2d 458, 1995 Pa. LEXIS 969 (1995)



DISPOSITION: We affirm the order of the PCRA court. The Prothonotary of the Supreme Court is directed to transmit the complete record in this case to the Governor in accordance with 42 Pa.C.S. § 9711(i).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's convictions of first-degree murder, robbery, and criminal conspiracy and his death sentence were affirmed, he petitioned the Philadelphia County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) for relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq. His petition was dismissed without a hearing, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted ineffective assistance of counsel. The supreme court held, to the extent he raised constitutional ineffectiveness claims, they were not waived under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9543(a)(2)(ii), as this was his first chance to raise them and some degree of latitude was afforded in capital appeals. Defendant did not show counsel was ineffective for not introducing equivocal evidence of his adjustment to prison between his two sentencing hearings, as he did not show counsel had no reasonably objective basis for not introducing the evidence. His claim that the prosecutor's peremptory challenges were racially discriminatory was waived, as it was not raised at trial, on direct appeal, or before the post-conviction relief court and was first raised in a reply brief. Failing to present testimony of a co-defendant claiming to be the actual killer, contrary to a prior statement, was not ineffective assistance, as it was not shown counsel knew of the testimony or that it was objectively unreasonable not to present the testimony. A catch-all ineffectiveness claim for not raising claims of trial court or prosecutorial error was insufficient.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

342 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Marinelli


No. 340 CAP


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


570 Pa. 622; 810 A.2d 1257; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 2425


April 15, 2002, Submitted  
November 25, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Commonwealth ex rel. Marinelli v. Beard, 571 Pa. 489, 812 A.2d 1164, 2002 Pa. LEXIS 2414 (2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Commonwealth v. Marinelli, 589 Pa. 682, 910 A.2d 672, 2006 Pa. LEXIS 2279 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered on 5/15/2001 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Northumberland County at No. CR 94-451 denying PCRA relief. Trial Court Judge: William Harvey Wiest, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Marinelli, 547 Pa. 294, 690 A.2d 203, 1997 Pa. LEXIS 441 (1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's first degree murder, robbery, conspiracy to commit robbery, burglary, theft by unlawful taking, receiving stolen property, and aggravated assault convictions and death sentence were affirmed, he petitioned the Northumberland County Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), for post-conviction relief under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq. The trial court denied his petition, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not decide claims not stated in a second post-conviction relief petition. The supreme court held the claims were in a first petition and incorporated into the second petition, and had to be heard, except those earlier litigated. Defendant did not show counsel had no basis not to object to a forensic pathologist's bullet trajectory testimony, nor was counsel ineffective in not calling an expert on this, and the expert was properly cross-examined. Defendant did not show the prosecutor suppressed a co-defendant's "deal" with the prosecution. No mitigating evidence on defendant's childhood was suppressed, and there was no evidence the prosecutor elicited a co-defendant's perjury. A co-defendant's intoxication did not have to be revealed. Defendant's lack of cooperation with discovery of mitigation evidence about his childhood precluded his claiming ineffective assistance on this basis. Lack of evidence of his psychological problems was not ineffective assistance as a defense psychologist found none. Alcohol did not overpower him, so the lack of an intoxication mitigating circumstance was not ineffective, and he prevented discovery of his substance abuse problem.


OUTCOME: The trial court's dismissal of two claims and denial of relief on three claims were affirmed, but the summary dismissal of eight claims was reversed, and the matter was remanded for hearing.

 

343 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Marshall


No. 216 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


570 Pa. 545; 810 A.2d 1211; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 2400


April 5, 1999, Submitted  
November 22, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Marshall v. Pennsylvania, 540 U.S. 833, 124 S. Ct. 81, 157 L. Ed. 2d 61, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 6201 (2003)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part Marshall v. Beard, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 35154 (E.D. Pa., Apr. 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Philadelphia County Court of Common Pleas, dated December 29, 1997, denying relief under the Post-Conviction Relief Act. Trial Court Judge: Albert F. Sabo, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Marshall, 534 Pa. 488, 633 A.2d 1100, 1993 Pa. LEXIS 242 (1993)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from an order of the Philadelphia County Common Pleas Court (Pennsylvania) dismissing his petition for relief under the Pennsylvania Post-Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq., from a sentence of death, imposed after his conviction of murdering his wife and daughter. He argued that relief was appropriate because of his counsel's ineffectiveness.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of murdering his wife and one of his daughters while he was taking family grocery money to buy drugs. The jury found two aggravating circumstances and no mitigators, and he was sentenced to death. The high court upheld the sentence on his direct appeal, and in the instant opinion, upheld the sentence against his post-conviction relief petition. The direct review had already established that petitioner had not been prejudiced by any alleged race discrimination or any other impropriety in jury selection, and there had been no showing that the Commonwealth had suppressed evidence that would have helped petitioner. He had an ample opportunity to present his arguments that he was impaired by drug use and brain injury at the time of the crimes. The jury instructions were accurate statements of the law. Although a few prosecutorial comments were unduly inflammatory, the trial court took care to adequately cure any effect they might have had on the jury. Since petitioner could not show that the trial court committed prejudicial error, counsel was not ineffective in failing to object to the trial court's rulings, and no evidentiary hearing was required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying post-conviction relief.

Commonwealth v. Harris


No. 271 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


572 Pa. 489; 817 A.2d 1033; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 2395


May 2, 2000, Argued  
November 20, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Harris, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 412 (Pa., Mar. 20, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Harris v. Pennsylvania, 540 U.S. 1081, 124 S. Ct. 939, 157 L. Ed. 2d 756, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 9115 (2003)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part Harris v. Beard, 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 25440 (E.D. Pa., Dec. 15, 2004)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Commonwealth v. Harris, 612 Pa. 576, 32 A.3d 243, 2011 Pa. LEXIS 2966 (2011)
Related proceeding at In re Commonwealth's Motion, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 119950 (E.D. Pa., Aug. 22, 2013)
Related proceeding at Harris v. Steadman, 160 F. Supp. 3d 814, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 17392 (E.D. Pa., 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of Death Imposed by the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County dated March 17, 1999, at No. 672 C.A. 1997. Trial Court Judge: Paul K. Allison, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), which imposed a sentence of death upon his conviction of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: The victim was a prosecution witness to aggravated assault committed by defendant. There was sufficient evidence to support the murder conviction where it was shown that defendant intended to kill the victim in order to prohibit his testimony, and in furtherance thereof he slashed the victim's tires, waited for the victim, slashed his throat, and concocted an elaborate alibi. The court found that the prosecution's peremptory challenge against a particular juror was race-neutral, in that she had equivocated on the death penalty. There was no error in admitting photocopies of letters that defendant mailed to his girlfriend. Those which were turned over to the police by the girlfriend's brother were not protected under U.S. Const. amend. IV or Pa. Const. art. I, § 8 because there was no state action; others were not protected by the attorney-client privilege because they were between non-lawyers. The court found evidence to support the sentence of death, finding that defense victim impact testimony was irrelevant where there was only an aggravating circumstance, and that 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9711(c)(2) was constitutional. Other objections to the penalty phase lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence.

Commonwealth v. Ford


No. 248 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


570 Pa. 378; 809 A.2d 325; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 2224


August 17, 2000, Submitted  
October 25, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Ford v. Pennsylvania, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 700 (U.S., Jan. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered on February 12, 1991 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Trial Division at Nos. 3222 to 3231.

Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered on February 12, 1991, in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Trial Division at Nos. 3222 to 3231.

Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County entered on October 30, 1998 at Nos. 3222 to 3231, October term, 1989. Trial Court Judge: Jane Cutler Greenspan, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Ford, 539 Pa. 85, 650 A.2d 433, 1994 Pa. LEXIS 637 (1994)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted appellant of, inter alia, two counts of murder and two counts of burglary. Appellant was sentenced to death. The conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. Appellant then filed several petitions for post conviction relief and for habeas corpus relief against the State. The Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Trial Division (Pennsylvania), denied the petitions. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant raised several claims which had been previously litigated or were otherwise waived for purposes of the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq. The appellate court ruled that to be eligible for relief under the PCRA, a petitioner needed to establish that his allegations had not been previously litigated or waived. However, appellant did raise two claims of ineffective assistance of counsel that were properly developed and were reviewable. The appellate court found that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to investigate and present sufficient evidence of mitigation at the penalty phase, including evidence of appellant's history of abuse and his mental illness and dysfunction, and that appellate counsel was ineffective for failing to raise trial counsel's ineffectiveness in this regard. During the penalty phase, trial counsel presented virtually no evidence of mitigating circumstances. There were several areas of mitigation, including appellant's hospitalizations, life history, and mental health. There was a reasonable probability that the outcome of the penalty deliberations would have been different if these issues were presented.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

Unisys Corp. v. Commonwealth


No. 73 MAP 1999, No. 74 MAP 1999, No. 75 MAP 1999, No. 76 MAPP 1999, No. 77 MAP 1999, 78 MAP 1999


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


571 Pa. 139; 812 A.2d 448; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 2226



October 25, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Filed November 7, 2002. Petition for Reconsideration/Reargument Denied January 2, 2003.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by UNISYS CORP. v. PA BD. OF FINANCE & REVENUE, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 5513 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered on 3/8/99 at 151 F.R. 1991 reversing the Order dated 3/29/91 and remanding to the Department of Finance and Revenue; Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered on 3/8/99 at 201 F.R. 1993 reversing the Order dated 3/29/91 and remanding to the Department of Finance and Revenue; Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered on 3/8/99 at 202 F.R. 1993 reversing the Order dated 3/29/91 and remanding to the Department of Finance and Revenue; Re-submitted August 22, 2002. Intermediate Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, President Judge, Doris A. Smith-Ribner, Judge, Dan Pellegrini, Judge, Rochelle S. Friedman, Judge, Bonnie B. Leadbetter, Judge, Joseph T. Doyle, Senior Judge and Jim Flaherty, Senior Judge.
Unisys Corp. v. Commonwealth, 726 A.2d 1096, 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 154 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for reinstatement of settlements as approved by Board.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer, a Delaware corporation, filed resettlement petitions challenging the Pennsylvania Department of Revenue's settlements of the taxpayer's franchise tax for certain tax years. The Department denied the petitions as did respondent Pennsylvania Board of Finance & Revenue. The Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) found no constitutional violation but found that the taxpayer was entitled to statutory relief. Both sides appealed.


OVERVIEW: Taxpayer's principal offices were in Pennsylvania and it conducted business throughout the United States. Pursuant to, inter alia, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, §§ 7601, 7602, of the Pennsylvania Tax Reform Act of 1971, 1971 Pa. Laws 6, as amended, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, §§ 7101- 10004, Pennsylvania imposed a franchise tax on out-of-state corporations to reach value from in-state business activity. Relying on constitutional fairness principles of the Commerce Clause and the Due Process Clause, taxpayer attacked the absence of factor representation in single-entity, franchise value apportionment, which related to value generated by its subsidiaries, arguing that the Department's methodology led to an overstatement of the value from its Pennsylvania business activity by about 45 percent. Although the trial court accepted taxpayer's figures in finding that it had a right to relief under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 7401(3)(2)(a)(18), the supreme court found that the taxpayer failed to show the appropriateness of its baseline figures, and thus failed to prove constitutional unfairness in the apportionment scheme applied by the Department or a right to relief under § 7401(3)(2)(a)(18).


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the trial court's order and remanded the cases to the trial court for reinstatement of the settlements as approved by the Board.

 

347 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Eller


50 WAP 2000


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


569 Pa. 622; 807 A.2d 838; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 1997


September 11, 2001, Argued  
September 25, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered September 1, 1999, at No. 1648PGH98, affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County entered August 24, 1998, at No. 2824 of 1995. 747 A.2d 411 (Table) (Pa. Super. 1999). Trial Court Judge: William R. Cunningham, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Berle M. Schiller, Judge, J. Michael Eakin, Judge, and John G. Brosky, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the order of the Pennsylvania Superior Court that affirmed the trial court order denying defendant's pro se motion for the reinstatement of defendant's direct appellate rights nunc pro tunc.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to rape. The sentence became final 30 days after its imposition on July 11, 1997. In August 1998, defendant filed pro se motions to appeal nunc pro tunc in the superior court and the trial court. The motions were denied. On appeal of the trial court's denial, defendant argued that he was entitled to reinstatement of his direct appellate rights nunc pro tunc, because his plea lawyer allegedly refused to file a direct appeal. In denying relief, the superior court found that defendant failed to file a timely Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. 9541 et seq. The superior court relied on a supreme court decision that was filed in 1999 to find that the PCRA was the exclusive remedy for post-conviction claims seeking restoration of appellate rights after counsel's failure to perfect a direct appeal. On appeal to the supreme court, defendant claimed that this retroactive application of the supreme court case was improper. The supreme court found that there was no retroactive application of that case, because 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9542 and supreme court cases consistently, repeatedly, and unequivocally recognized the exclusivity of the PCRA.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

348 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Gmerek v. State Ethics Comm'n


NOS. 55, 56 & 57 MAP 2000


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


569 Pa. 579; 807 A.2d 812; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 1752


April 30, 2001, Argued  
August 23, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL OF: HONORABLE MIKE FISHER, ATTORNEY GENERAL at 55 MAP 2000. APPEAL OF: STATE ETHICS COMMISSION at 56 MAP 2000. APPEAL OF: MARK R. CORRIGAN, SECRETARY OF THE SENATE OF PENNSYLVANIA, INTERVENOR at 57 MAP 2000. Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered May 18, 2000 at No. 323 MD 1999, denying the motion for summary judgment 751 A.2d 1241 (Pa. Cmwlth. 2000). Trial Court Judges: James Gardner Colins, Commonwealth Court President Judge, Bernard L. McGinley, Doris A. Smith, James R. Kelley, Jim Flaherty, Bonnie B. Leadbetter, Commonwealth Court Judges, Joseph Doyle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed by evenly divided court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee attorneys sought a declaratory judgment in the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) finding the Lobbying Disclosure Act, 65 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1303- 1311 unconstitutional. The trial court granted the attorneys' summary judgment motion, and appellees, ethics commission and attorney general, as well as intervenor senate secretary, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The attorneys represented clients regarding proposed legislation. The supreme court was evenly divided. Two justices in favor of affirming the trial court's opinion found the Lobbying Disclosure Act (the Act), 65 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1303- 1311, regulated the attorneys' conduct while servicing clients in the realm of lobbying. The proper analysis was whether the Act controlled the conduct of attorneys when engaged in the rendering of legal services to clients. The Act's broad definition of lobbying, including direct and indirect communication to state officials, included the practice of law. The attorneys provided legal analysis of proposed legislation to clients which was communicated to state officials, they appeared before executive departments during the legislative process, and they discussed the applicability of regulations. These activities were communication to which the Act applied, infringing on the supreme court's exclusive jurisdiction to regulate attorneys. 65 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1311(b) provided if any provision of the Act was held invalid based on the improper regulation of the practice of law, its remaining provisions were void.


OUTCOME: As a result of the Pennsylvania Supreme Court being evenly divided, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

349 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Bond


No. 212 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


572 Pa. 588; 819 A.2d 33; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 1753


July 15, 1999, Submitted  
August 23, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reconsideration Denied October 17, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Pa. LEXIS 2184.
Reconsideration denied by Commonwealth v. Bond, 2002 Pa. LEXIS 2184 (Pa., Oct. 17, 2002)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Bond v. Beard, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 28143 (E.D. Pa., Nov. 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order entered on 12/10/97 in the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, at Nos. 1778-1/4, 1783, 1785, and 1787 January term, 1992. Trial Court Judge: David N. Savitt, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Bond, 539 Pa. 299, 652 A.2d 308, 1995 Pa. LEXIS 7 (1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; motion for remand denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from an order of the Philadelphia County Common Pleas Court, Philadelphia County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), denying his petition for relief from a judgment sentencing him to death after his conviction of murder, under the Pennsylvania Post-Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of murdering a store manager in a hold-up. After an unsuccessful appeal, he raised many of the same issues in a post-conviction relief petition, but most of them were procedurally barred because they were or should have been decided in his earlier appeal. The high court proceeded to consider his remaining claims, which related generally to ineffective assistance of counsel (the same counsel that continued to represent him, or their colleagues), particularly in failing to investigate and produce more evidence in mitigation at the penalty phase, failure to seek more actively the admission of a prosecution witness's recantation, failure to argue more strenuously for a particular mercy instruction, and failure to pursue with greater energy various claims of racial prejudice. The court held that all these claims were meritless. Counsel was not ineffective in failing to investigate mitigating circumstances that the record did not support, in failing to pursue the admission of evidence that was not in fact exculpatory, in failing to seek a jury instruction that did not state the law, or in failing to make pointless claims of racial prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

350 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


In re Adoption of R.B.F.


No. 59 WAP 2001, No. 60 WAP 2001


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


569 Pa. 269; 803 A.2d 1195; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 1710


March 25, 2002, Submitted  
August 20, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 26, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court, entered November 8, 2000, at No. 67MDA1999, affirming the Order of the Lancaster County Common Pleas Court, Orphans' Court, entered October 22, 1998, at No. 101 1/2 of 1998. 2000 PA Super 337, 762 A.2d 739 (Pa. Super. 2000). Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court, entered November 8, 2000, at No. 1192WDA1999, affirming the Order of the Erie County Common Pleas Court, Orphans' Court Division entered June 18, 1999, at No. 42 in Adoption 1999. 2000 PA Super 338, 762 A.2d 724 (Pa. Super. 2000). Trial Court Judge: Cullen, James P., Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Johnson, Justin M., Judge, Hudock, Joseph A., Judge, Ford Elliott, Kate, Judge, Eakin, J. Michael, Judge, Stevens, Correale F., Judge, Todd, Debra, Judge, Kelly, John T., Judge, Popovich, Zoran, Judge, Cavanaugh, James R., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Orders vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, two pairs of appellants, legal parents and their same-sex partners, challenged affirmances by two different Pennsylvania Superior Courts of trial court orders denying in each case petitions by which the parents and partners sought the adoption of the parents' children by the partners, without the parents' relinquishment of their own rights.


OVERVIEW: In companion cases, two same-sex couples who were already raising children together sought to have the children adopted by the partner of the legal parent. In compliance with Pennsylvania statutes, the petitions contained consents to adoption by the legal parents, but omitted language mandated by 23 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2711(d)(1) by which the legal parent was also required to relinquish his or her own parental rights. The high court agreed with the lower courts that the plain language of the statutory provisions allowing parents whose spouses were adopting their children to retain their parental rights applied only to step-parent adoptions. It also agreed, however, with the legal parents and partners that 23 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2901 gave courts discretion, upon a showing of good cause, to permit adoptions in the best interests of the children where not all the statutory conditions had been met. Since the parents and partners had never had an opportunity to try to show good cause why termination of rights should not be required, the high court directed the trial courts to hold evidentiary hearings.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the orders and remanded the cases to their respective trial courts for evidentiary hearings.

Bold Corp. v. County of Lancaster


No 49 MAP 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


569 Pa. 107; 801 A.2d 469; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 1439


May 28, 2002, Submitted  
July 16, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Bold Corp. v. County of Lancaster, 809 A.2d 1096, 2002 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 882 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered January 23, 2002, at No. 1227 C.D. 2001, 790 A.2d 1099, vacating the Orders of the Lancaster County Common Pleas Court entered February 2, 2001 and April 23, 2001 at No. CI-00-02944. (Pa. Cmwlth. 2002). Trial Court Judge: Farina, Louis J., Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Colins, James Gardner, President Judge, Smith-Ribner, Doris A., Judge, Pellegrini, Dan R., Judge, Friedman, Rochelle S., Judge, Leadbetter, Bonnie B., Judge, Doyle, Joseph T., Senior Judge, Kelley, James R., Senior Judge.
Bold Corp. v. County of Lancaster, 790 A.2d 1099, 2002 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 24 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city and county authority, sought review of the Pennsylvania Commonwealth Court order vacating the trial court orders that found that appellee hotels failed to prove that the burdens of the hotel tax disproportionately outweighed the benefits. The appellate court found that the trial court had not conducted a proper benefit and burden analysis.


OVERVIEW: The city and county created the county authority. The county enacted a hotel room rental tax. Most of the rental tax revenues were to be used to build a convention center. The rest were to promote county tourism. The proposed convention center project included the development of a hotel next to the convention center that was to be financially independent from the center. The hotels claimed that the rental tax violated their due process and equal protection rights. The appellate court improperly found that the trial court did not properly weigh the burdens imposed by the tax against its benefits. The trial court properly considered the impact of the convention center hotel to the extent that the new hotel would absorb a portion of the new hotel business that would have been generated by the convention center. Although the new hotel was to benefit from the convention center, so were the remaining hotels in the county. Furthermore, the hotels, as challengers of the constitutionality of the tax, were required to establish its unconstitutionality. Nevertheless, they presented no evidence about how much money they would lose to the convention center hotel each year.


OUTCOME: The order was vacated, and the matter was remanded.

Pa. Sch. Bds. Ass'n v. Commonwealth Ass'n of Sch. Adm'rs., Teamsters Local 502


No. 34 EAP 1999


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


569 Pa. 436; 805 A.2d 476; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 1440; 9 A.L.R.6th 727; 170 L.R.R.M. 3124


October 16, 2000, Argued  
July 16, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division, entered June 15, 1999, at No. 1297 October Term, 1997. Trial Court Judges: O'Keefe, Joseph D., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, school district and others (collectively, "district"), instituted an action against defendants, school administration union and others (collectively, "union"), seeking declaratory relief that Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 71, § 371 was unconstitutional. The Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) entered an order granting the declaratory relief. The union appealed. Political representatives were granted leave to intervene.


OVERVIEW: The challenged statute included a portion that granted school administrators employed by a city of the first class the right to bargain collectively with their public employers. The school district argued, and the trial court found, that it violated Pa. Const. art. III, § 31, which prohibited the delegation of certain legislative powers. In rejecting this argument, the appellate court found that the statute could be interpreted in a manner that delegated purely administrative decision making. The district also argued that the final statute was not considered on three different days in each house, as required under Pa. Const. art. III, § 31. After determining that the political question doctrine, the Speech or Debate Clause, and the enrolled bill doctrine did not prohibit it from reviewing the challenge, the appellate court found that the statute was enacted in compliance with the Pennsylvania Constitution. Both the initial draft of the bill, as well as the subsequent amendments, related to the same subject. Legislation could be materially changed, without wholly changing its purpose. Policy considerations were non-justiciable, and the statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: All claims of constitutional infirmity were rejected, and the order of the trial court was reversed.

 

353 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


In re Condemnation by DOT of Right of Way for State Route 79, Section W10


No. 102 WAP 1999


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


568 Pa. 546; 798 A.2d 725; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 1239


September 11, 2000, Argued  
June 17, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered March 18, 1999, at No. 1055CD1997, reversing the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Washington County entered April 18, 1997, at No. 93-2357. 727 A.2d 618 (Pa. Cmwlth. 1999). Trial Court Judge: O'Dell-Seneca, Debbie, Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Colins, James Gardner, President Judge, McGinley, Bernard L., Judge, Smith-Ribner, Doris A., Judge, Pellegrini, Dan R., Judge, Friedman, Rochelle S., Judge, Kelley, James R., Senior Judge, Flaherty, Jim, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to the power of condemnation granted in the Pennsylvania Eminent Domain Code, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 26, § 1-101 et seq., appellant state transportation department filed a declaration of partial taking for property owned by appellee landowner. The trial court ruled that the landowner's property was not landlocked. On appeal, the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) reversed. The department appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issues were: (1) whether Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 26, § 1-406(a) required the landowner to raise by preliminary objections the claim that the condemnation landlocked his remaining property and diminished its fair market value; and (2) whether Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 26, § 1-602(a) allowed the admission of evidence of the department's later taking of neighboring property, which served to insure that the landowner had legal access to his remaining property, on the issue of damages. The appellate court concluded that the landowner was not required to file preliminary objections. The landowner's claim went to the value of his remaining property after the condemnation, which was not a matter that had to be raised by preliminary objections. The department's subsequent taking was not admissible in determining the just compensation to which the landowner was entitled. Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 26, § 1-602(a) provided that just compensation was the difference in relevant fair market values "immediately before" and "immediately after" a condemnation. The use of the word "immediately" allowed for no lapse between the taking and the point at which the landowner's property was valued.


OUTCOME: The order of the commonwealth court was affirmed. The case was remanded to the trial court.

 

354 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Perry


No. 11 EAP 2000, No. 12 EAP 2000


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


568 Pa. 499; 798 A.2d 697; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 1146


October 18, 2000, Argued  
June 3, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Commonwealth v. Perry, 2007 PA Super 36, 2007 Pa. Super. LEXIS 190 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of the Superior Court Entered on September 13, 1999 at No. 1313 Philadelphia 1998, Reversing the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County on March 11, 1998 at No. 1016 June Term 1996. 1999 PA Super 227, 740 A.2d 712 (Pa. Super. 1999). Trial Court Judge: Berry, Willis W., Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Cavanaugh, James R., Judge, Joyce, Michael T., Judge, Olszewski, Peter Paul, Judge.
Commonwealth v. Stewart, 1999 PA Super 227, 740 A.2d 712, 1999 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2842 (Pa. Super. Ct., 1999)
Commonwealth v. Perry, 747 A.2d 418, 1999 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2924 (Pa. Super. Ct., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state supreme court granted allocatur after the superior court (Pennsylvania) reversed a suppression court's suppression of evidence obtained through a warrantless vehicle search, after defendants were taken into custody, handcuffed, and put in a police car.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether exigent circumstances excused the warrantless search of a vehicle after the occupants were taken into custody. In a plurality opinion, the state supreme court held that the search was valid under the Pennsylvania Constitution. The lead opinion held that exigent circumstances existed, as there was a threat of deadly harm to the police. The Pennsylvania Constitution provided greater protections than the Fourth Amendment. A police officer had to move the running vehicle, and there was testimony that the officer ran the risk of injury from a concealed weapon during that process. Further, the search was limited to secure the passenger compartment, and after the weapons were discovered, no further search was conducted. Two justices joined in finding the search proper, as probable cause arose unexpectedly, before police had a chance to secure a search warrant. Their view was that the Pennsylvania Constitution did not require more than the Fourth Amendment. One justice opined that both probable cause and exigent circumstances were required, but sufficient exigency existed, because the vehicle was running, and firearms were said to be in the area.


OUTCOME: The order of the superior court was affirmed, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

356 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Packer


No. 2 MAP 2001


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


568 Pa. 481; 798 A.2d 192; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 1143; 32 ELR 20765


October 16, 2001, Argued  
May 31, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of Commonwealth Court entered 5/9/00 at 754 A.2d 44, No. 2265 CD 1999 which reversed the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County entered on 1/21/99 at No. 1603-98, Criminal Division. Trial Court Judge: MacElree II, James P., Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Smith, Doris A., Judge, Friedman, Rochelle S., Judge, Jiuliante, Jess S., Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of dumping or depositing solid waste without a permit, in violation of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 35, § 6018.610(1), of the Solid Waste Management Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 35, § 6018.101 et seq. His conviction was reversed, upon appeal, by order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania). The Commonwealth was granted review.


OVERVIEW: The lower appellate court held that defendant, as an employee, had no duty to obtain a permit, and therefore was not guilty of violating the statute prohibiting the dumping or depositing of solid waste without a permit. The supreme court found this was a case of first impression. In disagreeing with the lower appellate court, the supreme court found that the case turned on whether defendant, as an employee, was "any person," under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 35, § 6018.610(1). In finding that he was, the supreme court found that the plain language of the statute did not limit liability to only those responsible for obtaining a permit. The Pennsylvania General Assembly did not intent to so limit liability. It did not result in absurd results, but punished all that were involved in the unpermitted dumping of sold waste. Defendant also argued that the statute was unconstitutional. He argued he could not be punished for not obtaining a permit when he had no duty to obtain one. In rejecting this argument, the supreme court found that he was not punished for the failure to obtain a permit, but rather the affirmative act of dumping solid waste when a permit had not been obtained.


OUTCOME: The order vacating defendant's conviction was reversed.

 

357 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Machipongo Land & Coal Co. v. Dep't of Envtl. Prot.


Nos. 112 MAP 2000 and 119 MAP 2000


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


569 Pa. 3; 799 A.2d 751; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 1139; 32 ELR 20706


November 13, 2001, Argued  
May 30, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Decree Nisi of Commonwealth Court entered as final judgment on October 19, 2000 at No. 248MD1992. Trial Court Judge: Pelligrini, Dan, Commonwealth Court Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both plaintiff owners of coal mining property and defendant Pennsylvania environmental agency and officials appealed from a judgment of the Pennsylvania Commonwealth Court that declared invalid some, but not all, of the regulatory designations of the owners' property as unsuitable for mining pursuant to the Pennsylvania Surface Mining Conservation and Reclamation Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 52, § 1396.4e(b).


OVERVIEW: The Pennsylvania Surface Mining Conservation and Reclamation Act, at § 4.5, 52 Pa. Stat. § 1396.4e(b), complied with federal legislation by providing for the agency to declare certain areas unsuitable for mining because of environmental threats, particularly water pollution threats. When the agency designated a particular watershed as unsuitable, owners of coal mining property in that watershed challenged the regulation as an unconstitutional taking without compensation, violative of U.S. Const. amend. V and Pa. Const. art. I, § 10. The supreme court held that to make this determination, the trial court would first have to determine, as to each parcel as a whole, whether the owners had been deprived of all economically beneficial or productive use of land. If no such total deprivation was found, the trial court would have to apply the balancing test used in traditional takings case law. Finally, the trial court was to consider whether, because of the danger to clean public waterways, the danger of pollution constituted a public nuisance that could be enjoined.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the trial court ruling that one property parcel had no value for mining purposes, but reversed the remainder of the judgment and remanded for a finding of whether a taking had occurred under all applicable analyses, and for consideration of whether mining could be enjoined under a theory of public nuisance.

Erfer v. Commonwealth


14 MM 2002


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


568 Pa. 128; 794 A.2d 325; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 482



March 15, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Application for Relief Pursuant to Section 726 of the Judicial Code.



DISPOSITION: Relief on state constitutional law claims raised in petitioners' petition for review was denied. State law claims were dismissed. Jurisdiction was relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A single judge of the Pennsylvania Commonwealth Court, to whom the instant court had remanded petitioner voters' constitutional challenge, in an emergency application for an exercise of plenary jurisdiction, to reapportionment legislation, 2002 Pa. Laws 1, enacted and administered by respondent officials, reported his findings and conclusions to the court.


OVERVIEW: Certain voters who claimed to tend to vote Democratic, but who were not registered Democrats, challenged Pennsylvania's post-2000 congressional redistricting scheme as Republican gerrymandering, violative of equal protection and election rights guarantees set forth at Pa. Const. art. I, §§ 1, 5, and 26. Although the high court held that the voters had established aggrievement for purposes of standing, it found that they had failed to show gerrymandering violative of equal protection. Noting that Pennsylvania's guarantees were coterminous to federal guarantees, it applied a federal gerrymandering test that required the voters to show that the legislators had acted with a discriminatory purpose and that this action shut Democrats out of the political process. Although the high court appreciated that the Republican legislature, as a political body, undoubtedly intended to limit Democratic chances, it held that the voters' evidence failed to establish that Democrats would be excluded from the political process.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the voters' constitutional claims.

SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


568 Pa. 182; 795 A.2d 340; 2002 Pa. LEXIS 304


January 30, 2001, Submitted  
February 20, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Rice, 2002 Pa. LEXIS 750 (Pa., Apr. 18, 2002)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Rice v. Pennsylvania, 538 U.S. 926, 123 S. Ct. 1571, 155 L. Ed. 2d 319, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 2251 (2003)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Commonwealth v. Rice, 2013 Pa. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 577 (2013)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Rice v. Gavin, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 21258 (E.D. Pa., Feb. 18, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from Order of Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, entered December 17, 1998 at 0623 and 0624 September Term, 1996. Trial Court Judge: Jones, II, C. Darnell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought direct review of a judgment of sentence of the Philadelphia County Common Pleas Court (Pennsylvania) sentencing him, on a jury verdict, to death, after his conviction, in a trial to the court, of two counts of first degree murder and related offenses.


OVERVIEW: After a trial court convicted him of murder and other offenses, a jury determined that imposition of the death penalty was appropriate. The high court found that the evidence was sufficient to support both the guilt and penalty determinations, that the trial court had not abused its discretion in its evidentiary rulings, that the jurors properly weighed aggravating and mitigating factors, and that the prosecutor's remarks in closing argument during the penalty phase were not improper. The high court did find that one error occurred in instructing the jury in that, in the absence, at the time of trial, of Pennsylvania case law regarding instructions on victim impact evidence, the trial court used a New Jersey instruction that was not appropriate in Pennsylvania. However, the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because it stated an even more restrictive rule regarding victim impact evidence, so defendant could not possibly have been prejudiced.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Commonwealth v. Hawkins

SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


567 Pa. 310; 787 A.2d 292; 2001 Pa. LEXIS 2755

December 31, 2001, Decided

Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Commonwealth v. Hawkins, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 1289 (Pa., June 20, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the order of the MONTGOMERY COUNTY Court of Common Pleas which denied Petition for Post Conviction Relief. Trial Court Judge: Tressler, Paul W., Judge.
Commonwealth v. Hawkins, 549 Pa. 352, 701 A.2d 492, 1997 Pa. LEXIS 1924 (1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of murder and was sentenced to death, sought review of the judgment of the Montgomery County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) denying his petition for postconviction relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that his trial counsel and Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq., counsel rendered ineffective assistance on numerous issues. In proving his case, defendant had to prove that there was merit to the underlying claim, counsel had no reasonable basis for his or her conduct, and there was a reasonable probability that, but for counsel's action or omission, the outcome of the proceeding would have been different. Defendant's PCRA counsel was not ineffective due to a conflict of interest, although PCRA counsel had earlier represented one of the prosecution's trial witnesses. Defendant failed to assert how PCRA counsel's representation of the now-deceased prosecution witness affected his representation of defendant. Defendant's claim that PCRA counsel was ineffective for failing to raise a claim that previous counsel was ineffective for not objecting when the prosecution misstated the strength of evidence linking defendant to the crime scene. The reviewing court found that because there was plenty of evidence placing defendant at the scene, he was not prejudiced as a result of the misstatement.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Simmons


No. 260 Capital Appeal Docket

569 Pa. 405; 804 A.2d 625; 2001 Pa. LEXIS 2847

As Amended May 29, 2002.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition, pursuant to the Pennsylvania Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq., challenging his first-degree murder conviction and death sentence. The Court of Common Pleas of Cambria County (Pennsylvania), Criminal Division, denied the petition and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death. The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence on direct appeal and defendant subsequently filed a petition for postconviction relief, alleging that the Commonwealth violated his due process rights by failing to inform him that a key witness was unable to identify him when she was shown a book containing his photograph and photographs of other people who had been arrested, that the trial court improperly instructed the jury during the penalty phase of trial, and that he received ineffective assistance from counsel. The state supreme court held that (1) the Commonwealth should have informed defendant that its witness was not able to identify him when she looked at photographs, the violation was not excused because the prosecutor was never informed of that fact, but the defendant was not prejudiced by the Commonwealth's actions; (2) the trial court properly instructed the jury; and (3) defendant failed to prove that his counsel was ineffective.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

T.B. v. L.R.M.


No. 62 WAP 2000


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


567 Pa. 222; 786 A.2d 913; 2001 Pa. LEXIS 2753


September 10, 2001, Argued  
December 28, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by T.B. v. L.R.M., 2005 PA Super 114, 2005 Pa. Super. LEXIS 431 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered June 5, 2000, at No. 1996PGH1997, vacating the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Cambria County, entered August 26, 1997, at No. 1996-3626. 753 A.2d 873 (Pa. Super. Ct. 2000). Trial Court Judges: Leahey, Francis J., Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Del Sole, Joseph A., President Judge, McEwen Jr., Stephen J., President Judge Emeritus, Johnson, Justin M., Judge, Ford Elliott, Kate, Judge, Eakin, J. Michael, Judge, Joyce, Michael T., Judge, Stevens, Correale F., Judge, Kelly, John T., Judge, Popovich, Zoran, Senior Judge.
T. B. v. L. R. M., 2000 PA Super 168, 753 A.2d 873, 2000 Pa. Super. LEXIS 749 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania granted allocatur sole to examine whether an order of the superior court properly applied the common law doctrine of in loco parentis to confer standing upon appellee girlfriend to seek partial custody of appellant mother's child for purposes of visitation.


OVERVIEW: The mother and her girlfriend had an exclusive, intimate relationship and agreed that the mother should have a child. After the child's birth, they shared day-to-day child rearing responsibilities. After they separated, the mother refused to let the girlfriend visit the child. The lower courts both held that the girlfriend had standing to seek custody/visitation pursuant to the doctrine of in loco parentis. The state supreme court agreed. The nature of the relationship between the parties had no legal significance to the determination of whether the girlfriend stood in loco parentis to the child. The mother consented to the girlfriend's performance of parental duties. She was more than a frequent caretaker. The parties and the child lived as a family unit. The girlfriend assumed the role of co-parent. Therefore, she had standing to seek partial custody for purposes of visitation.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Ppg Indus. v. Bd. of Fin.


87 MAP 1996


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


567 Pa. 580; 790 A.2d 261; 2001 Pa. LEXIS 2564


February 25, 2000, Submitted  
November 30, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court dated June 19, 1996, at No. 2355 C.D. 1987, affirming the Order of the Board of Finance and Revenue dated October 2, 1987, at No. R-10-904 681 A.2d 832 (Pa. Cmwlth. 1996). JUDGES BELOW: COMMONWEALTH - Colins, PJ, Doyle, McGinley, Smith, Pellegrini, Friedman and Kelley, JJ.



DISPOSITION: On appeal after remand, supreme court held that 72 P.S. § 7602 was not a compensatory tax; that the manufacturing exemption was unconstitutional; that the void exclusionary language was severable; and the Commonwealth was directed forthwith to provide a retrospective remedy for the previous descriminatory result.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania granted appellant taxpayer's direct appeal of an order of the Commonwealth Court affirming an order of appellee Board of Finance and Revenue, construing the manufacturing exemptions of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 7602.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was a Pennsylvania corporation that conducted manufacturing operations both within and without the state. It challenged an order that affirmed a resettlement of its tax return. The trial court rejected its constitutional and statutory arguments and affirmed the resettlement. The state supreme court held that the State failed to carry its burden of proving that § 7602 was a compensatory tax. Neither party offered any evidence on the issue. Because the tax was not a compensatory tax, it was unconstitutional. The state supreme court was left solely with the issue of determining the appropriate remedy. It rejected the arguments against severability and severed the manufacturing exemption from § 7602 in its entirety.


OUTCOME: The statute was declared unconstitutional, the void exclusionary language was severed, and the matter was remanded for a retrospective remedy.

Allen v. Mellinger


Nos. 44 and 45 M.D. Appeal Dkts. 1999


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


567 Pa. 1; 784 A.2d 762; 2001 Pa. LEXIS 2497


November 15, 1999, Argued  
November 20, 2001, Decided  
November 20, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended January 8, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered August 20, 1998 at Nos. 2408 CD 1997 and 2310 CD 1997 affirming the judgment entered July 9, 1997 at Nos. 89-01668 and 89-01623 of the Court of Common Pleas of Lebanon County, Civil Division. Judges: Pellegrini, Leadbetter, JJ. and Juiliante, S.J., Com. Court / Hon. John C. Tylwalk, CCP.

Allen v. Mellinger, 722 A.2d 1183, 1998 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 743 (Pa. Commw. Ct. 1998) 



DISPOSITION: Order of the lower court reversed. Order of the trial court vacated. Case remanded to the trial court for recalculation of delay damages.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured party sued appellees, the department and an individual, seeking damages related to severe injuries that she suffered in a collision between automobiles driven by herself and the individual. The Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) affirmed a judgment of the trial court that calculated the department's delay damages upon its 40 percent share of the verdict instead of the entire verdict. The injured party appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the injured party argued that the appellate court's holding in Royer Garden was inconsistent with other cases and that the supreme court should have held that the department and the individual were jointly and severally liable for the entire amount of delay damages because they were jointly and severally liable for the entire amount of the verdict. Upon review, the supreme court overruled Woods and held that delay damages recoverable from the department were limited to those calculated based upon the statutory cap. Additionally, it held that the department, as a Commonwealth party, was not jointly and severally liable for delay damages that exceed those calculated on the statutory cap. The Woods rationale allowed Pennsylvania courts to create an uncertainty of outcome to motivate settlement where no uncertainty otherwise existed. That was far different from channeling the uncertainty of outcome that existed in the case of private litigants not subject to limitations on liability.


OUTCOME: The order of the appellate court was reversed, the order of the trial court was vacated, and the case was remanded to the trial court for recalculation of delay damages recoverable from the department in accordance with the opinion.

Commonwealth v. Stallworth


No. 278 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


566 Pa. 349; 781 A.2d 110; 2001 Pa. LEXIS 2175


December 4, 2000, Argued  
October 4, 2001, Decided  
October 4, 2001, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Commonwealth v. Stallworth, 2013 Pa. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 1035 (2013)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Stallworth v. Kerestes, 2016 Pa. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 4549 (2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered on 01/29/1999 in the CCP, Lancaster County, Criminal Division at 0910-1998. Trial Court Judges: Perezous, Michael J., Judge. Notice of Appeal Filed Below: August 13, 1999. Notice of Appeal Docketed in Supreme Court: August 18, 1999. Lower Court/Agency Docket Num 0910-1998.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED THE VERDICT OF GUILT, BUT VACATED THE SENTENCE OF DEATH AND REMANDED FOR A NEW SENTENCING HEARING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, the Court of Common Pleas, Lancaster County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania) entered a judgment convicting defendant of murder in the first degree and burglary, and sentencing him to death. Defendant filed a direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: At the conclusion of the trial's penalty phase, the jury found the existence of two aggravating circumstances: that defendant committed a killing while in the perpetration of a felony, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9711(d)(6); and that, at the time of the killing, defendant was subject to a protection from abuse (PFA) order restricting in any way his behavior towards the victim. On appeal, the state supreme court held that defendant's suppression motion was properly denied, because: (1) his statements during the stand-off were not the product of police interrogation, but were unsolicited statements uttered in response to police negotiations designed to encourage him to surrender; and (2) the mere fact that the seizure of his clothing was not contemporaneous with the seizure of his person, but occurred after he had been removed to the place of detention, did not prevent the seizure from being incident to his lawful arrest. However, because defendant did not have anecdotal knowledge of the existence of the PFA order, he was not subject to that order for purposes of the aggravating circumstance in 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9711(d)(18). Therefore, he was improperly sentenced to death.


OUTCOME: The verdict of guilt was affirmed. However, the sentence of death was vacated and the case was remanded for a new sentencing hearing.

Commonwealth v. Samuels


No. 91 M.D. Appeal Docket 2000


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


566 Pa. 109; 778 A.2d 638; 2001 Pa. LEXIS 1854


January 8, 2001, Submitted  
August 28, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Order of Superior Court entered November 15, 1999 at No. 3746 PHL 1998, which affirmed the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Criminal Division, entered July 16, 1998 at No. 4713-97. Trial Court Judges: Toal, William R., Judge. Intermediate Court Judges: Schiller, Berle M., Judge, Olszewski, Peter Paul, Judge, Beck, Phyllis W., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a Superior Court (Pennsylvania) affirmance of a judgment convicting him of homicide by vehicle while driving under the influence, in violation of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3735. He argued trial court error in failing to instruct jurors that they had to find he acted with criminal negligence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of involuntary manslaughter, driving under the influence, homicide by vehicle while driving under the influence, and accident involving death or bodily injury. He appealed the conviction of homicide by vehicle while driving under the influence, in violation of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3735(a), arguing that the trial court denied his due process rights when it failed to instruct jurors that the offense required a finding that he acted with criminal negligence. The court agreed with defendant. Because a minimum culpability level of criminal negligence was required to convict someone of vehicular homicide, a similar level of culpability applied to the offense of vehicular homicide while driving under the influence. However, in defendant's case, the error was harmless, because the jury determined that he was criminally negligent when it convicted him of involuntary manslaughter, because a criminal negligence instruction was given on that charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Commonwealth v. Ligons


No. 274 Capital Appeal Dkt.


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


565 Pa. 417; 773 A.2d 1231; 2001 Pa. LEXIS 1417


January 2, 2001, Submitted  
July 6, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of certiorari denied: Ligons v. Pennsylvania, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6082 (U.S. Oct. 7, 2002).
Writ of certiorari denied Ligons v. Pennsylvania, 537 U.S. 827, 123 S. Ct. 122, 154 L. Ed. 2d 40, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6082 (2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Commonwealth v. Ligons, 601 Pa. 103, 971 A.2d 1125, 2009 Pa. LEXIS 930 (2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at Commonwealth v. Ligons, 2014 Pa. LEXIS 3049 (Pa., Nov. 19, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order imposing Judgment of Sentence of Death and Other Judgments of Sentence dated 6/1/99 entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County at No. 9805-0086. Trial Court Judges: Greenspan, Jane Cutler, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) entered a judgment, upon a jury verdict, imposing a sentence of death on defendant for the first degree murder and robbery of the victim, a pizza deliveryman. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the State did not disclose evidence of a photographic identification by the victim's wife, and that when she testified to such identification, the trial court should have granted a mistrial. He also argued that he was entitled to a new penalty hearing as a result of the State's arguments inviting the jury to consider victim impact evidence and characterizing the death penalty statute, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9711, as geared in favor of imposing a life sentence. The state supreme court held that the trial court did not err in refusing to grant a mistrial, because the State, in its closing arguments, asked the jurors to disregard the victim's wife's identification testimony, and the trial court instructed the jury to consider the identification testimony with caution. Moreover, defendant was not entitled to a new penalty hearing, because the State's arguments regarding the victim were offered to counter the sympathy associated with defendant's mitigating evidence, and while the State's description of § 9711 might not have been ideal, the remarks were not meant to circumvent the judicial process by interjecting considerations outside of § 9711.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Natividad

Writ of certiorari denied Natividad v. Pennsylvania, 535 U.S. 1099, 122 S. Ct. 2300, 152 L. Ed. 2d 1056, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 3899 (2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Commonwealth v. Natividad, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2897 (Pa., Dec. 27, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, dated February 12, 1998, at No. 97-04-0013.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of sentence of death is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of murder, robbery, and related offenses, in Philadelphia County Common Pleas Court, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), and from a death sentence, raising various errors that allegedly occurred both during trial and during the penalty phase, particularly the use of victim impact testimony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death after conviction of, among other things, robbery and a murder committed later the same day as the robbery. As in all death penalty cases, the high court first assured that the evidence was sufficient on every matter determined at the guilt phase. It then addressed individual claims of error, holding there was no abuse of discretion in trying both indictments together, since potential for jury confusion was slight, that there was no reason to suppose an identification was tainted, that there was no abuse of discretion in the admission of evidence, and that robbery of the murder victim could be proven without showing it was successful. Defendant's primary challenge was to the use of victim impact testimony in the penalty phase. Victim impact testimony had already been held constitutional, but the court added a prospective requirement that notice of its use be given before trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Commonwealth v. Means


54 E.D. Appeal Docket 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


565 Pa. 309; 773 A.2d 143; 2001 Pa. LEXIS 1297


October 18, 1999, Argued  
June 25, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County at No. 91 January Term 1997, dated October 14, 1997, declaring 42 Pa.C.S. § 9711(a)(2) and (c)(2) unconstitutional.
Commonwealth v. Means, 34 Phila. 454, 1997 Phila. Cty. Rptr. LEXIS 91 (Pa. C.P., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's conviction of first-degree murder, the Commonwealth appealed an order of Philadelphia County Common Pleas Court (Pennsylvania) declaring that 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9711(a)(2), (c)(2), which permitted victim impact testimony at the penalty phase, violated federal and state constitutional prohibitions against cruel and unusual punishment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in a bench trial of first-degree murder and related charges. As the penalty phase began, defendant moved successfully to exclude victim impact evidence, on grounds that 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9711(a)(2), (c)(2) violated prohibitions against cruel and unusual punishment contained in U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Pa. Const. art. I, § 13. The high court held that there was no violation of any constitutional guarantees in this statute, which carefully limited consideration of such evidence to situations where aggravating circumstances had already been shown. Pennsylvania practice had long treated appropriate victim impact testimony as admissible where relevant, and the court expressed confidence that trial courts could limit the purposes for which such testimony was considered. Although it did not require its use, the court set forth an instruction that it recommended for trial court use in cases in which victim impact evidence was planned.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded for penalty phase proceedings.

Commonwealth v. Morris
