April 20, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Commonwealth v. Morris, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 710 (Pa., May 1, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Trial Division, entered on December 21, 1999, at Nos. 409-413, July Term 1982, staying the execution scheduled for January 27, 2000. JUDGE BELOW: C.C.P. - Honorable James Fitzgerald.
Commonwealth v. Morris, 522 Pa. 533, 564 A.2d 1226, 1989 Pa. LEXIS 383 (1989)



DISPOSITION: WE VACTATE THE TRIAL COURT'S ORDER STAYING THE EXECUTION SINCE THE TRIAL COURT FAILED TO FOLLOW THE REQUIREMENTS OF SECTION 9545(c).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, prisoner, filed a motion for a stay of execution, and a petition for post-conviction relief. The Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Trial Division (Pennsylvania) denied the petition for post-conviction relief, but granted the motion for a stay of execution, and the Commonwealth appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and robbery in 1983, and sentenced to death. On appeal, his conviction and sentence were upheld. Thereafter, defendant filed his first petition for post-conviction relief, but relief was denied. In this action on defendant's second petition for post-conviction relief, the state supreme court held that (1) it would exercise extraordinary jurisdiction, pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 726, to examine defendant's argument that 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9545 was unconstitutional; (2) § 9545 defined appropriate circumstances for securing substantive rights, and was not unconstitutional; and (3) a trial court should grant a stay of execution under § 9545 only when the petitioner demonstrated that the petition was timely, or, in cases where the petition was not timely, he established one of the exceptions recognized by § 9545(b); the petitioner filed his motion for a stay with his petition for post-conviction relief, or otherwise demonstrated that his petition was pending before the court; and the petition for post-conviction relief demonstrated some likelihood that the petitioner could prevail on the merits.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated the trial court's order staying defendant's execution.

Crooks v. DOT, Bureau of Driver Licensing


No. 70 MAP 2000


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


564 Pa. 436; 768 A.2d 1106; 2001 Pa. LEXIS 753


August 31, 2000, Submitted  
April 11, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Direct appeal from the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, Civil Division, at No. 00-00577, entered March 2, 2000. Trial Court Judge: Melody, M. Joseph, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and the suspension of appellee's driver's license reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commonwealth challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), which sustained the statutory appeal of appellee from a one-year suspension of his driver's license imposed pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1532(b)(3), 1581.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was found guilty of DUI in New Jersey. Appellant mailed appellee a notice that it was treating his New Jersey DUI conviction as the equivalent of a conviction for violating 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a), and as mandated by 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1532(b)(3) it was suspending his driver's license for one year. The trial court sustained appellee's statutory appeal, holding that New Jersey's report of the DUI conviction was insufficient and the amendment to the Driver's License Compact, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1584, was unconstitutional. On appeal, the supreme court held that 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1584 did not violate due process, and that section provided that the omission from foreign state reports of any information required by 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1581, art. III, would not prevent appellant from complying with its duties under the compact. In addition, the supreme court concluded that because appellee did not claim he did not know of the nature of the proceeding, or that he had no meaningful opportunity to be heard, or that he lacked notice of the actual conviction underlying the proceeding, there was no due process violation and the suspension should have been upheld.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the order and reinstated the suspension of appellee's driver's license.

Coady v. Vaughn


No. 212 MM 1999


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


564 Pa. 604; 770 A.2d 287; 2001 Pa. LEXIS 567


March 14, 2000, Submitted  
March 22, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On petition for certification of questions of law from the United States Court of Appeals for the Third Circuit. JUDGES BELOW: U.S. Court of Appeals, Third Circuit / U.S. District Court - Eastern District, Edward R. Becker, Chief Judge, Walter K. Stapleton, Circuit Judge and Stanley Harris, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Referred this matter back to the United States Court of Appeals for the Third Circuit.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state prisoner sought a writ of habeas corpus in federal district court attacking his parole denial on ex post facto grounds. When his petition was dismissed, he appealed to the United States Court of Appeals for the Third Circuit which declined to reach the merits as the claim had not been presented to a state court. The court of appeals petitioned Pennsylvania's supreme court for certification of questions of law.


OVERVIEW: The certified questions of law accepted by the state supreme court were whether a person who had been denied parole could obtain review from a Pennsylvania state court of a claim that the denial of parole violated the Ex Post Facto Clause of the United States Constitution, and, if so, what was the proper method for review. The state supreme court answered that direct review was not available, and because mandamus was not available to compel a purely discretionary act, mandamus would not be available where the substance of the board's discretionary action was the subject of the challenge. Where, however, the challenge was directed at the actions of the board taken pursuant to changed statutory requirements as opposed to the board's discretionary actions and criteria, an action for mandamus was viable as a means for examining whether statutory requirements were altered in a manner violative of the Ex Post Facto Clause. Such an action could be brought in the original jurisdiction of the state court. Absent a change in the statutes governing parole, however, denial of parole was generally a discretionary matter not subject to review.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court answered the certified questions and referred the matter back to the federal court of appeals.

Harrington v. DOT, Bureau of Driver Licensing


209 M.D. Appeal Docket 1999


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


563 Pa. 565; 763 A.2d 386; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 2991


December 3, 1999, Submitted  
December 22, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, Civil Division at Docket No. 99-02476, filed May 6, 1999. Trial Court Judge: MacElree, James P., Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the ruling of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County (Pennsylvania), Civil Division, which reversed the suspension of appellee's driver's license by the Pennsylvania Bureau of Driver Licensing pursuant to New Jersey's and Pennsylvania's Driver's License Compact, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:5D-1-14 and 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1581, and also pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellee, possessing a Pennsylvania driver's license, was convicted in a New Jersey court of driving under the influence. Pursuant to the Drivers' License Compact of 1961, New Jersey authorities notified appellant, Pennsylvania's bureau of licensing, of the conviction. Appellant then suspended appellee's license for one year. The trial court reversed, holding that the report provided by New Jersey did not include all the required information and therefore appellee did not have proper notice. The court reversed and reinstated the suspension, holding that under the recent case McCafferty, full compliance with the reporting requirements on the part of a reporting state was not necessary. New Jersey's report of appellee's conviction identified him specifically, as well as the substantially similar, out-of-state offense of which he was convicted. Appellant's fulfillment of its duties under the compact was consistent with due process requirements.


OUTCOME: Trial court judgment reversed and suspension of appellee's license reinstated. The notice provided by appellant was adequate under constitutional due process standards, and in addition appellee participated fully in a de novo hearing, in which he confirmed the factual predicate for the suspension and supplied the information which he asserted he lacked.

Commonwealth v. Sattazahn


No. 258 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


563 Pa. 533; 763 A.2d 359; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 2815


May 1, 2000, Argued  
November 27, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Sattazahn, 2001 Pa. LEXIS 1561 (Pa., July 20, 2001)
Writ of certiorari granted, Motion granted by Sattazahn v. Pennsylvania, 535 U.S. 926, 122 S. Ct. 1294, 152 L. Ed. 2d 207, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 1530 (2002)
Motion granted by Sattazahn v. Pennsylvania, 537 U.S. 807, 123 S. Ct. 57, 154 L. Ed. 2d 9, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 5442 (2002)
Affirmed by Sattazahn v. Pennsylvania, 537 U.S. 101, 123 S. Ct. 732, 154 L. Ed. 2d 588, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 748 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered February 16, 1999 in the Court of Common Pleas, Berks County, Criminal Division at No. 2194-89. Trial Court Judges: Keller, Scott D., President Judge.
Commonwealth v. Sattazahn, 539 Pa. 270, 652 A.2d 293, 1994 Pa. LEXIS 835 (1994)



DISPOSITION: Verdict of guilt and sentence of death on retrial affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review, on direct appeal, of the Court of Common Pleas, Berks County (Pennsylvania), Criminal Division, claiming counsel was not allowed to properly cross-examine co-defendant and imposition of death penalty was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: After an initial conviction for murder, imposition of a life sentence and reversal for a new trial, appellant was again convicted of murder, but sentenced to death. The court affirmed his conviction and sentence. Limitation of cross-examination of co-defendant regarding his guilty plea and preclusion of police reports which allegedly contained inconsistent statements was not error. Despite some limitations on cross-examination, the jury heard co-defendant pleaded guilty to third-degree murder in exchange for his testimony. Counsel was ultimately successful in showing co-defendant another police report after which he testified he lied to police. Imposition of the death penalty on retrial was constitutional. The first jury did not make a decision on the merits regarding an appropriate penalty, did not find the State failed to prove its case and made no findings concerning aggravating or mitigating circumstances. Since it made no decision, there could not in fact be any acquittal on the merits. Nor did the imposition of a life sentence by the trial judge operate as an acquittal.


OUTCOME: Conviction and sentence affirmed because counsel was allowed sufficient latitude to cross-examine co-defendant and death penalty was constitutional because the prior life sentence was not an acquittal on the merits.

Commonwealth v. Nixon


No. 87 W.D. Appeal Docket 1999, No. 88 W.D. Appeal Docket 1999


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


563 Pa. 425; 761 A.2d 1151; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 2816


March 7, 2000, Argued  
November 27, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied April 30, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 3422.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered 9/21/1998 at No. 1310PGH1997 affirming the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Blair County entered 6/10/1997 at No. 1260 CR 1996. Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered 9/21/1998 at No. 1311PGH1997 affirming the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Blair County entered 6/10/1997 at No. 1261 CR 1996. JUDGES BELOW: CCP - Callan, J.; SUPERIOR - DEL SOLE, Tamilia, Eakin, JJ.



DISPOSITION: Order of the Superior Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed Superior Court (Pennsylvania) affirmance of their convictions of involuntary manslaughter and child endangerment in refusing to obtain medical treatment for their 16-year-old. Defendants argued that mature minor affirmative defense should apply and decedent had constitutional privacy right to refuse treatment.


OVERVIEW: Defendants and their 16-year-old daughter belonged to a religious group that did not believe in seeking medical treatment. They were convicted of involuntary manslaughter and child endangerment when she died of an illness that could have been controlled. Although case law in some states applied a mature minor rule, letting older minors decline medical treatment for religious reasons, 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 10101 clearly set 18 as the age of consent, with only a few exceptions, not including health care decisions. Defendants also argued that decedent had a privacy right to make her own health care decisions. The court held that even though the Pennsylvania right was broader than federal privacy rights, it bowed to a compelling state interest. Since Pennsylvania had a compelling state interest in the welfare of minors, it overcame decedent's privacy right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment; since statutes provided a specific age of consent, with explicit exceptions, a mature minor rule was not appropriate. Even the protective Pennsylvania privacy rule gave way to the compelling state interest in a child's life.

 

381 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Harrisburg Sch. Dist. v. Hickok


No. 78 M.D. Appeal Dkt. 2000, No. 79 M.D. Appeal Dkt. 2000, No. 80 M.D. Appeal Dkt. 2000


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


563 Pa. 391; 761 A.2d 1132; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 2817


September 12, 2000, Argued  
November 27, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Harrisburg Sch. Dist. v. Hickok, 565 Pa. 210, 772 A.2d 435, 2001 Pa. LEXIS 1070 (2001)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered on 6/30/00 at No. 266 MD 2000. Trial Court Judges: Pelligrini, Dan, Commonwealth Court Judge.
Harrisburg Sch. Dist. v. Hickok, 762 A.2d 398, 2000 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 605 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged an order of the commonwealth court (Pennsylvania) which granted appellees' motion for a preliminary injunction to enjoin the enforcement of the Reed Amendment of the Education Empowerment Act, § 8.1, § 1707-B, 2000 Pa. Laws 16, for being unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Education Empowerment Act, § 8.1, 2000 Pa. Laws 16, provided that poorly performing school districts be identified and assisted by the Department of Education. The Reed Amendment to the act, § 8.1, § 1707-B, 2000 Pa. Laws 16, singled out the Harrisburg schools for special treatment. Appellees, Harrisburg School District and school board members, challenged the constitutionality of the act and filed for a preliminary injunction to enjoin the amendment for being unconstitutional. The trial court found the amendment was constitutionally infirm. The court found the amendment was unconstitutional because it was special legislation, since the Harrisburg school district was the only member of a class and there was no rational basis for treating that school district differently from other school districts with failed educational systems.


OUTCOME: Order granting preliminary injunction to enjoin the Reed Amendment was affirmed as the amendment was unconstitutional as special legislation that singled out the Harrisburg School District for special treatment with no rational basis for the special treatment.

 

382 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Butler


No. 38 E.D. Appeal Docket 1998


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


563 Pa. 324; 760 A.2d 384; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 2653


February 1, 2000, Argued  
October 27, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Criminal Division entered on September 14, 1998 at No. 9803-0354 1/1. JUDGE(S) BELOW: C.C.P. - Honorable Gregory E. Smith.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the judgment of sentence.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Commonwealth sought review of the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), Criminal Division, decision finding 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9714(A)(1) violated appellee's procedural due process rights pursuant to both the state and federal constitutions because the burden of demonstrating that an offender was a high risk dangerous offender must rest with the Commonwealth.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was convicted of robbery and other related charges. Because of a prior aggravated assault conviction, the Commonwealth requested that the trial court apply 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9714(A)(1), referred to as the "strike two" sentencing provision, and sentence appellee to a mandatory 10 to 20 year sentence. The trial court found the statute unconstitutional. The court affirmed. The statute placed upon an offender the burden of rebutting a mandatory presumption that, if not rebutted, would subject him or her to greater punishment. A subjective assessment of an offender's potential future dangerousness should have been made through the trial court's consideration of a variety of elements. Accordingly, resolution of competing facts presented at the post-trial proceeding, which was not governed by the rules of evidence, would most likely be outcome determinative. Thus, the Commonwealth should have been the one required to affirmatively convince the trial court of such facts.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because the statute was unconstitutional where it placed the burden of rebutting the presumption that appellee was a high risk offender on the appellee.

 

383 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


COMMONWEALTH v. MCCAFFERTY


No. 1 E.D. Appeal Docket 1998


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


563 Pa. 146; 758 A.2d 1155; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 2383


February 1, 1999, Argued  
September 28, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Direct Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County entered December 31, 1997, at Nos. 9710-0987, 9706-3324, 9707-1564, 9709-0599, 9709-2477, 9707-0806, 9706-3713, 9708-0175, 9707-0600, 9707-0736, 9707-1531, 9707-3368, 9709-4372, 9709-2565, 9709-4283, 9710-0985, 9706-1890, 9706-3055, 9710-0786,9706-4172, 9710-1631 and 9710-1049.
DOT v. McCafferty, 1997 Phila. Cty. Rptr. LEXIS 92 (Pa. C.P., 1997)



DISPOSITION: THE ORDER OF THE COURT OF COMMON PLEAS IS REVERSED AND THE ONE-YEAR SUSPENSIONS OF THE OPERATING PRIVILEGES OF APPELLEES THAT WERE IMPOSED BY PENNDOT IN COMPLIANCE WITH ITS STATUTORY MANDATE ARE REINSTATED. THE CASE IS REMANDED TO THE TRIAL COURT TO ADDRESS THE ISSUE OF WHETHER N.J.S. Section 39 : 4-50(a) IS SUBSTANTIALLY SIMILAR TO 75 Pa. C.S. Section 3731 FOR PURPOSES OF ARTICLE IV (c) OF THE COMPACT. JURISDICTION IS RELINQUISHED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Pennsylvania Department of Transportation sought review of Common Pleas Court, Philadelphia County's (Pennsylvania) consolidated order reinstating appellees' driving privileges after revocation pursuant to the Driver's License Compact of 1961, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1581-1585, finding compact violated United States Constitution double jeopardy, equal protection, and due process guarantees.


OVERVIEW: Pennsylvania adopted the Driver's License Compact of 1961, codified at Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1581-1585, which provided for revocation of operator's licenses of Pennsylvania drivers convicted of drunk driving offenses in participating states. The court held that the compact did not violate appellee drivers' rights under double jeopardy, both because of dual sovereignty and because appellant agency's actions were merely a collateral administrative consequence of convictions elsewhere; equal protection, because the compact did not create a classification of drivers; or due process, because appellees received full notice and hearing in the original proceedings and knew what was going on. Because the compact did require that statutes under which drivers were convicted be substantially similar to drunk driving statutes in the state of licensure, in the case of one appellee who raised the issue, the court ordered determination on remand whether Pennsylvania and New Jersey drunk driving statutes were substantially similar.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order, finding the compact, as a collateral administrative consequence, did not violate any constitutional guarantees, but remanded for determination, as to an appellee convicted in New Jersey, whether Pennsylvania and New Jersey drunk driving statutes were substantially similar.

 

384 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Albert


1 W.D. Appeal Docket 1998


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


563 Pa. 133; 758 A.2d 1149; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 2364


March 7, 2000, Argued  
September 27, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order and Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County entered January 5, 1998 at No. CC 9700990. JUDGE(S): BELOW: CCP-Manning, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commonwealth challenged the order and judgment of sentence entered in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which found that statutory sexual assault, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3122.1, involuntary deviate sexual intercourse, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3123(a)(7), aggravated indecent assault, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3125(8), and indecent assault, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2126(a)(8), were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was convicted of 11 counts of sexual assault on a minor. At sentencing, the trial court arrested judgment for the counts of statutory sexual assault, involuntary deviate sexual intercourse, aggravated indecent assault, and indecent assault, finding the statutes violated equal protection because the provisions criminalized sexual assaults where the victim was less than 16 years old and the offender was 4 or more years older than the victim. Specifically, the trial court held that there was no rational reason to differentiate among defendants based upon their age. The court reversed the decision of the trial court, noting that the right of equal protection under the law did not absolutely prohibit the Commonwealth from classifying individuals for the purpose of receiving different treatment provided that those classifications were reasonable rather than arbitrary. Further, the court agreed with appellant that the legislation served a legitimate state interest, that is, to protect minors younger than 16 years of age from older teenage and adult sexual aggressors.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision because the trial court erred in finding the statutory sexual assault provisions violative of equal protection. The legislation served a legitimate state interest, that is, to protect minors younger than 16 years of age from older teenage and adult sexual aggressors. Accordingly, the court remanded the case for resentencing.

 

385 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Pennsylvania AFL-CIO v. Commonwealth


Nos. 39, 40 and 46 M.D. Appeal Docket 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


563 Pa. 108; 757 A.2d 917; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 2192


November 16, 1998, Argued  
August 30, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court, entered April 1, 1997, at No. 704 M.D. 1996 691 A.2d 1023 (Pa. Cmwlth. 1997). JUDGES BELOW: - / Commonwealth - Colins, PJ, Doyle, Pellegrini, Friedman, KELLEY, Flaherty, Leadbetter, JJ.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff labor groups and one group of state senator intervenors appealed Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) order that sustained preliminary objections, arguing failure to state a claim, raised by defendant Commonwealth executives and other senator intervenors, in action for declaratory judgment that statutory enactment violated Pa. Const. art. III, § 5.


OVERVIEW: A revision of Pennsylvania's workers' compensation statute was enacted after both houses passed a version of the statute that had been further amended by the senate after reworking by a conference committee. In an action against defendant state officials and one group of senator intervenors, plaintiff labor leaders and other intervening senators sought an injunction, dismissed earlier, and a declaratory judgment that the enactment process violated Pa. Const. art. III, § 5 procedures for amended bills. Plaintiffs argued that when a bill returned to its originating chamber from conference, the chamber could have accepted or rejected any amendments, but not added more. Addressing the constitutional issue on its merits, the court found no support in the plain constitutional language, in legislative history, or in policy concerns for the position that further amendments were forbidden, so long as all further amendments were approved by both chambers in votes that were properly recorded.


OUTCOME: Although it found that the trial court erred in sustaining preliminary objections on issues that were not clear on the merits, the court analyzed state constitutional issues on the merits and found no violation. Therefore it affirmed the judgment of the trial court on that basis.

Commonwealth v. Bridges


No. 224 Capital Appeal Dkt.


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


563 Pa. 1; 757 A.2d 859; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 2046


November 15, 1999, Argued  
August 24, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of certiorari denied: Bridges v. Pennsylvania, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 3937 (U.S. May 28, 2002).
Reconsideration denied by Commonwealth v. Bridges, 2001 Pa. LEXIS 2289 (Pa., Oct. 22, 2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Bridges v. Pennsylvania, 535 U.S. 1102, 122 S. Ct. 2306, 152 L. Ed. 2d 1061, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 3937 (2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Commonwealth v. Bridges, 584 Pa. 589, 886 A.2d 1127, 2005 Pa. LEXIS 2590 (2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Decision reached on appeal by Commonwealth v. Bridges, 608 Pa. 562, 12 A.3d 748, 2011 Pa. LEXIS 386 (2011)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part Bridges v. Beard, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 57753 (E.D. Pa., Apr. 23, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered on 2/23/98 in the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Criminal Division at No. 117-97. Judges: C.C.P. - Honorable Scott D. Keller.



DISPOSITION: Verdicts and the sentences of death affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County (Pennsylvania) that sentenced the appellant to death following two convictions as an accomplice for first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for being an accomplice to two murders and was given the death penalty. Appellant filed an appeal, alleging various procedural and trial errors. Affirming the conviction, the court held the trial court properly denied appellant's request for an expert as the appellant was not entitled to unlimited court appointed experts until he found one that rendered the opinion he desired. Further, appellant's statement given to the police regarding the murders was properly admitted because appellant was not under arrest for the murders when he gave the challenged statement, it was not obtained in violation of the Davenport/Duncan rule, and was given voluntarily, knowingly, and intelligently by the appellant. The pretrial publicity did not result in the inability to select a fair and impartial jury; therefore, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellant's motion for a change of venue. Further, during the penalty phase, the trial court properly admitted evidence of aggravating circumstances and comments made by the prosecution did not prejudice the jury so that they could not have weighed the evidence objectively.


OUTCOME: Conviction and death penalty as an accomplice affirmed; trial court properly denied appellant's request for court appointed expert as appellant was not entitled to an unlimited number of experts. The statement that appellant gave to the police was properly admitted as the appellant was not under arrest for the murders at the time of the statement and it was given voluntarily, knowingly, and intelligently.

 

387 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Fiore v. White


No. 0269 M.D. Miscellaneous Docket 1999


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


562 Pa. 634; 757 A.2d 842; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 2016


March 14, 2000, Submitted  
August 21, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Petition for Certification of a Question of Law from the Supreme Court of the United States. JUDGES BELOW: U.S. SUPREME COURT - Justice Stephen Breyer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court of the United States petitioned the court for certification of a question of Pennsylvania law. The court granted the petition for certification on whether a particular judicial decision created new law or simply stated or clarified existing law.


OVERVIEW: After his co-defendant's conviction was overturned appellant, who had been tried with the co-defendant, sought postconviction relief from his own conviction. When that relief was denied, he sought federal habeas relief. That case went before the U.S. Supreme Court, which petitioned the court for certification of a question of Pennsylvania law, specifically, whether a particular decision of the court correctly stated Pennsylvania law as it existed when appellant was convicted. The court granted the petition for certification and answered the question in the affirmative. The earlier decision interpreted a statute, 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6018.401(a), for the first time but applied familiar rules of statutory construction; therefore, the decision clarified existing law rather than stated a new rule of law.


OUTCOME: The court answered in the affirmative the question certified for review and referred the matter back to the Supreme Court of the United States. Although the judicial decision at issue interpreted a particular statute for the first time, because it applied established rules of statutory construction it clarified, rather than announced, law.

DeFazio v. Civil Serv. Comm'n


No. 28 W.D. Appeal Docket 1998


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


562 Pa. 431; 756 A.2d 1103; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 2020; 16 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1121


March 7, 2000, Argued  
August 21, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, dated March 27, 1998, at No. G.D. 98-3346. JUDGE BELOW: CCP - Jaffe, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, attorney general as intervenor, directly appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which issued a permanent injunction and declared 16 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §§ 4216, 4217 unconstitutional as it violated the equal protection principles of Pa. Const. art. III, § 32.


OVERVIEW: Appellee county sheriff brought an action in equity seeking to enjoin the county from enforcing 16 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §§ 4216, 4217 which was directed specifically at his office. The trial court issued a permanent injunction and declared the legislation unconstitutional. The court affirmed because the legislation violated the equal protection principles of Pa. Const. art. III, § 32. The statutes regulated the activities of the sheriff's employees, and plainly interfered with appellee's interest in the management and operation of his office as it limited his ability to supervise and terminate his employees, and his ability to utilize appropriated funds. Therefore, appellee sheriff had standing as he had a direct and substantial interest. The legislation effectively created a new sub-classification, of sheriffs of second class counties, which bore no relationship to the distinction of that county as a second class county, or to any unique function of the county sheriff. The legislation singled out appellee as the only county official without some discretion in the hiring, termination, or promotion of his employees. Thus, it violated equal protection.


OUTCOME: Judgment declaring the legislation unconstitutional was affirmed because it did violate the equal protection principles in the state constitution by treating one particular county officer differently from any other similarly situated officer without a fair or reasonable relationship to the object of the legislation and bore no relationship to the distinction of the particular county as a county of the second class.

Danville Area Sch. Dist. v. Danville Area Educ. Ass'n


No. 22 M.D. Appeal Docket 1998


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


562 Pa. 238; 754 A.2d 1255; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 1713; 164 L.R.R.M. 3131; 141 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P59,042


November 16, 1998, Argued  
July 19, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered June 18, 1997, at No. 2310CD1996, reversing the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montour County entered July 18, 1996, at No. 27 of 1996. 700 A.2d 549 (Pa. Cmwlth. 1997). JUDGES BELOW: CCP - Hon. Scott W. Naus / COMMONWEALTH - Doyle, FRIEDMAN, JJ., and Jiuliante, S.J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), reversing the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montour County that affirmed a labor arbitration award in favor of a retired public school teacher.


OVERVIEW: A public school teacher retired and received credit for additional years of service based on recent legislation. The school district nevertheless determined that the teacher's total years of service were not sufficient to qualify for additional retirement benefits. The teacher and appellant state teachers' association filed a grievance, arguing that under the collective bargaining agreement, years of service had always been calculated by the same method as that used by the public employees' retirement system, which would have qualified the teacher for the additional benefits. The arbitrator ruled in favor of appellant and the trial court affirmed, but the intermediate court reversed. The supreme court reversed, holding first that the intermediate court improperly raised the issue of unconstitutional impairment of contract sua sponte. Further, the arbitrator's award did not violate the essence test; the arbitrator properly discerned the intent of the parties in light of the parties' past practice regarding retirement awards.


OUTCOME: Intermediate court reversed. The intermediate court improperly raised an issue not raised and therefore waived by the parties, and the arbitrator properly applied the terms of the agreement and discerned the intent of the parties viewed in light of the language, its context, and other indicia of the parties' intent.

Commonwealth v. Tharp


No. 149 W.D. Misc. Dkt. 1999, No. 155 W.D. Misc. Dkt. 1999


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


562 Pa. 231; 754 A.2d 1251; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 1707


May 2, 2000, Argued  
July 18, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Commonwealth v. Tharp, 574 Pa. 202, 830 A.2d 519, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 1159 (2003)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Commonwealth v. Tharp, 2014 Pa. LEXIS 2501 (Pa., Sept. 24, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (No. 149) Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered September 13, 1999, at No. 80 W.D. Misc. Docket 1999 denying permission to appeal from the interlocutory order of the Court of Common Pleas of Washington County entered June 9, 1999 at No. 1494 of 1998. JUDGE BELOW: CCP - Pozonsky, J. (No. 155) Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered September 13, 1999, at No. 82 W.D. Misc. Docket 1999 denying permission to appeal from the interlocutory order of the Court of Common Pleas of Washington County entered June 9, 1999 at No. 1472 of 1998. JUDGE BELOW: CCP - Pozonsky, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the order of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which denied them permission to appeal from an interlocutory order of the trial court that granted the Commonwealth's request for a jury trial and ordered that appellants be tried by jury pursuant to the provisions of Pa. Const. art. I, § 6 (1998).


OVERVIEW: Appellants, mother and step-father, allegedly starved a seven year-old child to death, dumped the child's body in a garbage bin, and reported her missing to the police. Appellants were charged with criminal homicide, endangering the welfare of a child, abuse of corpse, and aggravated assault. Appellants entered a plea of not guilty and requested a jury trial. One week before jury selection appellants filed requests to waive their right to a jury trial. The Commonwealth asserted its right to a jury trial pursuant to Pa. Const. art. I, § 6 (1998). The trial court granted the Commonwealth's request for a jury trial and appellants sought review. Judgment was affirmed because the amendment to Pa. Const. art. I, § 6 (1998) was constitutional, and there was no impediment, constitutional or otherwise, to applying the amendment to appellants' cases because the effective date of the amendment was November, 1998.


OUTCOME: Order granting the Commonwealth's request for a jury trial was affirmed because the amendment to the Pennsylvania Constitution was constitutional, and there was no impediment, constitutional or otherwise, to applying the amendment to appellants' cases because the effective date of the amendment was November, 1998.

Commonwealth v. Cotto


160 M.D. Appeal Docket 1998


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


562 Pa. 32; 753 A.2d 217; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 1522


October 20, 1999, Argued  
June 20, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered February 19, 1998, at No. 2375 Philadelphia 1997, affirming the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County entered May 19, 1997, at Nos. 1878-1996 and 3167-1996. 708 A.2d 806 (Pa. Super. 1998). Judges: Superior Court - Cavanaugh, Hoffman & Brosky, JJ. / CCP - Hon. D. Richard Eckman.



DISPOSITION: Order of the Superior Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed appellant's sentence for armed robbery on the basis that the 1995 amendments to the Juvenile Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6301 et seq., were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to armed robbery charges and was sentenced accordingly. Although at the time of the offense, appellant was a juvenile, he was charged as an adult pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6302. Appellant sought a transfer to juvenile court, but it was denied. On appeal from the denial, appellant contended that the 1995 amendments to the Juvenile Act were unconstitutional because they were void for vagueness and because they placed the burden of proof on the juvenile seeking transfer to juvenile court. The court held that contrary to appellant's contention that the statute was vague because it did not define the public interest standard, the statute clearly provided definite standards to be applied in determining whether a transfer would serve the public interest. The court also found that placing the burden of persuasion on appellant in no manner denied him his due process rights since the burden to prove every fact necessary for conviction was still on the state.


OUTCOME: Finding that a state statute provided definite standards for determining whether transfer to juvenile court served the public interest and that the burden of proof was still on the state, the court affirmed appellant's sentence and rejected his arguments that the statute was unconstitutional.

 

392 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Glass


No. 043 M.D. Appeal Docket 1999


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


562 Pa. 187; 754 A.2d 655; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 1523


November 17, 1999, Argued  
June 20, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Published Opinion and Order of the Superior Court (Cavanaugh, Popovich and Ford Elliott, JJ.), dated September 15, 1998, affirming the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Perry County (Quigley, P.J.), dated March 19, 1997. 718 A.2d 804 (Pa. Super. 1998). Judges: Cavanaugh, Popovich, Ford Elliot, JJ - Superior Court / Hon. Keith B. Quigley, CCP.



DISPOSITION: Order of the Superior Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which rejected appellant's broad state constitutional challenge to anticipatory search warrants and affirmed the judgment and sentence of appellant for possession of a controlled substance, possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance, and possession of drug paraphernalia.


OVERVIEW: Based on a police trooper's affidavit, a district justice authorized an anticipatory search warrant to be executed upon delivery of a large quantity of marijuana to appellant by a confidential informant. After informant signaled police, approximately 12 pounds of marijuana was seized from appellant's residence. Suppression court denied appellant's motion to suppress. Jury convicted appellant of possessing a controlled substance with intent to deliver, and possessing drug paraphernalia. Appellant sought review. Finding appellant waived issues of probable cause, the superior court rejected appellant's broad state constitutional challenge to anticipatory search warrants. The state supreme court granted appellant's petition for review with respect to the state constitutional claim. The supreme court affirmed, holding that Pa. Const. art. I, § 8, did not categorically proscribe the issuance of anticipatory search warrants. Thus, a warrant based upon an affidavit showing probable cause that at some future time (but not presently) certain evidence of crime would be located at a specified place was constitutionally sufficient.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed superior court's rejection of appellant's state constitutional claim, holding that anticipatory search warrants did not violate the state constitution because it was permissible to base warrant upon police trooper's affidavit showing probable cause that marijuana would be located at appellant's residence at some future time even though such evidence was not presently located at specified place.

 

393 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Gamboa-Taylor


No. 275 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


562 Pa. 70; 753 A.2d 780; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 1526


February 25, 2000, Submitted  
June 19, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Taylor v. Horn, 504 F.3d 416, 2007 U.S. App. LEXIS 22448 (3d Cir. Pa., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered June 8, 1999 in the Court of Common Pleas, York County, Criminal Division, at 1762 C.A. 1991. JUDGE BELOW: C.C.P. - Honorable John H. Chronister.
Commonwealth v. Gamboa-Taylor, 535 Pa. 266, 634 A.2d 1106, 1993 Pa. LEXIS 288 (1993)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal of the denial by the Court of Common Pleas, York County (Pennsylvania) of his second petition for post-conviction relief following his conviction for five counts of first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: In 1991, appellant entered a general plea to criminal homicide for the murders of his wife, his two minor children, his mother-in-law and her minor child. At the trial level, appellant presented no evidence and at the penalty phase he presented no evidence of mitigating circumstances. In 1997, appellant filed his first petition for collateral review, which was denied. In 1999, appellant filed an amended petition for habeas corpus. The Commonwealth of Pennsylvania filed a motion to dismiss as untimely. The Post Conviction Relief Act court dismissed the petition and the appellant filed an appeal. Affirming dismissal, the court held pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9545(b) a petition for post conviction relief must be filed within one year of the final judgment unless an the time limitations exceptions applied. Further, appellant must prove that one of the exceptions applied. Appellant filed his motion five years after the final judgment and appellant had no newly discovered evidence which would have allowed him to fit within the 60 days exception for newly discovered evidence.


OUTCOME: Denial of Post Conviction Relief Act motion affirmed; appellant's motion for post conviction relief was not filed within the one year requirement and appellant could not prove that he fell within one of the exceptions.

 

394 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Annenberg v. Commonwealth


No. 003 Miscellaneous Docket 1997, No. 004 Miscellaneous Docket 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


562 Pa. 581; 757 A.2d 338; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 1381


December 28, 1999, Resubmitted  
June 1, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 30, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 7078.


PRIOR HISTORY: LOWER COURT: Commonwealth Court - 344 M.D. 1996 Dated: - 12/23/96. JUDGES: Hon. William T. Nicholas, President Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners filed for review, seeking a declaration that the stock clause of the state's personal property tax violated the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution and was therefore null and void insofar as it imposed a tax on any corporate stock held by them.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners sought a declaration that the stock clause of the state personal property tax violated the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution and must be voided insofar as it imposed a tax on any corporate stock held by them. The state supreme court reasoned that a finding that the stock clause facially discriminated against interstate commerce was compelled by caselaw. Following the report of the lower court sitting as special master, the court found respondent counties did not meet their burden of proving the stock clause was a compensatory tax, and concluded the portion of the clause excluding from personal property tax stock held in companies subject to capital stock and franchise taxes was unconstitutional. But the court also rejected petitioners' arguments against severability and found the void exclusionary language severable and that respondent counties must provide a retroactive remedy to rectify the prior unconstitutional discrimination.


OUTCOME: The court found the stock clause was not a compensatory tax, and the portion of the stock clause excluding from personal property tax stock held in companies subject to capital stock and franchise taxes was unconstitutional, but the void exclusionary language was severable. Respondent counties were required to provide a retrospective remedy.

 

395 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. MacPherson


No. 36 W.D. Appeal Docket 1999


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


561 Pa. 571; 752 A.2d 384; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 1248


March 8, 2000, Argued  
May 18, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Crawford County entered June 12, 1998 at Criminal Division No. 1998-193. JUDGE(S) BELOW: CCP - Vardaro, J.



DISPOSITION: The trial court's order granting appellee's motion in limine, and requiring the Commonwealth to present relating back testimony, and declaring § 3731(a.1) unconstitutional is reversed, and the case is remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commonwealth appealed from the orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Crawford County (Pennsylvania), which held that 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a.1), part of Pennsylvania's Driving Under the Influence of Alcohol statute, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a)-(j), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Trial court granted defendant's motion in limine, challenging constitutionality of driving under the influence statute. In a direct appeal, the court considered whether the lower court correctly determined that 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a.1) of Pennsylvania's Driving Under the Influence of Alcohol statute, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a)-(j), offended constitutional guarantees of due process. The determination of § 3731(a.1)'s character was essentially a matter of statutory construction. The court concluded § 3731(a.1) created a permissible inference. The trial court's error was twofold: first, it treated a permissive inference as a mandatory presumption; and second, it determined the constitutionality of this permissive inference in a vacuum, before it was applied to appellee and apart from an evidentiary record. The trial court's order granting appellee's motion in limine, and requiring the Commonwealth to present relating back testimony, and declaring § 3731(a.1) unconstitutional was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The trial court's orders granting appellee's motion in limine, requiring Commonwealth to present relating back testimony, and declaring statute unconstitutional were reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings. The statute created a permissible inference, and it was error for the court to treat the inference as a mandatory presumption.

Commonwealth v. Pursell


No. 277 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


561 Pa. 214; 749 A.2d 911; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 958


December 10, 1999, Submitted  
April 17, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Denied May 3, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Orders entered June 22, 1999 and July 15, 1999 in the Court of Common Pleas, Erie County, Criminal Division at No. 1016 of 1981. Judges: C.C.P. - Honorable Ernest DiSantis.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the order of the trial court dismissing Appellant's petition, albeit on grounds different from those relied on by the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the Court of Common Pleas, Erie County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania) denial of his petition for post conviction relief, which found that issues had already been litigated on his first petition.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of murder and sentenced to death, filed a second petition for post conviction relief, claiming numerous errors in his trial and his first post conviction petition. Appellant argued his petition qualified for the exception to the one-year statute of limitations because he was denied his right to counsel on appeal from his first petition. He also argued claims of ineffective assistance at trial also qualified for an exception. The court found that appellant's petition was not timely and the court did not have jurisdiction to grant relief. To the extent that appellant contended ineffectiveness claims prevented him from raising his present claims, the exception did not apply. The trial court's refusal to grant him counsel, after his first attorney withdrew, was not grounds for an exception because appellant simply failed to raise the issue on appeal from the denial of his first petition.


OUTCOME: Order dismissing petition affirmed, finding appellant's petition was untimely and that none of the statutory exceptions applied.

 

397 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Miller


No. 236 Capital Appeal. Dkt.


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


560 Pa. 500; 746 A.2d 592; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 440


January 12, 1999, Submitted  
February 24, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Denied April 28, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the order entered on December 2, 1997 in the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Criminal Division at Nos. 2775, 2775A, 2787 & 2787A C.D. 1992. Judges: C.C.P. - Hon. Jeannine Turgeon.



DISPOSITION: The verdict and sentence of death are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged order from the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania) denying appellant's petition for post-conviction relief filed pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant alleged various claims of trial court error, prosecutorial misconduct, and ineffectiveness of counsel. The court found that appellant was not entitled to relief and the ruling of the lower court was affirmed. Appellant argued that his trial counsel failed to investigate and present available expert testimony regarding appellant's organic brain damage. Appellant's counsel presented all of the evidence available to him at the time of trial in support of the two mental health mitigators. There was no evidence that appellant's counsel ever received an EEG report from a hospital despite his request for all documents. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to present a witness as a mitigation witness. References and statements made by the prosecutor would not have prejudiced the jury, were relevant, and appropriate. The prosecutor's comments did not go beyond permissible oratory. Juvenile adjudications were admissible for purposes of sentencing, even in capital cases.


OUTCOME: Verdict and sentence of death were affirmed. Appellant's counsel was not ineffective for failing to present expert testimony regarding organic brain damage, allegedly failing to present mitigating evidence, or failing to object to prosecutor's comments. Trial court did not err in charging jury.

Commonwealth v. Lark


No. 235 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


560 Pa. 487; 746 A.2d 585; 2000 Pa. LEXIS 417


July 28, 1999, Submitted  
February 23, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Lark, 2000 Pa. LEXIS 1106 (Pa., May 2, 2000)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Lark v. Beard, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 34121 (E.D. Pa., May 23, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Poserina, J.) at Nos. 2012-13,2015 and 2021-22 January Term 1980. Judges: C.C.P. - Honorable John J. Poserina, Jr.
Commonwealth v. Lark, 548 Pa. 441, 698 A.2d 43, 1997 Pa. LEXIS 2090 (1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the dismissal of Appellant's second PCRA petition.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Pennsylvania, dismissing his second petition for relief pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq., as untimely.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. Appellant filed a Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 petition alleging a discriminatory jury selection policy. Appellant asserted that he filed his second PCRA petition in a timely manner because it was filed within 60 days of the court's orders denying relief pursuant to his first PCRA petition. Appellant's second PCRA petition fell within the exception under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9545(b)(1)(ii). Within 60 days of the order denying relief pursuant to his first petition, he filed his second petition. Appellant's Batson claim did not fall within any of the exceptions to the PCRA's jurisdictional time bar. Appellant's claims concerning jury instructions and review were untimely. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in failing to grant appellant's discovery request, as appellant did not present evidence suggesting that witnesses received economic benefits.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of appellant's petition was affirmed. Appellant's Batson claim did not fall within any of the exceptions to the Post Conviction Relief Act's jurisdictional time bar; failure to grant appellant's discovery request was not an abuse of discretion.

Commonwealth v. Watley


No. 845 EDA 2016


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2016 PA Super 311; 153 A.3d 1034; 2016 Pa. Super. LEXIS 810


September 19, 2016, Submitted. 
December 29, 2016, Decided 
December 29, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the PCRA Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Northampton County, Criminal Division, No(s): CP-48-CR-0001701-2009. Before ROSCIOLO, J.
Commonwealth v. Watley, 2013 PA Super 303, 81 A.3d 108, 2013 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3179 (Pa. Super. Ct., 2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-An inmate's ineffective assistance claims were properly denied in his petition under the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 9541-9546, as he failed to show that either the performance was deficient or that he was prejudiced thereby; [2]-Counsel was not ineffective for failing to file a suppression motion regarding a search and seizure of the vehicle, as the motion would not have been granted because the police officer engaged in a constitutional protective search by lifting the floor mat to search for weapons; [3]-The inmate's request for fingerprint analysis of an identification card was properly denied under Pa. R. Crim. P. 902(E)(1), as he failed to show exceptional circumstances because the evidence would not be conclusively exculpatory, and the alleged absence of fingerprints would not necessarily have any particular impeachment value.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

400 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Neyman v. Buckley


No. 2203 EDA 2015


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2016 PA Super 307; 153 A.3d 1010; 2016 Pa. Super. LEXIS 805


July 20, 2016, Argued. 
December 28, 2016, Decided 
December 28, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Family Court Division, No(s): 008400, Term June 2014. Before MURPHY, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court reversed the order of the family court dismissing plaintiff's complaint seeking dissolution of her Vermont civil union because a Vermont civil union should be considered the legal equivalent of a marriage for the purposes of dissolution under the Pennsylvania Divorce Code, 23 Pa.C.S. §§ 3101-3904, thus, jurisdiction over Vermont civil unions should properly vest with Pennsylvania's family courts; [2]-The court further held that under the legal precept of comity, Pennsylvania residents should not have to travel to Vermont to avail themselves of the rights and obligations they undertook when they entered into a Vermont civil union.


OUTCOME: Order reversed; case remanded to family court for further proceedings.
